# curiosity

**!!! (Chk Chk Chk) – From a 1980 South African Film and the Juǀʼhoan Click Language** : Named after the 1980 film The Gods Must Be Crazy, which featured a character speaking Juǀʼhoan, an indigenous South African language that uses mouth clicks. In written form, a click is represented by an exclamation mark. The character's name was pronounced approximately "chk chk chk." "You pronounce the man's name as chick, chick, chick." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**"Advanced Basics" Philosophy** : The title "Advanced Basics" for USS's 2014 album encapsulates a life philosophy: "the simplest things are the hardest things." This concept reflected the band's challenging period during the album's creation, requiring a "one foot in front of the other" approach. "Advanced basics is about that just the title of that song is like a very wonderful life philosophy which is the simplest things are the hardest things." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=N-3eddy4J7g
**"Amadeus" Film and Mozart's Creative Process** : The film "Amadeus" is cited as a favorite, particularly Salieri's observation about Mozart's work containing "no eraser marks" or "corrections," as if he were "taking dictation." This description is used by Ash Boo Shultz to explain his own evolved creative process, where he experiences direct "downloads" of information after shedding personal layers. "In the movie, Amadeus, which is one of my favorite movies, Solary says, when he was looking at Mozart's work, he said, there's no eraser marks. There's no corrections. It's almost like he's taking dictation." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=N-3eddy4J7g
**"Are You Talking to Me?" – Originated with Bruce Springsteen; Passed Through Robert De Niro to Punk Culture via Joe Strummer** : Robert De Niro had a night off from filming Taxi Driver in 1976 and went to a Bruce Springsteen concert. Between songs, Springsteen turned his back to the crowd and waited for the noise to build, then turned and said "Are you talking to me?" De Niro used the line the next day while filming the famous mirror scene, improvising repeatedly — director Martin Scorsese loved it. Separately, Joe Strummer saw Taxi Driver and was so impressed by De Niro's Travis Bickle that he copied the Mohawk haircut for himself and The Clash, which is how the Mohawk became embedded in punk culture. "That is how the Mohawk became ingrained in punk culture." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fnZx8EGnszw
**"Art Context" Podcast Objective** : The "Art Context, the Architects of Art" podcast aims to provide a platform for music video directors and filmmakers to share their stories, including their career beginnings, inspirations, triumphs, challenges, and the intricate processes of creating music videos, films, and other content. It intends to offer a behind-the-scenes look at the art form. "So our show is pretty much about, it's in the world of music. It's pretty much us sitting down with storytellers that come from music videos." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5PJRCC6EwUY
**"Baby Shark" Earnings** : The song "Baby Shark" has generated over $100 million for its owners, Smart Study, a South Korean company, and its education division, Pinkfong. Kim Min-Seok is named as a co-founder and beneficiary of this wealth. "The song Baby Shark has so far made its owners over $100 million." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=72Lei7uug8c
**"Celestial Jukebox" Concept (1994)** : In 1994, law professor Paul Goldstein coined and popularized the term "Celestial Jukebox" to describe his vision of a networked database, accessible to anyone with an internet connection, that would contain all music. "In 1994, a law professor named Paul Goldstein popularized the term Celestial Jukebox." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**"Coming of Age" Musical Immersion (Ages 14-24)** : Most individuals are deeply immersed in music and music culture between the ages of 14 and 24. The songs listened to during this period significantly shape an individual's musical taste for their entire life. However, once people reach their mid-20s, adult responsibilities like jobs, families, and mortgages often reduce the time, money, and inclination to actively seek out new music and attend shows. "The songs we listen to then sets our musical taste for the rest of our life." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**"Crate Digging" Defined** : "Crate digging" is a term used to describe the activity of searching for and purchasing used records from various sources such as record shops, record shows, and other collectors. "You may buy your records brand new right off the shelf, which is fine, or you may want to start crate digging. That is, buying used records at shops, records shows, and from other collectors." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IIJySSo276k
**"Dildo" – A 16th-Century Classical Music Filler Word** : The word "dildo" originated in 16th-century England as a filler word in songs — the "la la la" of its day. Written compositions of the era for lute and counter-tenor use the word extensively as a lyrical placeholder. "Dildo is a classical music term." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fnZx8EGnszw
**"Divestiture Laws" – Financial Censorship Forcing Pension Funds to Sell Shares in Music Companies** : A subtle form of financial censorship used in the United States, "divestiture laws" compel state agencies and funds — such as teachers' pension funds — to divest from companies that distribute or control music considered objectionable. For example, a teachers' pension fund could be forced to sell its shares in Seagram, which owned Universal Music, home of Marilyn Manson. "Forced state agencies and funds to sell shares in companies distributing 'objectionable' music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=f4TOWLYRnGs
**"Dun Dun Dun" Audio Meme – From Stravinsky's 1913 Rite of Spring; Modern Form from 1984 Production Record** : The dramatic "dun dun dun" musical cue's first apparent appearance was in Stravinsky's 1913 ballet Rite of Spring. Its contemporary form likely derives from a production record made in 1984, officially titled "Shock Horror A," using the notes D-sharp, C, and F-sharp. "Dun dun dun. Where did that audio meme come from?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZbHRIh3RUoo
**"Explore Music" Radio and TV Program** : "Explore Music" was an offshoot radio and TV program that primarily focused on music interviews. "For a while, there was an offshoot radio and TV program called Explore Music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bI6TTA-fn7c
**"Facility Fee" for Venues** : In addition to service charges, a "facility fee" may be levied on concert tickets, with the revenue going to the venue to help cover its costs. While venues also generate income from concessions, parking, and alcohol, this fee is an additional way for them to make money from ticket sales. "There may also be a service charge that goes to the venue for the same reason. This became known as a facility fee in some territories." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8q2bRZyHnHE
**"Get Your Own Riffs"** : This phrase originated from a sign reportedly posted on Oasis's rehearsal room door by another band, accusing them of using unoriginal material. The phrase became a symbolic critique of plagiarism and unoriginality in music, reappearing in the discussion of other artists. "the sign said, get your own riffs." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=L09R2evjyMc
**"Good Vibrations" Title – Inspired by Brian Wilson's Mother's Theory About Dogs and Vibrations** : Brian Wilson's mother told him that dogs could pick up vibrations from people, which is why they bark at some but not others. Wilson originally titled the song "Good Vibes," but after bringing in someone to play a theremin-like instrument, the title became "Good Vibrations." "It's all about the vibrations they sense from individual people, she said." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZbHRIh3RUoo
**"Harvey Weinstein, the Musical" Produced in Northern Ireland** : A musical titled "Harvey Weinstein, the musical" has been produced and is running out of Northern Ireland. This production emerges while Harvey Weinstein continues to face consequences for years of sexual misconduct and abuse. "Somebody is already running Harvey Weinstein, the musical. It's coming out of Northern Ireland." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-N6IM5Nm5iw
**"Jingle Bells" – Originally Written for American Thanksgiving (1857)** : "Jingle Bells" was written by James Lord Pierpont and published in 1857 as a song celebrating American Thanksgiving, not Christmas. "It was originally written as a song to celebrate American Thanksgiving." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZbHRIh3RUoo
**"Johnny Apple Seeds of Rock"** : The Ramones earned this nickname because their influence inspired thousands of young people to pick up guitars. Wherever the band played, new local bands seemed to emerge in their wake, spreading their musical legacy. "Some people call them the Johnny Apple Seeds of Rock because wherever they stop to play, new bands sprung up in their wake." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=j8uk7BnbXwU
**"License Plate Names" Trend** : Around 1979, there was a trend for bands to adopt short, memorable names, referred to as "license plate names," exemplified by groups like INXS, U2, and XTC. "That's back when it was really hot to have what I call a license plate name, you know, in excess, U2, XTC." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gxbuajGKbko
**"Loudness Wars" and CD Compression** : The "loudness wars" describe a post-recording trend where music, particularly for CDs, is heavily compressed to make it sound louder. This process, while aiming for impact, often introduces significant distortion and eliminates the dynamic nuances between loud and quiet passages, leading to a "pristine digital signal" that ironically sounds "awful." "We've come to know this as the loudness wars. This has introduced a ton of distortion into what should be a pristine digital signal." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D8GU8ZpSgY8
**"M-O-H" Input in Phone Systems** : Most commercial phone systems include an "M-O-H" input, which stands for "Music On Hold." This dedicated input facilitates the integration of various musical sources for callers awaiting assistance. "And pretty much every commercial phone system comes with an M-O-H input." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D8GU8ZpSgY8
**"Metal Machine Music" Locked Groove** : Lou Reed's "Metal Machine Music" features a locked groove at the end of side four of the double album. This design means that the stylus never runs out, causing the sounds to theoretically continue indefinitely, or until the record is worn out. This extreme feature contributes to the album's reputation as a weaponized and unending sonic assault. "The last groove is locked, meaning that the stylist never gets a chance to run out." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iGav9uJwA_w
**"Metal" as an Adjective in Merriam-Webster** : The Merriam-Webster dictionary was considering or may have declared that the word "metal" can be used as an adjective, typically in informal contexts, as exemplified by phrases such as "that dude is so metal." "By the time you hear this, the Merriam Webster dictionary may have declared that metal can be used as an adjective, as in that dude is so metal." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GO0K_N7Ys7I
**"Mr. Obituary" Role for News Networks** : The speaker is frequently contacted by every major news network in Canada (CBC, CTV, Fox, CNN, and a station in Tel Aviv, Israel) for commentary when musicians pass away, earning him the moniker "Mr. Obituary." "When anybody dies, every single news network in Canada calls me for a comment." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90
**"My Way" Is Known as the World's Deadliest Karaoke Song in the Philippines** : Frank Sinatra's "My Way" is documented as the deadliest karaoke song in the Philippines, with more than a dozen killings recorded in connection with it — typically triggered by disputes over poor singing or refusing to share the microphone. "'My Way' by Frank Sinatra is known as 'the world's deadliest karaoke song' in the Philippines, with more than a dozen documented murders." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qtdetc5-MQo
**"New New Wave" Term (Early 2000s)** : British music papers frequently used the term "New New Wave" to describe the new wave revivalist bands emerging from the UK in the early 2000s, such as Bloc Party, The Kaiser Chiefs, Ladytron, The Ting Tings, and The Foals. "In fact, if you read any write-ups in the British music papers, you'll have seen them refer to as New New Wave." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9CNNsqXiL6U
**"Playlist Burnout" – Infinite Music Choice Causes Listening Fatigue** : The infinite availability of music through streaming can lead to "playlist burnout," whereby music becomes background noise and loses its ability to generate satisfaction. Active listening and deliberate periods of silence are recommended to reset the brain's reward system. "The infinite choice of music can lead to 'playlist burnout,' where music becomes background noise." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0DFmS6MPbFI
**"Radiohead" Band Name – Came from a Talking Heads Song About Radio** : The band name Radiohead derives from "Radio Head," a track from the Talking Heads 1986 album *True Stories* about someone's experience listening to the radio. "That is where the band got their name." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iyGUXdDqIlI
**"Rock and Roll Traveler, Great Britain and Ireland" Book** : An excellent travel guide for rock fans wishing to visit historical music sites in the UK and Ireland, published by Fodor's Travel Guide. Although long out of print, it can be found for purchase online at very low prices. "It's by the Fodder's Travel Guide people. It's perfect for the rock fan who wants to visit some history in the UK and Ireland." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yl2poVWguu0
**"Rock is Dead" Claims (1960-1999)** : Throughout history, there have been recurring declarations that "rock is dead," notably in 1960, 1972, 1988, and 1999. These claims often coincide with periods when pop music dominates the forefront of the industry. "Just like we heard in 1999, 1988, 1972, and 1960." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**"Rock is sick and living in London" (1977)** : This headline appeared on the cover of Rolling Stone magazine on October 20th, 1977, featuring The Sex Pistols. It captured the critical sentiment and controversy surrounding punk rock at the time, with some critics branding it a short-sighted fad. "The October 20th, 1977 edition of Rolling Stone magazine had the sex pistols on the cover, but the headline, Rock is sick and living in London." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9CNNsqXiL6U

"In 2020, HBO released a documentary called Showbiz Kids, where child stars got to tell their stories, warts and all." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dY7uB_QQWBc
**"Sidewalk Surfing"** : Early skateboarding was also commonly referred to as "sidewalk surfing," reflecting its origins among surfers who adapted their ocean tricks to dry land, particularly in Southern California. "Skateboarding or sidewalk surfing caught on with some people in Southern California, usually surfers who tried the same tricks on dry land as they did in the ocean." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=44dXy0StjIQ
**"The Day the Music Died" (1957)** : February 3, 1957, is historically referred to as "the day the music died." On this date, pioneering rock and roll musicians Buddy Holly, Richie Valens, and The Big Bopper were all killed when their small plane crashed into a cornfield outside of Mason City, Iowa, marking a significant loss in music history. "February 3rd, 1957 has gone down in history as the day the music died." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hmnMG6f80Sg
**"The Ox-Bow Incident" Quotes** : Gord Downie's song "The East Wind" incorporates "found objects quotes" from various sources, including Walter von Tilburg Clark, who wrote "The Ox-Bow Incident." A specific quote, "night is like a room. It makes the little things inside your head too important," appears in the song and is attributed to Clark, whose 1943 novel was adapted into a film by William Wellman. "So the second verse is night is like a room. It makes the little things inside your head too important. That's Walter von Tilburg Clark who wrote The Oxbow incident." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Um_KEEcCeT4
**"Ticket to Ride" – About Prostitutes in Hamburg with Clean Health Cards** : The Beatles song "Ticket to Ride" sounds like it should be about public transport, but it refers to a card carried by prostitutes in Hamburg certifying that they had a clean bill of health and were therefore legally permitted to work. "I have not been able to listen to that song the same way since." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fnZx8EGnszw
**"What's the Big Deal About" Series** : The death of a musician provides an opportunity to create a "What's the Big Deal About" series, which aims to explain the significance of these artists to a broader audience who may not be familiar with their careers or cultural impact. "Because how do you conceptualize Shnato Conner or Shane McGowan on their own? But now we can package it better." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90
**10,050 Cielo Drive (Manson Murder Site)** : This address in Benedict Canyon, Los Angeles, was the site of the first Manson family murders on August 8, 1969. Tex Watson, Susan Atkins, Linda Kasabian, and Patricia Krenwinkel brutally murdered Abigail Folger, Woodjick Freierkowski, Jay Sebring, Stephen Parent, and the heavily pregnant actress Sharon Tate, who was renting the property with Roman Polanski. The word "pig" was written in Tate's blood on the living room wall. Trent Reznor later rented this house in July 1992 to record "The Downward Spiral," unknowingly at first, and established his studio in the room where Tate and Sebring were found. "10,050 C.L.O. Drive is where the first of the Manson family murders took place." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DKdF8NgF5Bw
**13 Universal Emotions Evoked by Music** : A study involving 2500 participants across North America and China revealed that music can consistently elicit exactly 13 distinct emotions, irrespective of an individual's musical preferences or cultural background. These emotions include amusement, joy, eroticism, beauty, relaxation, sadness, dreaminess, triumph, anxiety, scaringness, annoyance, defiance, and feeling pumped up. "Scientists say that music can bring forth exactly 13 different emotions, regardless of who you are or what kind of music you like, or it seems your cultural background." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**1545 Weevil Trial in St. Julianne, France** : In 1545, winemakers in St. Julianne, France, legally prosecuted weevils for eating their grapevines. The weevils were appointed a defense lawyer, underwent a formal trial, and were found guilty. Almost a year later, the presiding judge issued a proclamation demanding the weevils cease, and surprisingly, the infestations stopped for 40 years, only to resume in 1587, leading to a second, unrecorded trial. "This was all very formal. Documents were drawn up and the weevils were appointed a defense lawyer by the court." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dVJuITJyNTU
**16 and 2/3 RPM – Spoken Word, Children's Records, and Chrysler In-Dash Turntables** : Turntables were briefly manufactured to operate at four speeds: 33⅓, 45, 78, and 16⅔ RPM. Slow-speed records were used for spoken word, children's releases, and as an in-dash turntable option sold by Chrysler in the 1950s. The Chrysler turntables were not practical (too much bouncing), and fewer than 50 titles were released, available only at Chrysler dealers. Audiobook records for the blind were made at speeds as slow as 4⅙ RPM. "Several audiobook records were once manufactured for the blind with speeds of 24, 8 and 1 3rd, and 4 and 1 6th RPM." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=I291j5WBc4k
**1896 Pornographic Cylinder Recording – Gonorrhea Soliloquy; Creator Jailed in Government Sting** : Among the earliest surviving examples of censored recorded material, three wax cylinders from a collection called "The Stag Party" feature dirty jokes and bawdy verses, sold at the outrageous price of $1.50. One is a parody of Hamlet's "To be or not to be" soliloquy in which the speaker laments a case of gonorrhea, titled "To Pee or Not to Pee." The person who made and distributed these recordings was caught in a government sting operation on June 24, 1896, fined, and jailed. These recordings are among the oldest surviving examples demonstrating that censorship of recorded material has existed since the very beginning of the medium. "The person was caught in a government sting operation on June 24, 1896. He was fined and sent to jail for months." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Dt7mb4yyuWM
**1968 film - 2001, A Space Odyssey** : This film had a profound impact on David Bowie, significantly influencing his creative output. Its themes of space exploration and existentialism contributed to the inspiration behind his hit song "Space Oddity." "The 1968 film, 2001, A Space Audity, had a huge impact on him." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0xd0Hf5REg4
**1980s Vision of Digital Music Archive** : During the 1980s, individuals began envisioning a massive centralized computer capable of storing all of humanity's music in digital format, making any song instantly accessible upon demand. "In the 1980s, some people started to conceive of a giant computer somewhere that could hold humanity's music in digital form." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**1990s Album Art Production Budget** : During the 1990s, there were significant budgets allocated for the creation of album artwork, allowing for elaborate physical sets and detailed photography, in contrast to modern methods like AI-generated artwork. "Now keep in mind this was the 90s when there was a budget for this sort of thing and we didn't have AI-generated artwork." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sn5TWBFd0XM
**1990s Stand-up Sitcom Boom** : The 1990s saw a massive boom in stand-up comics starring in their own TV sitcoms. This trend was spurred by the success of shows like *The Cosby Show* and *Roseanne*, leading networks to scout comedy clubs for well-established stand-up comedians around whom they could build shows. Suddenly, every major network was adding one or two stand-up sitcoms a year. "Thanks to the success of the Cosby Show and Roseanne, networks began searching comedy clubs looking for a well-established Stand Up comics they could build shows around." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6O5TCTO-go4
**1994 Woodstock 25th Anniversary – Alt-Rock's Triumphant Peak; Lineup Proved Genre's Dominance** : The 25th anniversary of Woodstock was held in Saugerties, New York, with a lineup that demonstrated just how thoroughly alternative rock had taken over popular music: Red Hot Chili Peppers, Peter Gabriel, Green Day, Nine Inch Nails, Live, Collective Soul, Violent Femmes, Metallica, Blind Melon, the Cranberries, Primus, Porno for Pyros, and more. The conditions were muddy and cold. The same summer's Lollapalooza featured the Smashing Pumpkins, Beastie Boys, the Breeders, the Verve, Green Day, Flaming Lips, and others. "If you were a fan of rock and you were around in the early 1990s, you probably remember that era very, very fondly." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4Jvy4q40tuo
**1995 vs. Today's Internet Access** : The level of global internet access for music distribution in the late 2000s was "the stuff of science fiction" in 1995. The ability to instantly upload a song or video and have it accessible worldwide became a taken-for-granted reality. "That kind of access was the stuff of science fiction in 1995 and today we just take it for granted." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**1998 Warped Tour Accommodation** : During the 1998 Warped Tour, all participants, including bands and crew, slept either in tents or in Boy Scout camps, reflecting the tour's rugged, no-frills environment. "everyone on the 1998 tour either slept intense or in Boy Scout camps." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7jfQaUV6Bq4
**19th-Century Copyright Law Left a Legal Vacuum for Sound Recordings** : Copyright laws of the nineteenth century were designed for the printed word and left a complete legal vacuum regarding audio recordings, allowing unauthorized recordings to exist without clear legal prohibition. The United Kingdom was the first country to extend copyright protection to sound recordings; the United States did not do so effectively until 1972. "Copyright laws were designed for the printed word, leaving a legal vacuum for audio recordings." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OrHtPVBjXw4
**2010s Alt Rock Sound Evolution** : In the 2010s, the overall sound of Alt Rock evolved significantly, moving "down Temple and away from being guitar heavy." It incorporated "more keyboards, more samples, more banjos," experiencing "a pop phase more profound than we'd seen since maybe the 1980s." In this context, pop punk, by contrast, "sounded heavy." "overall, Alt Rock moved down Temple and away from being guitar heavy, more keyboards, more samples, more banjos." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pE7TaWSUa-o
**2010s Combacks as Industry Health Indicator** : The comebacks of established "monsters of rock" in the 2010s, such as Tool, Guns N' Roses, Pearl Jam, and Metallica, were crucial for the health of both the recorded music industry and the touring industry, as well as music in general. These acts continued to fuel massive tours and album sales, largely supported by Boomers and Gen Xers. "The comebacks that we saw in the 2010s were an extremely important part of the health of the recorded music industry, also the touring industry, and you know what, music in general." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HSvgRyGiOpE
**2010s Defining Characteristics** : The 2010s decade began on time and was characterized by prosperous economic growth, the rise of authoritarianism, and a massive surge in technology adoption, including smartphones, the explosion of social media, and cord-cutting, significantly impacting how music was consumed. "For the next 10 years, we saw everything from prosperous economic growth to the rise of authoritarianism and technology." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5Y6nHw5xx88
**30 Seconds to Mars – Harvard Professor's Thesis on Technological Progress** : Jared and Shannon Leto found the name in a subsection of a Harvard professor's thesis about how fast technology advances — the suggestion being that on an evolutionary scale, humans are close to reaching Mars. They felt the concept described their musical ambitions. "Such a grand thought described perfectly what they wanted to do with their band." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**30-Second Minimum for Streaming Payouts** : A universal rule across all streaming music services dictates that a song must be listened to for a minimum of 30 seconds to qualify as an official play, and anything less than this duration results in no payment to the artist. "In order to qualify for a song as being officially played, you have to listen for at least 30 seconds." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**360 Deal Business Model** : The "360 deal" emerged as a new business relationship where a music industry entity (label, promoter, etc.) provides upfront financial support for an artist in exchange for a percentage of all revenue streams. This includes traditional income, as well as concert ticket sales, merchandise, and licensing, aiming for mutual survival and growth in a changing market. "We began to hear of something called the 360 deal. This is a new type of business relationship between an artist or some kind of music industry entity." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**6/8 Time Signature Challenges in Music** : Songs written in a 6/8 time signature are noted for being difficult to perform effectively live, are seldom played on radio, and are considered "tough to dance to," often described as a "double waltz." "6'8", grooves are hard to deliver live." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VR5Fncdc2kQ
**606 Studios Location and Description** : The Foo Fighters' recording studio, 606 Studios, is located in Northridge, California. On September 30, 2014, surveillance audio described the studio's exterior as "like a fortress" in a "rough neighborhood," suggesting a formidable and somewhat secluded creative space. "This place looks like a fortress." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Mh-qg1izM98
**80s Alt-Rock Radio Station Differences** : In the 1980s, commercial alt-rock radio stations operated independently, without industry magazines publishing alternative charts or tracking airplay. This autonomy meant each station curated music based on local audience preferences, resulting in distinct sounds between stations across North America. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**90s Music as Top Nostalgia Driver** : Music from the 1990s has emerged as the number one source for nostalgia, surpassing the public's fascination with the 80s, 70s, and 60s. This trend is so strong that even young music fans who were not alive in the 90s have fiercely embraced the music from that era, making it "fresh and top of mind" for them. "It's been so long since the 90s, for example, that music of that era is number one for nostalgia. It clipsing the public's fascination with the 80s, the 70s, and the 60s." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZzIqIydZTlA
**911 Call Regarding Chester Bennington's Death (July 20, 2017)** : On July 20, 2017, around 9 AM, a limo driver contacted 911 after Chester Bennington's housekeeper informed him of finding a body. The driver reported that the housekeeper found Chester dead from hanging in his room at his home in Pollock's, confirming no signs of life. An empty vodka bottle was found by the body, but toxicology reports showed nothing. "Around nine in the morning of July 20, what would have been Chris Cornell's 53rd birthday, the family's housekeeper ran out to an arriving limo driver who was there to pick up Chester for a photo shoot. She'd found a body." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qQm7u3W13eM
**924 Gilman Street Punk Club** : This punk club in Oakland was a pivotal venue for the local teen punk scene and played a significant role in Green Day's early career. Tre Cool was a regular there. After Green Day signed a major label deal, some traditional fans from Gilman Street protested their shows, perceiving the move as "selling out." The club remains near where all three Green Day members still reside, not far from San Francisco. "He was a regular at a punk club called 924 Gilman Street, which catered to Oakland's team punk scene." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nyfdGYWelic

**AM Top 40 Radio Dominance (1970s)** : Between 1974 and 1976, AM Top 40 radio was the predominant source of music for the vast majority of people, significantly more popular than FM stations that played rock and album cuts. This widespread exposure to what was often perceived as "awful music" on AM radio played a role in fueling the rise of punk. "the vast majority of people got almost all their music from AM top 40 radio." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tZV1lz-obQE
**AM and FM Frequency Standards Vary by World Region – Western Radios Don't Work in Russia or Japan** : AM radio in North America uses the 520-1710 kHz band with stations spaced 10 kHz apart; much of the world uses 9 kHz spacing starting at 531 kHz, meaning North American digital radios cannot properly receive most global AM stations. FM differs even more dramatically: North America runs 87.9–107.9 MHz; parts of the former Soviet Union and Warsaw Pact countries use 65–74 MHz (fully incompatible with Western radios); Japan uses 76–90 MHz (also incompatible). When the US moved FM to its current band on January 15, 1945, all FM radios sold to that point in history became instantly useless. The world is divided by the International Telecommunication Union (founded 1865) into three broadcasting regions with different regulations. "Did you know that the radio that you're listening to right now won't work in Russia or Japan?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JvOEAzmC6l0

**Accents in Singing: Flattening Effect** : When people sing, their regional accents tend to disappear approximately 99% of the time. This occurs because the melody and rhythm of a song override normal pronunciation, stretching out vowels and neutralizing phonemes, leading to a more "North American" or "mid-Atlantic" sound. "Where do accents go when we sing? This happens 99% of the time, no matter how thick a broke might be." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Accents in Singing: Phonemes and Melody** : Linguists refer to vowels and consonants as phonemes, which are the sounds that differentiate words. While phonemes are pronounced differently across regions, the melody and rhythm of a song tend to neutralize these distinct pronunciations during singing. Stretching out vowels and the emotional expression in singing contribute to flattening accents. "The melody of a song tends to override how someone would normally pronounce a word and it's phoneme. It cancels out what makes an accent an accent." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Accidental Creation of the 12-Inch Single** : The 12-inch single format was developed by accident in the early 1970s by engineer Tom Moulton. Faced with the urgent need to complete a new mix by the end of a weekend and having run out of standard 7-inch blanks, Moulton improvised by stretching the grooves onto a 12-inch blank disc. This new format was quickly embraced by disco DJs and gained widespread popularity. The first 12-inch single is believed to be "All Because of Holding On" by R&B singer Al Downing. "The twelve inch single was created by accident. In the early 1970s, Tom Molten was working as an engineer and he had to finish a new mix by the end of the weekend. He was out of seven inch blanks, so Molten stretched out the grooves on a twelve inch blank." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HoBx6s3JmVQ
**Acoustic Recording Method (Pre-Microphone)** : In the early days of recording, music was captured acoustically using a large horn or funnel that channeled sounds to a diaphragm. A stylus attached to the diaphragm vibrated to cut grooves into a rotating metal disk, which became the master. This method allowed "no edits, no overdubs, no fixing in the mix," requiring perfect, loud performances and complete re-recording if any mistake occurred. "That's because records were made in the acoustic way. But it was arranged around a big horn, basically a large funnel, which channeled sounds down to a diaphragm." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NAroxFbYkRw
**Acoustic Tweezers for Moving Objects** : Scientists have developed "tweezers of sound" that can move objects without physical contact, marking a step towards the concept of a tractor beam. Although current capabilities are limited to moving millimeter-sized objects, this development utilizes sound waves to manipulate physical items. "Scientists have figured out how to make tweezers of sound that can move objects without actually touching them." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-N6IM5Nm5iw
**Acquisition of CFNY Vinyl Library (1996)** : In 1996, when the CFNY radio station moved from a rundown strip mall in Brampton to downtown Toronto, management decided to discard its extensive vinyl library, believing digital music would soon render it obsolete. **Adolf Rickenbacher's Background** : Adolf Rickenbacher, a Swiss immigrant, had a diverse background. His wife was heir to the Standard Oil fortune, and his early success involved inventing a process for manufacturing plastic knobs for ovens. He owned a tool and die shop in Los Angeles, where he was approached by George Beechum and John Dupira for their guitar projects. "He was a Swiss immigrant, whose wife was heir to the standard oil fortune. His first success was creating a process to manufacture plastic knobs for ovens. Not eventually, he led to his old tool and die shop in Los Angeles, which is where he was found when the guitar guys came calling." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=E6cXyaHALBQ
**Advantages of Modern New Vinyl (Post-2008)** : Since approximately 2008, purchasing new vinyl records has become less risky due to improved manufacturing standards. Modern vinyl is typically made from "virgin" PVC (not recycled) and is produced to be notably heavy, with discs weighing 180, 200, or even 220 grams. This increased weight contributes to better stability on the turntable, reducing warping and allowing the stylus to track grooves more accurately, which can lead to improved sound quality depending on the source material and playback system. "Since about 2008, buying new vinyl has come with less of a risk. The vinyl is virgin, and the records tend to be nice and heavy, with each disc weighing 180, 200 or even 220 grams each." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B2g4QSREzpw

**Aesthetic and Artistic Constraints on Note Combinations** : Despite the astronomical number of theoretical note combinations, music must ultimately sound pleasing to the ear and soul. This artistic and aesthetic requirement significantly narrows down the number of *workable* note combinations, increasing the likelihood of unintentional repetition in compositions. "Music has to sound pleasing to the ear and to the soul, too. ...there are only so many combinations of notes that work from an artistic and aesthetic point of view." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=L09R2evjyMc
**African-American Contribution to Music History** : The history of rock music and its ongoing development are deeply indebted to people of African descent. Tracing important innovations and accomplishments backward often leads to Black culture, from the rhythms and songs brought by enslaved Africans in 1619 to the modern genres like rock and roll, funk, and hip hop. "We would not be sitting here talking about rock music if it weren't for people of African descent." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hQJ3r-DCoMQ
**Age-Related Music Consumption Habits** : As people age (into their 40s or 45-46+), their music consumption patterns tend to shift. They either revert to listening to the music of their youth exclusively or begin exploring bands they missed during their formative years (14-24). The experience of having heard "an awful lot of music" makes it harder to achieve the same "high" from new discoveries. "You'll go back to the music of your youth and listen to that over and over again for the rest of your life. Or you will go back to the era of when you were 14 to 24 and you'll start investigating bands that you missed the first time around." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90

Furthermore, excluding contemporary pop acts like Ed Sheeran, Beyonce, and Taylor Swift, the "vast majority of the all-time top-grossing tours" are by acts with an average age of 45 and above. **Album Cover Art History – Plain Brown Wrapper to Art Form; First Color Record Jacket in WWII; Sgt. Pepper as Milestone** : Early record covers were plain brown wrappers whose sole purpose was to identify contents. The first color record jacket appeared during World War II. By the late 1950s–early 1960s, most LP records featured portraits of the artist. As the 1960s progressed, artwork concepts became more ambitious, culminating with the Beatles' Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band package. The album cover became essential, spawning design companies like Hypnosis. The 12x12-inch LP gave designers an enormous canvas; with gatefold sleeves, designers had 6–8 square feet to work with. "From the middle 1960s, album art just exploded." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JdSUHkXM1mQ
**Album Dominance in Music Business (Post-1967)** : Following the release of *Sgt. Pepper* in 1967, the album became the primary economic unit of the recorded music industry, with singles transitioning into promotional tools designed to drive album sales, which offered significantly higher profit margins. "From that point on, the album became the currency of the recorded music business." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Album as an Artistic Medium (Post-1965 Shift)** : The perception of the album changed around 1965 when artists like The Beatles and Bob Dylan began to utilize it as a larger creative canvas. They started writing longer, more complex, and carefully sequenced collections of songs meant to be heard as a unified work, a paradigm solidified by albums like The Beatles' *Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band*. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU

**Alex Steinweiss – Pioneer of Album Art (1938)** : In 1938, 23-year-old graphic designer Alex Steinweiss was hired as Columbia Records' first-ever art director in New York, where he pioneered the concept of album cover artwork. His revolutionary idea to photograph a specially arranged marquee sign for a Richard Rodgers and Lorenz Hart release, and use it as the cover, dramatically increased sales and launched a new creative industry. "In 1938, a 23-year-old graphic designer named Alex Steinweiss was hired as the first-ever art director for Columbia Records in New York." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_tbKuJR0cPs

**Alfred Levy's Patent (1966)** : In 1966, Alfred Levy filed a patent for a machine that automatically played music to callers on hold. This early patent serves as the foundation for virtually every on-hold device used today, whether it provides generic pre-taped music, a radio station, or another musical source. "In 1966, he filed a patent on a machine that automatically played music for callers anytime they were placed on hold." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D8GU8ZpSgY8

**All-in Pricing vs. Drip Pricing** : Artists have the option to implement "all-in pricing," where the displayed ticket price includes all fees and charges. However, studies have indicated that fans are just as annoyed by a single, higher all-in price as they are by the "drip, drip, drip" of multiple added fees, leading ticket sellers like Ticketmaster to continue absorbing blame for fragmented pricing to deflect negativity from the artists. "Now here is a weird thing. The artist could ask for all in pricing. **Amen Break Development** : Around a decade after its 1969 recording, the drum break from The Winston's "Amen Brother" was discovered by hip-hop DJs who began looping it on turntables. With the advent of affordable sampling technology like the Akai S1000, this seven-second, four-bar syncopated break became known as the "Amen Break" and was extensively manipulated by producers. "And someone, and we are not sure who, found Coleman's bit in Amen Brother and started to use it on the decks." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Amen Break Usage** : The "Amen Break" is recognized by Who Sampled as the most sampled piece of music in history, appearing in over 5,309 songs across hip-hop, electronic, and EDM genres. Artists from Slipknot to Oasis have utilized this ubiquitous drum break. "According to the website Who Sampled, which tracks samples and songs, the Amen Break sample has been used no fewer than in 5,309 songs, more than any other sample in the history of music, 5,309 songs." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**American Musician Strike (1942-1944)** : The American musician strike, lasting from 1942 to 1944, significantly pressured the music industry by effectively shutting down the recording industry during that period. This strike exacerbated an already challenging environment for music production, occurring concurrently with the shellac shortage caused by World War II. "There was also a paralyzing musician strike in the US that lasted from 1942 to 1944, which pretty much shut down the recording industry." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**American Red Cross – Logo Complaint** : The American Red Cross lodged a formal complaint regarding the use of a Red Cross symbol on the nurse's hat worn by Jeanine Lindemulder on early versions of Blink-182's "Enema of the State" album cover. They contended that this constituted an infringement on their official logo, leading to its removal from subsequent album pressings. "The American Red Cross complained. They said that the Red Cross on Jeanine's hat infringed on their logo." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_tbKuJR0cPs
**Amusia – Up to 4% of Humans Cannot Experience Music as Pleasurable Sound** : Amusia is a neurological condition, either congenital or resulting from brain injury, that prevents the person from processing pitch and music in a pleasurable way. Those with amusia perceive music as meaningless or unpleasant noise — approximately as distressing as fingernails on a chalkboard. They cannot hum a song, tell a major chord from random piano smashing, or detect when a guitar is out of tune. Melody is meaningless to them. It is estimated that up to 4% of humans have some form of amusia. In tonal languages like Mandarin, where pitch changes the meaning of words, amusia creates additional communication difficulties. "Basically amusia is an inability to hear music as pleasurable sound." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NMwMwqMQpf4
**Amygdala and Emotional Processing** : The amygdala, interconnected with the nucleus accumbens, is the brain region where all emotions are processed and triggered. The sensation of "chills" experienced when listening to a great song originates here, manifesting as a direct result of a dopamine rush. "This is where all our emotions are processed and triggered. Again, when we hear a great song and you feel chills, this is where they come from. That's a dopamine rush." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Analog vs. Digital Sound Reproduction** : Vinyl records are an analog format, designed to smoothly capture real-world sounds. Compact discs (CDs), established with standards in the 1970s, are digital, sampling sound 44,100 times per second with a 16-bit depth, which can store up to 65,536 levels of information to define dynamic range, operating at 44.1 KHz 16-bit. CDs generally offer superior sound quality to MP3s, as MP3s are compressed files with removed information, which the brain attempts to compensate for. "Vinyl is an analog format, which means it smoothly captures real-world sounds. The compact disc is digital." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B2g4QSREzpw
**Analog vs. Digital Source Material for Vinyl** : If the original source material for a vinyl record was recorded digitally, the resulting vinyl record is merely an analog copy of a digital recording, which may diminish the perceived benefits of vinyl. A truly noticeable difference in sound quality is most likely when the entire production chain, from initial studio recording to the final pressing of the record, remains purely analog. "it may not matter if the original material for a vinyl record was recorded digitally. You just end up with an analog copy of a digital recording." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B2g4QSREzpw
**Ancient Greek Music Example** : The phrase "Horses on this fine moon made in hollow, so beautiful, pro soligone, esti ta dain, ta teloso hummus, that by day" is cited as an example of the kind of music Plato was referring to when he expressed his strong opinions on its impact. This specific ancient Greek phrase is presented as a representation of the music of his time. "Horses on this fine moon made in hollow, so beautiful, pro soligone, esti ta dain, ta teloso hummus, that by day." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Ancient Origins of Tattoos** : Tattoos have a history stretching back thousands of years, with evidence found on mummified remains. Examples include Otsul, discovered in the Swiss Alps after a glacier melted, who had 61 tattoos and lived over 5,000 years ago. Egyptian mummies, Pacific Islanders, ancient African communities, bodies from Iron Age Britain, early Japanese societies, and indigenous peoples of North and South America all engaged in body art. "Archaeologists have found mummified remains that are thousands and thousands of years old that sport tattoos. There's a guy named Otsul. He was found in the Swiss Elps when a glacier melted. He'd been there for over 5,000 years and the dude had 61 tattoos, Egyptian mummies, Pacific Islanders, members of ancient African communities, bodies dating to Iron Age Britain, early Japanese societies, and the indigenous peoples of North and South America have all engaged in this kind of body art." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jZeMmPekKMQ
**Ancient Origins of Ticket Scalping** : Ticket scalping, the practice of reselling tickets at inflated prices, has roots stretching back to ancient times. It's speculated that in ancient Rome, individuals outside the Coliseum likely engaged in similar activities, attempting to sell tickets. "Back in ancient Rome, there were probably guys and togas and sandals outside the Coliseum yelling, Quizz and Tiniot Terpiss, which is, I think, Latin for who's got tickets." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D8GU8ZpSgY8
**Andreas Pavel: The First Personal Music Player Concept (1972)** : In 1972, while walking in Brazil, Andreas Pavel conceived the revolutionary idea of listening to music on the go. He subsequently invented the "Stereo Belt," a small cassette player with headphones, which represented the very first conceptualization of a personal music player, years before Sony's Walkman would popularize the device. "The bottom line to all this is that Andreas Pavall was the guy who first came up with the concept of the personal music player." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PNiL63fY1Y8

**Architecture Influencing Music (Cathedrals)** : The architectural design of large, cavernous, and echoey stone cathedrals profoundly influenced the composition of music from the 12th century onwards. Composers like Hildegard von Bingen developed styles, such as slow, somber liturgical chanting (sacred monophony), that harmonized with the long reverberation times, preventing musical chaos and demonstrating how the "technology of architecture influenced the composition of music." "Because of this echo, because of the architectural design of these places, you have to be very careful with the music play during church services." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NAroxFbYkRw

**Audio Quality of Novelty Vinyl** : The audio quality of novelty vinyl records varies significantly. Picture discs are generally considered to have the worst sound quality, followed by glow-in-the-dark records. Records incorporating glitter or spattered colors can also produce "dodgy" sound. For optimal audio fidelity on vinyl, it is typically recommended to purchase basic black records. "In my experience, picture discs sound the worst, followed by any record made with something that makes them glow in the dark." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B2g4QSREzpw

**Auditory Cortex Function** : Located directly behind the ears and approximately the size of a thumb, the auditory cortex serves as a primary filter and sorter for all incoming audio information. It breaks down what we hear into fundamental components and then funnels these bits to the appropriate processing areas of the brain, working in conjunction with the cerebellum. "It's the thing that filters and sorts all the audio information coming at us. It breaks down what we hear into rudimentary bits and funnels those bits to the appropriate parts of the brain." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ

**Auto-Erotic Asphyxiation Theory (1999)** : In a 1999 interview on *60 Minutes* Australia, she suggested that Michael Hutchence died from auto-erotic asphyxiation gone wrong, a claim that the coroner explicitly refuted due to lack of evidence, but which nonetheless fueled tabloid speculation and was widely accepted by many. **Auto-Tune Technology Origins** : Auto-tune's core technology originated in the 1990s from Andy Hillbrand's work at Exxon, where he developed methods for interpreting seismic data to locate oil and gas deposits. Hillbrand later realized that the same underlying technology, which could detect, analyze, and modify seismic data, was transferable to audio files, allowing it to "detect, analyze, and modify the pitch of audio files," thereby creating real-time pitch correction for music. "Back in the 1990s, a guy named Andy Hillbrand was working for Exxon. His job was to develop techniques for plumbing the depths of the earth to locate deposits of oil and gas." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7Zniri9uSlc
**Auto-Tune in Live Concerts** : Auto-tune is not confined to studio use; it can also be deployed in live concert settings. This real-time pitch correction technology allows a performer's off-key notes, whether slightly flat or sharp, to be instantly corrected, making it sound as though the artist on stage is "nailing every note perfectly" and ensuring a flawless vocal performance during a show. "Auto-tune can be used in a concert setting, making it sound like the person on stage is nailing every note perfectly." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7Zniri9uSlc
**Auto-Tune's Robotic Effect** : When auto-tune is applied at extreme levels, it ceases to be a subtle pitch correction tool and instead creates a distinctive, "robotic effect" on the vocals. This artificial sound is a direct result of the technology being "turned up all the way to absurd levels" and is recognizable in many recordings. "That robotic effect? That's auto-tune turned up all the way to absurd levels." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7Zniri9uSlc

**Avro Arrow Project Cancellation (1959)** : The Canadian government canceled the Avro Arrow, a state-of-the-art jet fighter developed in the 1950s and considered one of the greatest air machines, on February 20th, 1959. This decision resulted in 50,000 people losing their jobs. However, many of the project's engineers were subsequently hired by the newly formed American organization NASA, becoming integral to the Apollo space program, or found work in Britain and France contributing to the development of Concorde. The cancellation is cited as an example of a "hinge factor," where a seemingly negative event had unforeseen, significant impacts on future projects. "So really, who knows if these two projects would have ever succeeded as well as they did had Prime Minister Diefenbiker not canceled the Avro Arrow?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MTDY6qT11Dc

**Backlash Against Moshing (21st Century)** : The 21st century saw a major backlash against moshing due to persistent injuries, lawsuits, and escalating insurance premiums for artists, promoters, and venues. **Backwards Masking: Decline and Digital Revival** : Backmasking saw a decline in the era of CDs due to the impossibility of playing a CD backward. However, the practice experienced a resurgence in the late 1990s and early 2000s with the widespread availability of digital sound editing software, which made creating and embedding backward messages much easier. "then back masking sort of went away in the era of the CD because, well, how are you going to spin a CD backward?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Backwards Masking: Definition** : Backwards masking, or backmasking, is a recording technique where a sound or message is recorded forward and then dubbed backward into a song. When the song is played, this specific segment is heard in reverse, creating an audio effect or a hidden message. "This is a recording trick where you record something forward and then dub it backward into a song so that when it's played, that piece is heard backward." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Backwards Masking: Early Film Use (1935)** : Reverse audio effects were incorporated into films as early as 1935, notably appearing in the movie "Gold Diggers of 1935," predating its common use in popular music. "Reverse audio can be found in the movie Gold Diggers of 1935." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Band Management Bureaucracy** : A significant challenge for Blink-182 during the recording of their "Neighborhoods" album was managing the complex bureaucracy that developed during their hiatus. Each of the three members had acquired separate managers, lawyers, accountants, and publicists, leading to a situation where the three-piece band had four managers at one point, making any decision-making process incredibly cumbersome. "At one point during the recording of neighborhoods, this three-piece band had four managers. Imagine trying to get anything done." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q-QP7ePxkQE

**Band Name and Domain Name Strategy** : In 1999, Linkin Park deliberately misspelled "Lincoln" in their name to "Linkin Park" specifically to secure the domain name "Lincolnpark.com." This foresight in leveraging the internet for branding was uncommon for bands at the time. "The reason they deliberately misspelled Lincoln, so they could get the domain, Lincolnpark.com." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cUqdY_T7luM
**Bands with Multiple Reunions** : Some groups, such as the Happy Mondays, are known for breaking up and reforming multiple times, often driven by recurring financial or tax problems, though such bands are excluded from this specific historical account of "clean breaks and definite reunions." "The happy Mondays come to mind. They get together every time they have tax problems." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=yR3xc3ra5tE
**Bastille – Dan Smith's Birthday, July 14; Bastille Day in France** : The band had a hard time finding a name until someone pointed out that singer Dan Smith's birthday is July 14 — Bastille Day in France. "That's Bastille Day in France." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE

**Beastie Boys Paul's Boutique Cover (1989) – Photo Is at 99 Rivington Street in Manhattan, Not Brooklyn; Lee's Sportswear, Not Paul's Boutique** : The cover of Paul's Boutique, photographed by Nathaniel Hornblower (Adam Yauch's alter ego), shows a shop supposedly in Brooklyn — but the photo was actually taken at 99 Rivington Street at the corner of Ludlow on the Lower East Side of Manhattan, close to where the Beastie Boys first rehearsed at 59 Christie Street near Hester and Canal. The store in the photo is actually called Lee's Sportswear. You can spot an Al Green record, a record by the Modern Lovers, and Dwight Gooden's New York Mets jersey hanging in the image. Today a coffee shop a few feet away is called Paul's Boutique — named after the album, not the other way around. "The shop in the photo is actually a store called Lee's Sportswear." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JdSUHkXM1mQ
**Beats Per Minute (BPM) as a Tempo Measurement** : BPM, or beats per minute, is a fundamental measurement of tempo, widely recognized in DJ culture for selecting music suitable for the dance floor. It ranges from 80-100 BPM for rock and hip hop, 120-135 BPM for house music, and 200+ BPM for genres like Gabber and Speedcore. "It means beats per minute. It's a measurement of tempo." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zWNzlSxrj6s
**Belarusian President's Control Over Radio Music** : Alexander Lukashenko, the president and dictator of Belarus, exercises complete control over the music played on Belarusian radio. He enforces a 20% limit on songs by foreign artists and has banned so many local performers he dislikes that radio stations struggle to find enough music to fill their airtime. "Alexander Lukashenko is the president and dictator of Belarus. He has complete control over what artists get played on Belarusian radio. Songs by foreign artists are limited to 20%. That he has banned so many local performers because he doesn't like them that Belarusian radio stations have a hard time finding enough music to play." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aSk1XQHNkd8
**Bell Labs' Role in Big Muff** : Mike Matthews, founder of Electroharmonics, hired Bob Meyer, an engineer from Bell Labs, to develop the Big Muff pedal in 1969. Meyer's expertise was sought to create a foot pedal that could deliver both on-demand fuzz and significant sustain, which became key features of the influential Big Muff. "He hired an engineer at Bell Labs, named Bob Meyer, to come up with a foot pedal that could provide on-demand fuzz, but also one that could make a guitar sound ring for a long time." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iGav9uJwA_w
**Beneath the Boardwalk Demos** : "Beneath the Boardwalk" was the title given to a collection of Arctic Monkeys demo tracks by a fan named Mark Bull, also known as The Sheriff. This title referenced a regular venue where the band performed. The collection, which eventually contained 18 songs, was instrumental in the band's online breakthrough as fans downloaded and shared the music. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YvcnHKI4oIw
**Benefits of Apple Commercial Placement - Music Video Replacement** : For artists, Apple commercial placements offer a dual benefit: they act as a 30-second advertisement for their music, essentially doubling as a music video. This eliminates the need to spend thousands on producing a video that might not get airplay or be discovered on YouTube. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk

Engaging in hobbies allows individuals to step away from their instruments, explore other interests, and become more well-rounded. For successful musicians, hobbies also offer an opportunity to indulge in long-held dreams and spend accumulated wealth. "Everybody needs a break from whatever it is that they do. You gotta rest the brain, recharge and go in a search for new inspiration." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xc85sLj0Cnk

He then called the record company and informed them that the dealer would have bootlegs on the street within a week unless the artwork was fixed. The label capitulated. **Birth of Punk Rock in New York (1973-1974)** : The simultaneous collapse of the Mercer Art Center in August 1973, which displaced New York's "weird music freaks," and the subsequent rise of CBGB as a music venue provided the essential conditions for punk rock's birth. Television's pioneering gigs at CBGB, starting in December 1973, attracted former Mercer Art Center regulars and led owner Hilly Crystal to pivot his club's music policy, making CBGB "ground zero" for punk rock throughout 1974 and the rest of the decade. "The collapse of the Mercer Art Center and the rise of CBGBs in New York. Two events that when combined together gave punk rock a place to be born." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MTDY6qT11Dc

**Blackwork Tattoos - History and Characteristics** : Blackwork tattoos are a style with a history dating back thousands of years. Ancient peoples used such body art to signify identity, loyalties, and authority, a designation that evolved into "tribal tattoo." This style entered modern tattoo culture towards the end of the 1980s, influenced by the book *Modern Primitives*. Due to the extensive ink required, Blackwork pieces demand many hours of tattooing and are associated with significant pain. "This is called a Blackwork tattoo and has a history going back thousands of years. Ancient peoples use such body art to promote their identity, their loyalties, and their authority, and it's the designation as a tribal tattoo." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jZeMmPekKMQ

**Blink-182 "Enema of the State" Cover – Red Cross Symbol Removed Under Geneva Convention Complaint** : The original album cover featured a red cross on the nurse's hat. "Blink understood and changed it to what we see now." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZbHRIh3RUoo

**Blink-182 – Multiple Stories; Most Likely Random; Possibly "F*** Off" in Poway High School Code** : Originally just Blink, forced to add a suffix due to an Irish band with prior rights. The 182 has multiple explanations: times Tony Montana says the F-word in Scarface (widely cited but disputed), Mark Hoppus's ideal weight in pounds, a ship his grandfather served on. Most likely it was pulled randomly out of the air during a phone call with the label. Additional theory: at Tom DeLonge's high school in Poway, California, "182" was code for the F-word (8th letter = H? No: B=18th letter... actually under this theory "go" meaning 182). DeLonge has discussed this, suggesting the name should be pronounced "Blink F**k Off." "Blink 182 or Blink 182 if you want to go with the Tom DeLong explanation." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ

**Bootlegging and Organized Crime – Mafia, IRA, Al-Qaeda Connections** : The bootleg trade has historically had documented links to organized crime. "Has had historical ties to organized crime, from the Mafia to accusations of funding the IRA in the 80s or Al-Qaeda in the South American 'triple frontier.'" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Uly2cT2vc28
**Bootlegging of Unreleased Material** : Unreleased or demo material from famous musicians, even if "never supposed to be released," often finds its way to the public through bootlegs. For example, Dave Grohl's 16 demo songs from 1994, despite being discarded, appeared on an "unofficial CD" (a bootleg) released in Japan in 1995. Similarly, his Pre-Foo Fighters demos were "immediately bootlegged" after limited distribution to friends. "But, like I said, nothing that Dave has ever done seems to disappear." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_AY5lS-FmlU
**Bootlegging of the Show** : The speaker's show has been extensively bootlegged over the years. This includes cassette tapes being sold for $40 each in independent record stores (such as in Chicago) and instances of the show being broadcast over shortwave radio at festivals. Additionally, torrent sites are populated with these shows. The speaker acknowledges there is "nothing we can do about it." "My sister was living in Chicago for a while. She went into an independent record store and they had a whole bunch of cassettes out into the counter that were were my shows taped off the radio somewhere. And they were selling them for 40 bucks a piece." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90
**Border Blaster Mexican Radio Stations – 500,000-Watt Signals Covering the Continent** : While US and Canadian AM stations were capped at 50,000 watts, Mexican stations just across the US border operated at 100,000, 250,000, or even 500,000 watts — powerful enough for signals to reach across North America and sometimes Europe. Birds approaching transmitters were literally cooked by the electromagnetic radiation. The most famous was XERF AM in Ciudad Acuña (across from Del Rio, Texas), associated with Wolfman Jack, which could reportedly be heard continuously from New York to LA. XERB near Tijuana claimed 500,000 watts while branding itself as "the mighty 1090 in Hollywood" to seem like a US station. "Animals coming too close to the transmitters would be literally cooked to death." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iyGUXdDqIlI
**Boredom with Conventional Rock and Pop (Late 1960s)** : By the end of the 1960s, a growing number of music fans became bored with conventional rock and pop. They actively sought out and reveled in music that was different and challenging, especially if it was disagreeable to the mainstream and hippie culture. "By the end of the 1960s, there was a growing number of music fans who were bored with conventional rock and pop." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6oUkMOkEr9U
**Boston Area Music Scene** : The Boston area fostered a rich musical subculture, boasting 11 universities and colleges, plus the prestigious Berklee College of Music. This concentration of institutions attracted people from around the world to share ideas, leading to the emergence of many influential indie bands. "For some cities, it was an embarrassment of riches. For example, there are 11 universities and colleges in the Boston area, plus the prestigious Berkeley College of Music. This means people from all over the world meet in the Boston area to share ideas." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sCtQqVBtCaI
**Bots and Instant Sell-outs** : Online ticket sales are heavily targeted by scalpers using automated software programs called "bots." These bots, combined with the high-speed processing capabilities of ticketing systems like Ticketmaster, can hammer online box offices with thousands of requests per minute, causing a limited public ticket inventory to sell out within 60 seconds. "Plus we have scalpers using software buying programs called bots to hammer the online box office with requests for tickets." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8q2bRZyHnHE

**Brain Connectivity and Chills** : Research from California indicates that individuals who frequently experience chills when listening to music possess a greater number of connecting fibers between their auditory cortex and the brain regions responsible for processing emotions. This enhanced communication allows for a more fluid interplay between music and emotions, leading to a distinct physical response, suggesting such individuals have an "extra special brain." "people who get chills when listening to music have more fibers connecting the auditory cortex to those parts of the brain that deal with processing emotions." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Brain Wave Music – Neural Oscillations Can Be Transposed Into Audible Music; Used to Treat Depression and Anxiety** : Brain activity produces electrical neural oscillations (brain waves): delta, theta, alpha, and beta waves at very low frequencies. Scientists discovered that by transposing these waves up into audible frequency ranges, the resulting sounds can be used therapeutically. Doctors have found that playing a patient's own brain waves back to them appears to reboot brain chemistry in ways that treat insomnia, anxiety, and depression. Classically trained cellist Katinka Kleijn demonstrated the technique by playing her own EEG brain waves live alongside her cello. "The music of your own brain can be used to treat certain neurological and psychological conditions." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NMwMwqMQpf4
**Brain's Ability to Correctly Identify Reversed Music** : An experiment demonstrated that even when presented with a half-second clip of a song played in reverse, the brain's extremely fast processing of musical memories allowed for correct identification of the song. This illustrates the remarkable efficiency and robustness of our memory system for music. "Yet your brain would have none of that. It worked so fast with your musical memories that it was able to correctly identify the song even though it was hearing it wrong." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Brain's Effort to Process Compressed MP3s (Theory 2)** : Another theory posits that when the brain receives an MP3, it subconsciously registers that something is missing, even if the ear can't consciously detect the stripped-out audio. The brain then attempts to fill in these blanks, either by accessing analog memories or by finding nothing, which takes extra milliseconds before the music reaches consciousness. This additional processing effort disrupts connections with emotional centers, stunting dopamine production and leading to a diminished sense of enjoyment compared to uncompressed or analog music. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BHN6db7m3DM
**Brain's Musical Hardwiring** : The human brain, a three-pound organ containing billions of neurons, appears to be naturally hardwired for music, possessing special areas exclusively devoted to processing musical information. Possible evolutionary theories suggest this might be a result of ancient ancestors imitating bird song, a development related to language, a tool for storytelling (as details are easier to remember with music), or a phenomenon that evolved alongside religious rituals and chants. "There is no obvious biological reason for it, but our brain seemed to be hardwired for music. There were special areas of the brain devoted to just dealing with music and nothing else." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Breakdown of Music Silos** : The rigid "us versus them" tribalism that characterized rock music for decades, where fans were either alternative or mainstream, has diminished. Today, individuals can enjoy diverse music genres without stigma, exemplified by liking both The Beatles and a Norwegian death metal band. "all the silos have broken down. Johnny Rotten walked into Malcolm McLaren's clothing shop in 1975. He was immediately considered for the job of lead singer of the sex pistols, based on the fact that he was wearing an eye-hate pink Floyd t-shirt." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Breakdown of Traditional Cultural Gatekeepers** : In earlier eras, record labels, radio stations, and record stores acted as powerful cultural filters, influencing what music was considered good or widely available. The internet, particularly through file sharing, liberated music listeners from these traditional gatekeepers, allowing thousands of indie bands to be discovered and strengthening the position of indie artists and labels. "The internet had delivered them from the traditional cultural gatekeepers and it made it possible for thousands upon thousands upon thousands of indie bands to be discovered." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=raRCZ0Y5up8

**Brian May Uses Banjo Strings on Guitar – Creates Signature Queen Sound** : Brian May uses banjo strings on his guitars instead of standard guitar strings because they are lighter, thinner, and bend more easily. This technique is credited with producing Queen's signature guitar tone. "They're lighter and thinner and thus can bend much easier and that's how we got the signature Queen sound." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZbHRIh3RUoo

**Broca's Area and Musical Expression** : Broca's area, located between the frontal and temporal lobes, is a crucial brain region involved not only in the production of speech but also in the expression of music, such as singing or playing an instrument. It is situated in close proximity to Wernicke's area and the auditory cortex. "This is the spot that not only helps us produce speech, but it's what we use to express music, like playing an instrument or singing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Broken Social Scene – Kevin Drew's Jokey Gig as "John Tesh Jr. and the Broken Social Scene"** : Kevin Drew had a keyboard setup he likened to soft music king John Tesh. **Bromley Contingent** : The Bromley Contingent was a group of fans, including Jordan Mooney, who closely followed the Sex Pistols in their early days. Their presence and shared fashion sensibilities contributed to the development of the British punk rock scene. "Jordan followed the pistols everywhere as part of a pack of fans known as the Bromley contingent and wherever she went she influenced the fashion sense of punk rock." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Brunel Music Rating Inventory for Workout Music** : The Brunel Music Rating Inventory is a questionnaire developed over 20 years of research to rate the motivational qualities of music for sports and exercise. A key element is matching song tempo to workout intensity, with ideal tempos ranging from 120 beats per minute (for a brisk stroll) to 160 bpm (for a runner), roughly aligning with heart rates. Regular tempos are preferred, as changes in intensity or time signatures can disrupt rhythm. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BHN6db7m3DM
**Bryan Adams Concert Cancelled by "Fatberg" (2025, Perth, Australia)** : A Bryan Adams concert in Perth, Australia, in 2025 was cancelled due to a massive fatberg — an enormous accumulation of fat and waste — in nearby sewers that threatened to overflow the venue's bathrooms during the show. "A concert was cancelled due to a 'fatberg' in nearby sewers that threatened to overflow the venue's bathrooms." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0DFmS6MPbFI
