"Brandon, if you remember, was accidentally shot when an improperly loaded prop gun went off, wounding him fatally in the abdomen." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TDwagoyMvck
**Decades as Momentum-Driven Periods** : Decades don't simply end when the calendar flips to a new year; they often carry momentum or a "hangover" that extends their influence for one to three years. For instance, the 1950s arguably continued until 1963, and the 1960s' influence stretched into 1972-ish. "Decades have momentum, sometimes a hangover, that carries things forward for a year or two or even three afterwards." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5Y6nHw5xx88
**Decimation of the Musician Middle Class** : The dramatic reduction in artist income from streaming and declining sales has "decimated the middle class of musicians," which historically served as the breeding ground for superstars, creating a gap between huge top acts and a large underclass of struggling performers. "This has decimated the middle class of musicians, the traditional breeding ground for superstars." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Decline in High-Fidelity Sound Pursuit** : Since the turn of the millennium, there has been a societal shift away from prioritizing "pure, clear sound," with many now content with the fidelity offered by cheap earbuds or laptop speakers. This contrasts sharply with the 1970s, 80s, and 90s, when a passionate pursuit of "perfect sound" (big, tight bass; accurate mid-range; bright, smooth highs) led many—predominantly men—to spend "thousands upon thousands of dollars" on elaborate home stereo equipment and car audio systems, engaging in detailed comparisons of technical specifications and brands. "But sometime after the turn of the millennium, society shrunk away from pure, clear sound." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7Zniri9uSlc
**Decline in Musical Tribalism** : Younger generations of music fans, those who came of age in the new millennium, are far more "ecumenical" in their tastes and less tribal than previous generations. Technology allows them to freely sample music across all genres and eras, frequently switching between rock, hip hop, pop, classic rock, dance, and EDM. "People who came of age musically in the new millennium aren't nearly as tribal as previous generations." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Decline in Superstar Rock Acts** : The music industry has done a "terrible job" of generating new superstar rock acts on the same level as in previous decades. "We have done a terrible job of generating new superstar rock acts on the same level that we used to." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Decline of "Star-Making Machinery" in the 21st Century** : In the 2000s, with the rise of streaming and the decline of physical media and record stores, the power of traditional "cultural gatekeepers" (record labels, radio stations, music magazines, video channels) significantly diminished. They could no longer create a consensus around "superstar" acts, as individual listeners became their own music directors with vast access to music. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Decline of CD Profits & Rise of Streaming** : The significant profit margins once associated with CD sales are irrecoverable, as streaming has fundamentally replaced traditional methods of music consumption, leading to a drastically different and less lucrative revenue model for artists compared to physical sales. "Those margins and profits on CDs are not coming back. Streaming has supplanted the old ways when it comes to the way people consume music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Decline of Cultural Gatekeepers and Consensus** : In the past, five major "cultural gatekeepers" (radio stations, record stores, record labels, music magazines, and video channels) determined popular music, creating scarcity and strong consensus around artists like KISS, who became "very socially important." Today, with streaming, this ubiquity and consensus are gone; even huge artists like Taylor Swift do not achieve the same level of universal recognition as bands of previous eras. "There were five major cultural gatekeepers. There were radio stations, record stores, record labels, music magazines, and I guess after a while video channels. Those were the things that determined the music that we listened to." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90
**Decline of Early 1990s Alt-Rock Scenes** : By the late 1990s, the "awesomeness" of early 1990s alternative rock subgenres such as grunge, industrial, Manchester, and Britpop had faded. This left a void and a sense of disillusionment among fans, exacerbated by the lingering specter of Kurt Cobain's suicide, and rock was "flailing" to find the "next big thing." "The awesomeness of the alternation of the early 1990s, with grunge and industrial and Manchester and Britpop, had faded away." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Decline of Independent Live Music Venues** : Many independent live music venues closed during the 2010s due to high rents, gentrification, or an inability to generate sufficient revenue. This reduction in performance spaces meant fewer opportunities for new bands to develop their sound and gain live experience. "Many, many independent live music venues closed during the 2010s because owners were unable to make enough money to keep the lights on, squeezed up by higher rents or became victims of gentrification." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5Y6nHw5xx88
**Decline of Package Tours (Late 1960s)** : The package tour approach, common since the 1950s, began to decline in the late 1960s as the music business started producing artists with enough individual appeal and drawing power to tour independently and fill larger venues like arenas and stadiums, where the real money was made. "This package tour approach was pretty common until the late 1960s when the music business was producing artists big enough to tour on their own and play arenas and later stadiums." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7jfQaUV6Bq4
**Decline of Record Stores and Rise of Online Retailers** : The necessity of visiting physical record stores diminished with the advent of online platforms like iTunes, P2P programs, and torrent sites, which offered instant access to music. Online ordering also provided a more convenient way to obtain physical copies, eliminating stock issues. "Many people really don't feel the need to go to a record store anymore. iTunes, P2P programs, and torrent sites give us almost instant access to whatever we want, often whenever the spirit moves us and wherever we happen to be." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Decline of Traditional Music Formats** : Sales of CDs and global album sales are projected to continue their decline, while the purchase of individual digital tracks is experiencing a significant collapse. "CD sales will continue to fall. The global album sales continue to decline. And the purchase of digital tracks are cratering." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Decline of Traditional Music Gatekeepers (Post-2000)** : The rise of the internet around 2000 led to a rapid decline in the power of traditional cultural gatekeepers in the music industry. Record labels saw their century-old business model of selling physical plastic collapse. Record stores experienced reduced foot traffic, leading to the closure of major international chains. Music magazines suffered a collapse in revenue as labels cut advertising and consumers sought information online. YouTube effectively "killed off music videos on television." Only radio, though still powerful, popular, and profitable, now shares its dominance with the digital world. "The power, the traditional cultural gatekeepers enjoyed before the rise of the internet, waned quickly." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xid8CZf4oYo
**Decline of Traditional Record Stores** : While record stores continue to exist, their numbers have significantly dwindled compared to their "glory days" from the 1960s to the late 1990s. Many legendary stores and chains have permanently disappeared, reflecting a shift in how music is acquired and consumed. "Record stores are still with us, but there were fewer and fewer of them." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jD1dWxNLvfE
**Declining Licensing Fees for Indie Artists** : While licensing deals initially offered a significant income boost for indie bands, the widespread adoption of this strategy led to increased competition and a subsequent decrease in the amount of money offered for placements, especially for lesser-known acts. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Declining Record Sales Impact** : The music industry has seen a significant shift where "nobody's buying records" anymore, and the revenue model is "all about streaming." This decline in physical sales is a driving factor for artists, especially older generations, to sell their catalogs. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Dee Dee Ramone's Failed Robbery Attempt** : In his youth, Douglas Colvin (Dee Dee Ramone) attempted to rob a neighborhood drug store. **Deep Six Compilation (1985)** : This compilation, released on the CZ label in the fall of 1985, featured contributions from several local Seattle bands. Although it took two years to sell all 2000 copies, it was a pivotal record as the first time people could hear and recognize the distinct sound emerging from their city. "But then in the fall of 1985, several local bands contributed material to a compilation called Deep Six, a label called CZ. Although it took two years for all 2000 copies to sell out, this was a really important record. The first time people could hear what was happening in their city." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sCtQqVBtCaI
**Definition and Components of Metadata** : Metadata refers to the descriptive information embedded within a digital audio file, encompassing details such as song title, artist, album title, composer, genre, release year, song length, track number, artwork, lyrics, bit rate, and sampling rate, all of which are crucial for identification. "Metadata is the information about a song embedded within the digital file." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Definition of Indie Music** : Indie music refers to artists who undertake all aspects of their work independently, without assistance from major established record labels. This often includes self-producing albums or even launching and running their own record labels to release their music. "indie, as far as we're concerned, means artists who have done everything on their own with no help, that is independent from one of the big established record labels." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LgJ7ww2AgF4
**Definition of Plagiarism** : Plagiarism in music, and in general, is defined as passing off someone else's original work as one's own without acknowledging the true creator. It is considered cheating, unethical, dishonest, and a form of theft, capable of ruining reputations if proven. "Plagiarism is when you pass off someone else's work as your own without ever acknowledging the original creator. And plagiarism is a nasty thing. It's cheating. It's unethical. It's dishonest and it's theft, plain and simple." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=L09R2evjyMc
**Definition of Streaming** : Streaming is defined as the ability to listen to songs transmitted to a device over the internet on demand. Full-featured streaming services allow access to any song on any number of devices, anytime and anywhere, exemplified by platforms like Spotify, Apple Music, and Deezer. "This is the ability to listen to songs transmitted to your device over the internet on demand." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Definition of a "Superstar" Act** : A superstar act is characterized by selling tens of millions of units, drawing tens of thousands of people who would "crawl over broken glass" for tickets, possessing a deep catalog of hits released over many years, and achieving a consensus among millions of people that they are great and worthy of love and devotion. "I'm talking about an act that sells music by the tens of millions of units." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Definition of a Generation (ISGG)** : The International Society of Genetic Genealogy (ISGG) specifies the length of a generation to be between 29 and 31 years, aligning closely with Wikipedia's definition regarding the child-parent child cycle of human existence. "The International Society of Genetic Genealogy sets the length of a generation between 29 and 31 years." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=v_am7ifh7Pk
**Definition of a Generation (Wikipedia)** : According to Wikipedia, a generation is defined as approximately 30 years, representing the time required for children to be born, grow up, become adults, and then have children of their own. "Well, according to Wikipedia, it's about 30 years, which is the time it takes children to be born, grow up, become adults, and then start to have children of their own." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=v_am7ifh7Pk
**Del Glover – Leaked 20,000+ Unreleased Albums Online Over 11 Years** : Del Glover, a temporary warehouse employee, was responsible for leaking at least 20,000 unreleased albums online over an eleven-year period. His motivation was not financial gain but the desire to be the first to release material. "Leaked at least 20,000 unreleased albums online in 11 years, motivated by the desire to be the first, not by profit." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Uly2cT2vc28
**Demise of Digital Rights Management (DRM)** : Digital Rights Management (DRM), which previously restricted the sharing and transfer of legitimately purchased music across devices, became obsolete. The music industry's efforts to lock down music and sue file-sharers ultimately failed, leading to a landscape free of these technological barriers. "digital rights management, those locks that made it very, very difficult to share music, even when it came to moving legitimately purchased songs from one device to another that you all own, that's all dead. DRM is done." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Democratization of Music Creation and Distribution Leading to Glut** : The barrier to entry for releasing music has drastically lowered due to cheap and powerful home recording equipment and easy uploading to streaming platforms, YouTube, and TikTok. This offers "instant global distribution" and cuts out traditional "cultural gatekeepers" like record labels, radio, and magazines, which previously filtered new music, allowing only about 2,500 new albums per year. While promoting democratization, this ease of entry has resulted in a massive "glut of music," with over 100,000 songs uploaded daily. By early 2025, approximately 202 million songs will be available, but an estimated 25% (over 50 million) have never been heard, illustrating a diluted and cheaper music consumption experience. "Today, though, the barrier to entry for anyone wanting to release music is so low that anyone can do it. Home recording equipment is cheap and powerful, and uploading your music to the streaming music platforms can be done with a push of a button." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZzIqIydZTlA
**Demonstration of Double-Sided Records (1910)** : A demonstration recording from 1910 promoted the innovative "Columbia Double Disc Records," which featured different selections on each side. These records were explicitly not for sale but served to illustrate the "double value" proposition, offering two recordings for only a few cents more than a single-sided record, playable on any disc machine, including Columbia Graphophones or Victor Talking Machines. "The purpose of this record is to demonstrate the Columbia Double Disc Records." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jD1dWxNLvfE
**Depeche Mode – Name of a French Fashion Magazine; Translates as "Fast Fashion"** : The name is directly taken from a French fashion magazine called Dépêche Mode. "It translates as fast fashion." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Despacito's Energy Cost – 5 Billion Streams Could Heat 40,000 Homes for a Year** : An analysis of the energy required to stream "Despacito" by Luis Fonsi and Daddy Yankee 5 billion times found that the equivalent electricity could have heated 40,000 homes for an entire year. "40,000 homes could have been heated for a year with the equivalent amount of electricity." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fnZx8EGnszw
**Deterioration of Vinyl Quality (Late 1970s/Early 1980s)** : Due to the 1973 oil crisis, the recording industry began using recycled, impure vinyl and producing thinner records to cut costs. This resulted in "more rumble, more hiss, more clicks, more pops," shallower grooves causing skips, and increased warping. By the late 1970s and early 1980s, the quality of new vinyl records was often inferior to older, used records, making consumers eager for the superior audio offered by the compact disc when it arrived in late 1982. "Vinyl quality deteriorated to the point where it was so bad that when the CD came along in late 1982, it was exactly what lovers of good sound were looking for." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NAroxFbYkRw
**Developmental Psychology and Personal Growth** : The transformation of Ash Boo Shultz from a control-averse, internally struggling artist to a collaborative and connected performer is described as an "incredible beautiful experiment" rooted in developmental psychology. His journey from hysterically leaving songwriting sessions to openly connecting with an audience on stage highlights the success of this personal evolution. "Isn't it an incredible expect credible beautiful experiment Alan when you can take the same person which is what developmental psychology is all about you can take the same person who who hysterically had to leave the idea of working with another person on a song in 2011 and then you can fast forward to 2017 and now you're singing who's with me and I'm I'm overjoyed to say that this public experiment has been successful." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=N-3eddy4J7g
**Diamond Record Sales Achievement** : In America, a diamond record signifies the sale of 10 million physical copies of an album. While past mega-sellers like Michael Jackson's "Thriller" (65 million), AC/DC's "Back in Black" (50 million), and Pink Floyd's "Dark Side of the Moon" (45 million) achieved significantly higher numbers, current mega-sellers typically reach around 2.5 million copies. The era of such massive physical sales is believed to be over due to declining physical sales and the rise of music streaming. "In America this means you've sold 10 million copies, 10 million physical copies of your album." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Epz5Sn151bk
**Difficulty Transitioning from Rock Star Life** : After years immersed in the "rock star bubble," many musicians find it challenging to transition back to being a "civilian" or "normal person," missing the crowds and gigs. "And after living in a rock star bubble for years, it's hard to make the transition to being a civilian, a normal person." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=yR3xc3ra5tE
**Difficulty for New Bands to Gain Traction** : In the contemporary music industry, new bands releasing a debut record face a very narrow window, typically 6 to 13 weeks after the first single's release, to generate significant traction with radio, retail, and fans. Failure to achieve this, or to succeed with a second single, can severely jeopardize a band's career. "If you're a new band with a debut record, you've got anywhere from 6 to 13 weeks to make an impression once that first single comes out." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ooNAHswiT5Q
**Difficulty of 21st Century Rock Superstardom** : It is significantly more challenging for rock acts to achieve superstar status in the 21st century compared to previous eras, largely due to drastic changes in the music industry and how fans consume music. "Why is it so much harder to be a superstar rock act in the 21st century?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Digital Jukebox Concept** : Professor Dieter Selzer, an expert in psychoacoustics and advisor to Carlheinz Brandenburg, envisioned a "digital jukebox" in the 1980s. This system would store all the world's music on a central server, accessible by anyone with a telephone line, a concept that was initially rejected as impossible for a patent. "Selzer had this dream of what he called a digital jukebox. A system whereby all the music in the world would be stored on a central server which then could be accessed by anyone with a telephone line." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Digital Jukebox to Streaming Evolution** : The concept of the digital jukebox, initially proposed by Professor Selzer, evolved into the modern streaming music service as internet exchange of songs became widespread. This progression allowed for on-demand access to music libraries, fulfilling the original vision. "As people got into the idea of exchanging songs over the internet, we really didn't have much further to go, at least in a tactical sense, before we went back to Professor Seltsor's idea of the digital jukebox." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Digital Music Consumption** : The increasing popularity of downloading and digital platforms like iTunes led to fans typically buying individual songs, challenging the traditional album format and prompting record labels to seek strategies, such as concept albums, to preserve it. "See fans were getting far too used to the idea of being able to just buy one song at a time and not buying full albums." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1KyNY3zv6uc
**Digital Music Origins (Microsoft vs. IBM)** : The rise of streaming music services can be traced back to the rivalry between Microsoft and IBM in the early 1990s to develop a user-friendly graphical operating system for personal computers. Microsoft's Windows 95, a large program that necessitated the use of CD-ROMs for installation, inadvertently made CD-ROM drives ubiquitous, which then allowed users to rip music from CDs to their hard drives, ultimately leading to MP3s and streaming. "We can trace the rise of streaming music services back to a fight between Microsoft and IBM in the early 1990s." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NAroxFbYkRw
**Digital Trickery and Lack of Talent** : Digital recording and editing technologies, particularly sophisticated software like Pro Tools, can be used to mask a performer's lack of talent. While beneficial for production, this capability means artists are not required to be as "spot on" during recording sessions, as "glaring mistakes" can be digitally corrected in post-production. This practice is criticized for leading to "unreal and unnatural recordings," contrasting with the analog era where artists had to perfect their parts and imperfections were sometimes valued for their beauty. "If you could fix it in the mix, it absolves you of being spot on during recording." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7Zniri9uSlc
**Diminished Artist Payouts from Streaming** : Artists receive only a fraction of a cent per stream, comparable to radio play, which is significantly less than the income from selling a digital file or CD. This, combined with declining CD sales, has led to a shrinking flow of money to artists and composers. "A single stream pays a fraction of a cent, much in the same way that a single play on the radio pays." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Disbursement Error due to Generic Song Titles** : When a generic title like "I Love You" is streamed, services must identify the correct artist, and if metadata is faulty, they often default to the most popular song with that title, potentially misdirecting royalties to an unrelated artist. "The streaming music services have to figure out which I love you it is, which artists it really belongs to." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Disney's CDVU Plus Failure** : Disney attempted a similar initiative to Warner Music Group's digital liner notes with a product called "CDVU Plus." However, this effort to enhance digital music with interactive content did not gain traction or significant interest from consumers. **Distortion Definition** : Distortion, also known as overdrive, occurs when an electrical signal is pushed past the capacity of an amplifier's circuitry, making it too loud or powerful. This process causes the signal to clip, where its peaks and troughs are cut off, introducing new characteristics like overtones, sustain, and compression. "Distortion is also known as overdrive. Basically it means you've pushed the electrical signal past what the circuitry and the amplifier can handle." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iGav9uJwA_w
**Diverse British Music Scene of Early 1980s** : By the early 1980s, British music diversified significantly, moving in "all directions at once." This included the quirkiness of The Cure, the goth sounds of Bauhaus, the harsh industrial music of Throbbing Gristle, the four-octave voice of Kate Bush, a ska revival, and deepened interest in reggae and rockabilly, all prioritizing unfettered self-expression over traditional rock virtuosity. "By the beginning of the 1980s, it was obvious that music in Britain had gone off in all directions at once. This wave of fresh new talent was unconcerned about being good enough to tear off a lead zeppelin style guitar solo." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9uTORLOm5Yg
**Diverse Early Retailers for Records** : Beyond dedicated record stores and furniture shops, records were sold in a variety of other retail outlets, including department stores such as Sears, Kresge's, Kmart, and Woolworths, as well as independent stores and even drug stores. These establishments typically featured small displays with four to six bins, holding around thirty records each, with no more than two copies per title. "Department stores had them. Sears, Cresgies, Cammart, Woolworths." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jD1dWxNLvfE
**Doc Kauffman's Innovations and Collaboration with Leo Fender** : Doc Kauffman, a lap pedal steel guitarist and former Rickenbacker employee, invented the Vibrola, a precursor to the whammy bar. He collaborated with Leo Fender, with Leo handling electronics and Doc focusing on guitar design, on building lap steel guitars. Doc eventually moved on by 1946. "One day he met Doc Kaufman. He was a lap pedal steel guitarist, not a wine guitarist. He once had a job with Rick and Bokker. In fact, he was the guy who invented something called the Vibrola, which would later evolve into something we now call the Whammy Bar. Leo and Doc started building up lap steel guitars. Leo handled the electronics and Doc took care of guitar design. But by 1946, Doc had decided to move on." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=E6cXyaHALBQ

Research indicates that dogs are most soothed by music that aligns closely with their own heartbeat. "There has actually been plenty of scientific study into this area as dog people are looking to help animals with separation anxiety, animals that are hyperactive or are scared of thunderstorms." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GO0K_N7Ys7I

**Dominance of Pre-Internet Rock Bands in Touring** : In the 2010s, the biggest rock bands capable of filling arenas, amphitheaters, and stadiums were overwhelmingly those who had established their careers and achieved many big hits before the internet disrupted the music industry around 2000. **Don Letts' Band Lifespan Theory** : Don Letts, a British DJ and filmmaker involved in the original punk scene and close to The Clash, theorizes that the average "proper lifespan" for most bands is seven to nine years. He believes this period allows bands to "be born, to rise, to peak, and then explode," typically due to internal pressures such as creative differences and diverging lifestyles. "He believes the average and proper lifespan of most bands is seven years, nine at the outside. He said that was enough time for them to be born, to rise, to peak, and then explode, usually due to some kind of internal pressures." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=t2uXHP9cBdM
**Dopamine and Musical Pleasure** : The brain areas—nucleus accumbens, amygdala, and cerebellum—secrete dopamine, a natural "feel-good" hormone. When music, particularly a song that induces chills or makes hair stand up, triggers dopamine, the body experiences pleasure and associates that song with feeling good, creating a chemical link between music and positive emotion. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BHN6db7m3DM
**Dorian Mode and Ancient Greek War Music** : The ancient Greeks used music, specifically a special marching music named after the Dorian Greeks called Dorian mode, to motivate and psychologically prepare for war. This practice highlights an early recognition of music's power to influence physical and mental states. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BHN6db7m3DM
**Dotcom Bubble Impact** : The dotcom bubble was cited as the reason why Sony's plans to create a series of animated shorts for The Smashing Pumpkins' *Machina* concept never came to fruition. "Dotcom bubble you understand." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1KyNY3zv6uc
**Dr. Peter Goldmark and the Invention of Vinyl Records** : Dr. Peter Goldmark, chief engineer for Columbia Records, spearheaded the development of vinyl records in the 1940s. Faced with a shellac shortage due to World War II, Goldmark's team innovated by using polyvinyl chloride (vinyl), a material previously used for sewer pipes, as a record substrate. This groundbreaking invention led to more durable records that could hold five times more music per side than shellac discs, fundamentally transforming the recording industry with the introduction of the LP and single formats. "This is where Columbia records stepped in with their chief engineer, a guy by the name of Dr. Peter Goldmark." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**Dr. Seuss Quote** : A quote from Dr. Seuss, "Don't cry because it's over. Smile because it happened," was used as a fitting closing sentiment for a program dedicated to The Tragically Hip after Gord Downie's passing, encapsulating the appreciation for his life and work. "It goes like this. Don't cry because it's over. Smile because it happened." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Um_KEEcCeT4
**Dramatic Audio Quote (N/A)** : An unidentified audio clip, presented as part of the "sound of history," states, "The councils. They've banned my concepts, and they take one money." **Dream Instruments** : Many musicians harbor a clear vision of the instruments they aspire to own, often making do with what they can afford initially while never losing sight of the goal to one day acquire an iconic rock and roll machine. These dream instruments are desired globally regardless of skill level, valued for their sound, playability, and association with famous musicians. "If you know what you're doing, you can get the job done on any instrument. But if you're able to choose anything, I'm Alain Cross." (Ignoring the host intro, the statement about choice stands as a general curiosity). ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Y0HW8LQKvJw
**Drug Smugglers Hid Ketamine in Kinder Eggs Inserted Into Their Bodies at Creamfields** : Marshall Maddock and Harry Hewitt-Simms tried to smuggle ketamine into the Creamfields music festival by concealing drug packets in Kinder eggs stuffed into their rectums. Specially trained sniffer dogs found a small amount of drugs on them; when they refused further searches, an intimate examination discovered the concealed eggs. Both were sentenced to 18 months in prison. "Each man was found to have kinder eggs stuffed up their bum's each containing 10 packets of ketamine." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fnZx8EGnszw
**Drum Recording Technique ("Chamber of Density")** : A specialized drum recording technique involves capturing drums in a dry, small room, then routing the sound through a band's PA system set up in an adjacent, empty warehouse. The PA is then re-mic'd to achieve a more powerful, "harder hitting" sound, creating a unique "chamber of density" effect without conventional reverb. This method was notably used by U2 for "Bullet the Blue Sky" and later by Rage Against the Machine for "Killing in the Name" in 1992. "For you technical people out there there’s kind of a variation on the reverb chamber but without reverb, a chamber of density." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=L03Yk1SHRNM
**Drummers' Significant Contributions to Rock Music – Beyond the Spotlight** : Drummers have made very significant, yet often underappreciated, contributions to music throughout the history of rock and roll, a genre where "all the glory is gone to the singers and the guitar players." Without the input of these individuals, the music we listen to today "might not have been possible." This includes those who altered the course of rock music, even if they weren't necessarily the "best drummers or the most talented drummers." "drummers have made some very significant Contributions to music and without these people what we listened to today Might not have been possible." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gsSTJWN6cUo
**Dual Objectives of Cancon** : The Canadian content rules served a dual purpose: a cultural strategy to expose Canadians to music from their own country rather than solely American and British fare, and an industrial strategy to foster a domestic music creation infrastructure including studios, labels, producers, engineers, agents, and promoters. "First, make sure that Canadians got to hear music from other Canadians instead of just a steady diet of American and British music. In that sense, it was a cultural strategy. But this was also an industrial strategy." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Duration of Licensed Music Snippets** : Unless the licensing deal is for an entire soundtrack album, the agreement typically involves using only a short "snippet" of a song. These snippets commonly range from 15, 20, or 30 seconds in length. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Dynamic Pricing Controversy and Price Moderation** : Dynamic pricing often causes initial controversy when tours go on sale, especially for popular acts, as high demand can lead to exorbitant initial prices (e.g., $5,000 for nosebleed seats). However, demand typically moderates after the first few days, and algorithms adjust, causing prices to fall, a fact rarely reported in the news. "This causes controversy during the first couple of days the tour goes on sale, especially for a super popular act." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8q2bRZyHnHE
**Dynamic Pricing Mechanism** : Dynamic pricing, similar to that used for hotel rooms and airline tickets, adjusts concert ticket prices up or down based on real-time demand. Algorithms aim to find the "fair market value" where artist popularity meets fan willingness to pay. Unlike scalping, the increased revenue from dynamic pricing directly benefits the artist, not a secondary seller. "This is where dynamic pricing comes into play. Just like hotel rooms and airline tickets and Uber rides, go up and down with demand." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8q2bRZyHnHE
**Dysania** : This is a condition describing the inability or extreme difficulty in getting out of bed in the morning. "Can't get out of bed in the morning. Well, you have a condition known as dysania." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Early 1990s Music Diversity** : The early 1990s were a period of significant musical diversity, characterized not only by the dominance of Grunge but also by a resurgence in punk rock, the emergence of Britpop, a spike in industrial music production, and a fresh approach to Goth. Additionally, many unique bands defied genre classification, often grouped under the "nebulous umbrella term" of "alternative." "The early 1990s were an awesome time for new music... The big thing of course was Grunge, but there was also a resurgence in punk rock. We got Britpop, there was a spike in the production of industrial music, along with a fresh approach to Goth." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=t2uXHP9cBdM
**Early 20th Century Context for Electricity** : In the early 20th century, electricity was still a relatively new concept, and electric household appliances were just beginning to gain traction. Even owning a radio was considered a novel and futuristic possession, highlighting the nascent stage of electrical integration into daily life. "Electric household appliances were just starting to catch on and even having a radio was still a novel thing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=E6cXyaHALBQ
**Early 90s Record Label "Gold Rush"** : The early 1990s saw a significant rush by record labels to sign bands that had an "aggressive sounding" style or simply "a whiff of alternative about them." This intense period of recruitment helped propel bands like L7 into the mainstream. "Because there was a gold rush to sign up aggressive sounding grins like bands around that time, L7 was swept away into the hands of producer Butch Vig." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Eo32mAZd8DI
**Early Applications of Amplification Technology** : The initial convergence of vacuum tubes, speakers, and widely available electricity led to the invention of radio. Subsequently, amplifiers capable of converting electrical energy back into sound enabled the development of public address (PA) systems and sound systems for movie theaters. "The first collision of these three inventions was radio, and then amplifiers that could turn any sound that had been converted into electrical energy back into sound. This translated into PA systems and sound systems for movie theaters." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=E6cXyaHALBQ
**Early Demonstration Recordings (1906)** : In 1906, demonstration recordings, such as "I am the Edison hologram," were utilized in stores by salespeople to introduce customers to the novel concept of recorded audio. These recordings aimed to showcase the entertainment capabilities of phonographs and records, highlighting their ability to provide melody, tales, laughter, and music for dancing or evoking memories. "Salespeople would play this in the store as a way of introducing customers to this new idea of recorded audio." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jD1dWxNLvfE
**Early Email and Internet Access (1980s)** : Before the public internet became widespread, email was already in use, with David Bowie engaging with it as early as the late 1980s. This early exposure informed his understanding of the internet's future potential. "He'd been going online since the late 1980s. That's when he first started using email and that's before the public Internet opened up." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM
**Early Fame and Documentation** : When individuals achieve a certain level of fame, "everything you do will be recorded somewhere" and becomes "out of your control." This perpetual documentation by fans, management, social media teams, and record labels means a famous person's life "becomes one ever-expanding Wikipedia page." "Fans are going to do it, your management team will do it, your social media people will make sure it gets done, probably somebody at your label, they'll just keep doing it and doing it and doing it." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_AY5lS-FmlU
**Early Influential Figures** : Beyond religious figures and scientists, music has its own highly influential figures such as Elvis, Chuck Berry, The Beatles, Dylan, Marley, Hendrix, Prince, and David Bowie, who profoundly shaped the evolution of life on Earth. "Elvis, Chuck Berry, The Beatles, Dylan, Marley, Hendrix, Prince, and David Bowie." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM
**Early Internet Music Sharing Challenges (Pre-1999)** : Initially, using the internet for music sharing was cumbersome due to slow uploading/downloading speeds and clunky, awful software. This made early digital music distribution awkward and inefficient for users. "It was awkward at first because uploading and downloading took forever and the software you had to use was clunky and awful." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Early On-Demand Music Acquisition** : For over a century, the primary method for individuals to listen to music on demand was through ownership, typically by purchasing physical media like a "piece of plastic" for a set price. This transaction represented both an emotional and financial investment, encouraging listeners to extract maximum enjoyment from their purchase. "for over a hundred years, the only way you could hear music on demand was to own it." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jD1dWxNLvfE
**Early Podcasting Attempt (2007)** : An attempt to launch podcasting for the show in 2007 did not gain traction. The prevailing concern at the time was that a podcast would "catapultize" or cannibalize the radio show's listenership, leading to its cancellation despite the potential for early adoption. "If we put out a podcast, well, that'll catapalize our radio. Yeah. So we're not going to do that. And we could have been doing this podcast in 2007, but there just wasn't a neat, it wasn't a market for it." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90
**Early Radio Show Production (Analog Era)** : The first 250 episodes of the show involved a labor-intensive analog production process. Voice tracks were recorded on quarter-inch tape, then manually edited with razor blades and grease pencils. Music was laid onto multi-track tape in real time, and the entire production was mixed down to two-track tape for real-time radio playback. "So that's how it was for first 250 shows until we moved out of Brampton and went digital. Yeah, and that will go. It was a lot of work." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90
**Early Radio Stations and Record Store Collaboration** : In the early days of radio, experimental stations like XWA in Montreal, one of the world's first, and KDKA in Pittsburgh, relied on local record stores for their programming. Engineers would obtain phonograph records from shops like Layton Brothers record store, which provided them for free in exchange for on-air announcements acknowledging their source. "When engineers got bored with speaking, they grabbed some phonograph records from the Layton Brothers record store down the street." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jD1dWxNLvfE
**Early Recorded Music Sales Venues (Late 1880s)** : When pre-recorded music, in the form of Edison cylinders and Berliner discs, was first introduced in the late 1880s, it was primarily sold in furniture stores. These establishments also sold phonographs and gramophones, which were initially regarded as pieces of fine furniture, making their sale alongside records a logical pairing. "When pre-recorded music was introduced in the late 1880s, these Edison cylinders and Berliner discs were sold at furniture stores, the same places that sold phonographs and gramophones, which made sense, given that these first units were looked upon as fine furniture." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jD1dWxNLvfE
**Early Sound Manipulation Techniques** : Before electronic instruments became widespread, musicians and engineers utilized various methods to alter the sounds of traditional instruments like guitars, bass, drums, and keyboards. These included effects pedals, studio tricks, and even "happy accidents" that occurred during the recording process, which provided plenty of creative possibilities for several decades. "There were plenty of ways to manipulate the sounds of those instruments, you know, effects, pedals, studio tricks, happy accidents that happened when you least expected them." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5PJRCC6EwUY
**Early Stereo System (Tiatrophone)** : The Tiatrophone system, demonstrated in 1881, featured a rudimentary form of stereo sound decades before it was officially "invented." It achieved this by placing 40 telephone transmitters on the left side of a stage and another 40 on the right, providing listeners with a spatialized audio experience in their homes. "And in stereo, too, this is like 70 years before stereo was invented because you had 40 transmitters put along the left side of the stage and another 40 along the right." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Early Telephone Exchange Design (George Koi)** : George Koi revolutionized telephone service by conceiving of a central exchange where all phones would connect, replacing the impractical system of direct wires between every two callers. He devised the idea for a specialized telephone operator to manually connect callers using short wires and durable, quick-connect plugs, ultimately leading to his invention of the quarter-inch funnel plug. "It was his idea that all phones be connected to a central exchange." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NAroxFbYkRw
**Earworm** : This term describes a phenomenon "when a clip of a song keeps running through your head over and over and over again on a loop and a drive you crazy." "Everybody's had one of those." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rfObVld9rIE
**Earworms – Involuntary Musical Imagery; Brain Fills in Silence; Best Cure Is a Sudoku** : When a song cuts out, the brain automatically continues it for a few seconds using stored musical memory. Sometimes a snippet catches in a loop — the neurological phenomenon known as an earworm. Almost 100% of the population experiences earworms. Key facts: they last longer and are more irritating for women; more than 75% of earworms involve lyrics; people with OCD are more susceptible; most loops are no longer than 30 seconds (the approximate buffer size of auditory cortex RAM). For some people, earworms are debilitating, persisting for months or years; only strong OCD medication helps. For most people, doing a sudoku puzzle appears to be an effective cure — the kind of brain processing required flushes the audio cache of the auditory cortex. "The best cure for an earworm seems to be to do a sudoku." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NMwMwqMQpf4
**Ease of Modern Music Creation** : The ease of music creation today is exemplified by software like Ableton Live and GarageBand (with its included "Beats and Stims"), songwriting methods such as "Top Lines and Beats," and the ability to purchase "ready-made beats online for a few bucks." Once created, a song can be uploaded to Spotify "for nothing" and made available globally. This contrasts with older methods that required mastering instruments and navigating a limited industry. "Others will point to the ease with which music can be created today." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Easy Eye Sound - Dan Auerbach's Nashville Studio** : Easy Eye Sound is Dan Auerbach's personal "butter zone studio" in Nashville, where The Black Keys recorded *El Camino* in a relaxed environment with functional gear. "Dan had butter zone studio by this time, a place called Easy Eye Sound". ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PmwfC4HR3_I

**Eco-Friendly Vinyl Initiatives** : Efforts are underway to develop more environmentally sustainable vinyl records. Some European pressing plants are achieving nearly 99% carbon neutrality in their manufacturing processes. Other companies are exploring the use of recycled vinyl, although historically (e.g., during the 1970s oil crisis), recycled vinyl was often impure. Experiments also include biodegradable PVC substitutes and even edible vinyl alternatives. "people are working on creating more eco-friendly vinyl records. There are a couple of pressing plants in Europe that approach being 99% carbon neutral in their manufacturing process." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B2g4QSREzpw
**Econoline Crush – A Ford Econoline Van Jammed Full of Band and Equipment** : Ford manufactured a van called the Econoline. Being crammed with your band and all your equipment into one of these vans — the classic touring band experience — was an Econoline Crush. "If you and your equipment is jammed into that van, it's an Econoline Crush." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Economic Impact on New Wave** : A severe economic downturn in the late 1970s and early 1980s, marked by the disco bubble bursting and a worldwide recession, inadvertently benefited New Wave. Record labels found it cheaper to produce and release New Wave records than those by larger mainstream acts, leading to increased investment in the genre. "Record labels found that it was cheaper to produce and release records by this new generation of new wave bands than it was to do the same with bigger mainstream acts." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bYsV3ozbk4M
**Economic Incentive for Albums (Post-1965)** : Record labels found albums significantly more attractive than singles due to "profit margins [that] were so much higher on albums." This economic incentive drove the industry's shift away from singles and into the album-dominated world that has largely persisted until the streaming era. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Ecumenical Tastes of Modern Youth** : Today's 15-year-olds have access to 120 million songs via streaming, encompassing the "entire library of recorded human musical history." This exposure leads to highly diverse and eclectic musical tastes, unlike previous generations who focused primarily on contemporary music. A Humber College student, for example, might listen to Drake, AC/DC, The Beatles, and Billie Holiday. "Your kid is absorbing far more music to influence him in his musical development than we ever did, because we were only focused on our largely on what was happening to us contemporaries, as contemporaries." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90
**Ed Sullivan Theater Marquee Performance** : Audioslave's debut performance on November 25, 2002, was unconventional, taking place on top of the marquee of the Ed Sullivan Theater as part of a *Late Show with David Letterman* appearance. "They played on top of the marquee on the Ed Sullivan theater as part of an appearance on the late show with David Letterman." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vLZla5h4xKQ
**Egalitarianism in Alt Rock** : The explosion of alternative music in the 1990s fostered a sense of egalitarianism, where previously fringe ideas and sounds were welcomed into the mainstream. Being "weird" was not only tolerated but encouraged, leading to the celebration and promotion of artists who challenged mainstream tastes with their strangeness. "From the earliest days, being weird was not only tolerated but encouraged. People who annoyed the mainstream with their strangeness were celebrated and promoted." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=h6snk0m4200
**Elders' Attitudes Towards Young People's Music (Late 19th/Early 20th Century)** : The negative attitudes of older generations towards the music of the young intensified in the late 19th and early 20th century. While church hymns and classical music were deemed acceptable ("uplifting and sophisticated"), folk songs were considered "vulgar," and show tunes were thought to be dangerously energetic. The emergence of jazz from New Orleans around 1900 was particularly condemned as "vile and evil," especially due to its association with African Americans. "These attitudes of elders towards music of the young only accelerated in the late 19th and early 20th century." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Electrical Audio Studio Ownership** : Electrical Audio, a recording studio located in Chicago, is owned by Steve Albini. This studio is notable for having recorded Nirvana's "In Utero" album, and later the Foo Fighters' "Something from Nothing." "That track was recorded at electrical audio in Chicago, the studio owned by Steve Elbeni, a guy who recorded Nirvana's in utero album." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Mh-qg1izM98
**Electronics and Future Music** : The increasing affordability and power of synthesizers and related electronics in the 1980s attracted tech-minded musicians uninterested in traditional instruments. This segment of the music world equated synthesizers with the "music of the future," which in turn connected to science fiction, a realm strongly associated with nerds. "First of all, tech-minded people into music who weren't interested in traditional instruments were attracted to the technology." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=h6snk0m4200

**Emergence of Modern Ticket Scalping (Mid-1800s)** : The contemporary form of ticket scalping emerged in the mid-1800s. "Sidewalk men" would acquire tickets for events and resell them at a premium to people waiting outside theaters. "But ticket scalping, as we know it today, first appeared in the mid 1800s." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D8GU8ZpSgY8
**Emergence of Music Licensing Industry** : Following the success of early music licensing deals in advertising, a new industry emerged dedicated solely to navigating the legal complexities of licensing real music from real artists for commercial use. These companies aimed to connect advertisers with meaningful, non-generic music to help sell goods and services. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Emil Berliner's Gramophone** : In the late 19th century, German inventor Emil Berliner conceptualized the gramophone, a device for storing music as microscopic bumps in a spiral groove on a flat, rotating platter. "Goes all the way back to the late 19th century to a German inventor named Emil Berliner." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IIJySSo276k
**Empowerment of Individual Music Fans** : With the advent of the internet, the traditional gatekeepers of music are gone, and power now lies with individual music fans. They are free to pursue any musical interests, acting as their own A&R persons, music directors, editors, and curators, and no longer need external sources to dictate what they listen to. "With the internet, the power lies with the individual music fan." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Enduring Desire for Physical Music** : A segment of the audience continues to desire physical music ownership. Bands and labels respond by issuing special editions and features, such as T-shirts or posters, that cannot be digitally downloaded, catering to collectors and those who value tangible media. "A portion of us will still want to own music in a physical form. Both bands and record labels will continue to issue special editions and feature stuff that you can't download." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Enduring Musical Influences** : New Wave's influences continue to be felt today, fragmenting into various subgenres like Electroclash, Cold Wave, Dark Wave, Synth Wave, and Chill Wave, as well as terms like Post Disco, New Pop, and New Wave. "New Wave's influences continue to be felt today." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9CNNsqXiL6U
**Enduring Popularity of 90s Music** : Music from the 1990s, particularly grunge and related acts, was so popular and good that audiences continued to demand it into the 21st century. Many acts from that era remained active and popular, while even defunct bands like Nirvana and Stone Temple Pilots maintained significant fanbases, making it challenging for new artists to break through due to the limited "oxygen" and airplay available. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Enduring Role of Albums in the Music Industry** : Despite the streaming-driven focus on singles, albums still serve as the primary "currency" of the recorded music industry. Contracts, awards, and sales in physical stores (CDs and vinyl LPs) are still based on albums, ensuring their short-term survival even as CD sales decline annually. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Enduring Success of Pre-2000 Artists** : Artists who achieved success before the year 2000, such as Pearl Jam, Red Hot Chili Peppers, Green Day, The Offspring, The Rolling Stones, Paul McCartney, and U2, often continue to thrive today, sustained by the career momentum built in the pre-internet era. "The acts that thrived pre-2000 are in many cases still thriving today." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Engineered Electronic Sound Revolution** : The ability for musicians to create previously unimagined sounds was born when engineers began to manipulate electricity in novel ways. This innovation led to an "explosion of new, amazing music" predominantly based on electronic sounds, with experimentation taking off in the 1960s. "But when engineers started messing with electricity in new ways, it became possible for musicians to create sounds that not only we'd never heard before, but never imagined hearing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5PJRCC6EwUY
**Enigma Veyron EV1D Speakers (Million-Dollar Audio)** : For audiophiles and those in the top 1% income bracket, there exists a set of speakers called the Enigma Veyron EV1D, produced by Karma. **Environmental Groups** : The Warped Tour also supported various environmental groups as part of its broad philanthropic outreach. "and various groups dealing with the environment." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7jfQaUV6Bq4
**Environmental Impact of Music Consumption (Physical vs. Streaming)** : Contrary to popular belief, physical music formats like vinyl records and CDs can be more environmentally friendly than streaming, depending on consumption patterns. Streaming and downloading music require energy for servers, routers, and playback devices. However, playing a downloaded song consumes significantly less energy than repeatedly streaming it. An estimated 80% reduction in carbon emissions from digital music consumption could be achieved if all streamed songs were downloaded instead. If an album is streamed 27 times, it becomes more ecologically sound to purchase a physical copy. "If you stream an album 27 times, it's actually better for the planet just to go ahead and buy a physical copy of it, be that a vinyl record or a CD." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B2g4QSREzpw
**Eric Stefani Left No Doubt to Animate The Simpsons** : Eric Stefani, brother of Gwen Stefani and keyboardist in No Doubt, quit the band before it really took off to become an animator for The Simpsons. He did contribute some parts to the Tragic Kingdom album before leaving. Separately, Tunde Adebimpe of TV on the Radio also worked as an animator for The Simpsons; David Bowie collected some of his artwork. "He quit before the band really took off." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fnZx8EGnszw
**Erosion of Cultural Gatekeepers by Streaming** : Prior to streaming, entities like record labels, radio stations, and print media acted as cultural gatekeepers, filtering music for quality and commercial viability, thus fostering a general consensus about popular music. Streaming, by offering access to millions of songs on demand, transformed individuals into their own gatekeepers, leading to a fragmented listening landscape where a broad consensus is rare beyond a few superstars. "For decades and decades and decades, music had to go through a series of cultural gatekeepers, record labels, record stores, radio stations, print media." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5Y6nHw5xx88
**Erosion of Royalty Income for Older Acts** : The past reliable system where acts could generate substantial, consistent royalty checks from decades-old album sales (e.g., The Doors going platinum annually, Beastie Boys selling 2 million *Licensed to Ill* annually, Eagles/Fleetwood Mac retiring on royalties) has ceased. These "retirement annuities" have shrunk, forcing even established acts to tour to maintain their lifestyle and cash flow. "That's not happening anymore. These royalty checks, which were like retirement annuities, have shrunk and shrunk and shrunk." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Ethical Refusals in Licensing Deals** : Some artists maintain strong ethical boundaries, choosing to refuse licensing offers for certain types of products or campaigns. Examples include products promoting meat, anything related to the military, or beer companies, reflecting personal or moral objections. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Etymology of "Nerd"** : The word "nerd" first appeared in a 1500s book titled "a true discourse of the assault committed upon the most noble prince Prince William of Orange, County of NASA, Marquess de la Verre and C," written by John Jarkuy Speniel. It fell out of use around 1725 before being revived by Dr. Seuss in 1950 to describe a peculiar creature. "According to these nerds, nerd, the word, shows up for the first time in a book called a true discourse of the assault committed upon the most noble prince Prince William of Orange, County of NASA, Marquess de la Verre and C, written by John Jarkuy Speniel." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=h6snk0m4200
**Evolution of Album Artwork Industry** : The success of the first album cover artwork by Alex Steinweiss led to the creation of an entirely new industry, with design studios worldwide dedicated to creating album art. This profession faced challenges as album formats shrunk from 12x12 inch vinyl to smaller CD covers (6x6 or 5x5 inches) and then to digital files and streaming, though the resurgence of vinyl has revitalized interest in the art form. "A whole new industry was created." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_tbKuJR0cPs
**Evolution of Album Artwork Presentation** : The glory of album artwork faced decline with the advent of digital formats. Initially, it was shrunk to CD size, then reduced to a postage stamp-sized image on platforms like iTunes, and became almost non-existent with streaming services. In pre-digital and pre-CD days, artwork was crucial for the listening experience, mystery, mystique, and marketing of music, sometimes even prompting purchases solely based on a cool-looking cover. Album artwork was once highly revered, inspiring coffee table book collections like *The 100 Best Album Covers* and *The Album Cover Album*, which treated rock and pop album covers with respect and offered insights into both the musical artists and the artists who created the artwork. "For a while, we were in real danger of seeing the glories of album artwork disappear." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sn5TWBFd0XM
**Evolution of Bass Instrument Role** : The evolution of the bass instrument from tubas to double basses, and finally to the electric bass like the Fender Precision, marked a significant shift in music. The electric bass offered solutions to volume, portability, and playability that its predecessors could not, quickly becoming the new standard. "Throughout the 1950s, the big double bass disappeared, and it was replaced with a relatively tiny Fender Precision, which was easier to transport, play, amplify, and modify." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Y0HW8LQKvJw
**Evolution of Musical Sensibilities by Fuzz (1960s)** : The advent of the fuzz pedal in the 1960s triggered a significant shift in musical tastes and sensibilities. Sounds that, a mere decade earlier, might have been dismissed as "painful noise" began to be perceived as desirable and good. This unexpected evolution in taste fundamentally changed what was considered acceptable and appealing in music, leading to new sonic possibilities. "Ten years earlier we might have dismissed this new sound as painful noise. But thanks to the fuzz pedal, our taste began to evolve in a completely unexpected direction." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PNiL63fY1Y8
**Evolution of Sitcom Storytelling (Pre-Seinfeld vs. Seinfeld)** : Before Seinfeld, most sitcoms typically followed an A story and a B story, with a "runner" joke loosely continuing throughout the episode without much more narrative integration. Seinfeld, however, revolutionized this by having each character pursue their own storyline, which then converged in the final moments to create a joke "larger than its parts." "Before Seinfeld, most sitcoms broke down into an A story and a B story, and the surrounding material could take the form of a so-called runner, a joke that continued throughout the episode and told a very loose story but didn't do much more than that." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6O5TCTO-go4
**Evolution of Songwriting for Streaming** : To counter high skip rates and ensure artists get paid, modern songwriting has evolved to prioritize holding listener attention within the crucial first 30 seconds, leading to shorter intros, front-loaded choruses, and an abundance of immediate hooks. "It's become the goal of artists and composers and producers to write songs that will hold our attention for that important first thirty seconds." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Evolutionary Purpose of Music - Collective Voice** : Early humans used music as a collective voice to bring individuals together during times of celebration, sadness, rituals, and war. This function helped foster community and cohesion within early human tribes. "It brought individuals together in time of celebration and sadness for rituals and for war." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**Evolutionary Purpose of Music - Mating** : Charles Darwin theorized that human appreciation for music might be linked to the mating calls of birds and other animals, suggesting that the brain's music centers are connected to the species' need for reproduction. This theory aligns with the observation that nearly 90% of all songs ever written are related to love or sex. "He thought human appreciation of music might somehow be related to the mating calls of birds and other creatures." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**Evolutionary Purpose of Music - Preserving Stories** : Before written language existed, music was crucial for preserving ancient stories, myths, folk tales, and histories across thousands of generations. Setting important cultural information to music allowed it to be stored and passed down, aiding the survival of cultures from early human migrations out of Africa through ancient Roman and Greek civilizations. "It's now thought that myths and folk tales and histories managed to survive for so many years because they were stored and passed down as songs." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**Evolutionary Purpose of Music - Raising Young** : Another theory suggests music evolved from the need to raise young, specifically through lullabies. Anthropologists have found no societies that do not use lullabies to calm babies, which serves as a survival mechanism by preventing crying that could alert predators to vulnerable infants. "Anthropologists have yet to find any societies that don't use lullabies to calm babies and to stop them from crying." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**Evolving Landscape of Corporate Endorsements in Music** : Initially, bands like 5440 maintained a strict anti-commercial stance, rejecting offers from cigarette companies and insisting on contractual control over stage branding. However, by the late 1990s, the battle was lost as major corporations (Molson, Bud, Labatt's, Coca-Cola) began directly sponsoring venues and promoters, making it impossible for bands to perform without their branding present, thus removing artists' choice. "the Moulson and the cigarette companies went directly to the venues, went directly to the promoters where if you wanted to play at all, you had to see Moulson or Bud or LaBaz or, you know, players light or whatever it was, or Coke, you didn't have a choice anymore." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=W9gdKha0PLg
**Exceptions to the Seven-Year Band Lifespan** : While many bands follow a seven-year cycle from formation to breakup, several notable groups have defied this trend, surviving multiple such periods. These exceptions include U2, The Rolling Stones, Oasis, Green Day, and Foo Fighters, demonstrating remarkable longevity. "Groups that have survived multiple seven-year cycles." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q-QP7ePxkQE
**Exclusive Ticketing Inventory Deals** : Ticketmaster secured exclusive deals with venues where it was granted the entire inventory of tickets for a given show, rather than sharing it with multiple sellers. This system benefited fans by providing a single point of purchase and venues by ensuring consistent business relationships over several years, similar to exclusive concession deals for beverages. "Instead of sharing the inventory of tickets with multiple ticket sellers, Ticketmaster signed deals where they were given the entire inventory for a given show." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8q2bRZyHnHE
**Exploitation of Nostalgia by the Music Industry** : Marketers, the music industry, and concert promoters actively leverage the powerful force of nostalgia. This explains why "legacy bands" (acts popular before 2000) continue to "fill arenas," with Gen Xers and increasing numbers of Gen Y fans willing to pay significant amounts to "relive their youth" by seeing bands they connected with as teenagers. "Nostalgia can be a very, very powerful thing. Marketers know this. The music industry knows this. And promoters know this." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Extended Mixes on 80s Radio** : In the 1980s, radio announcers had significant leeway in choosing music, often preferring extended mixes over album or single mixes. These longer versions were perceived as artistically superior and also provided announcers more time to manage station operations like filing records or answering request lines. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Extensive Early Record Dealer Network (1906)** : By 1906, the United States boasted an extensive network of 25,000 record dealers, most of which were furniture stores. This widespread distribution system was established and supported by the major record companies of the era, Victor and Edison. "In 1906, there were 25,000 record dealers just in the United States." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jD1dWxNLvfE
**F**ked Up – Deliberately Offensive Name for a Band Planned to Last 10 Shows** : The group was deliberately formed with members expected not to get along, intending to play 10 shows and break up — hence the name. **FACTOR and Video FACT – Funding Bodies Born from CanCon (1982 and 1984)** : The Foundation to Assist Canadian Talent on Records (FACTOR) was introduced in 1982, requiring radio stations to contribute funds distributed to artists passing industry juries. The money can be used for recording, touring, and general artist development. When foreign artists learn that Canadian artists have access to such a fund, the common reaction is shock and envy. In 1984, MuchMusic launched as Canada's music video channel, and Video FACT was established to fund Canadian music video production. "When foreign artists find out that Canadian artists have access to such a fund, they just can't believe it." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-JWO_jYXwEM
**FBI Investigation into "Louie Louie" Lyrics** : The unintelligible lyrics of The Kingsmen's song "Louie Louie" were rumored to be pornographic, prompting a six-month sound analysis test by the FBI. However, the investigation failed to prove the alleged pornographic content. "The completely unintelligible lyrics were rumored to be pornographic, but not even a six-month sound analysis test by the FBI could prove that." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6oUkMOkEr9U

**FM Radio Broadcasts as Bootleg Sources (1970s–1990s)** : For several decades, FM radio broadcasts of concerts served as a major source of bootleg material. These broadcasts sometimes compelled record labels to issue official releases — as occurred with Elton John in 1970 and David Bowie in 1972 — to preempt the unauthorized recordings. "Radio broadcasts of concerts were an important source of bootlegs, sometimes forcing labels to release official versions (e.g. Elton John 1970, David Bowie 1972)." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OrHtPVBjXw4
**FM Radio Invention and Edwin Armstrong's Tragic End** : Edwin Howard Armstrong, one of the engineers who put KDKA on air, discovered Frequency Modulation (FM) while working for RCA. After more than a decade developing the mathematics and science, the first FM broadcast was made on June 9, 1934, at exactly 10:23am from the top of the Empire State Building — an organ recital that sounded remarkable compared to AM. However, RCA suppressed FM to protect their lucrative AM radio business and patent portfolio, spending years tying Armstrong up in courts. On February 1, 1954, broken and depressed after decades of legal battles, Armstrong dressed in his best suit, put on his hat and gloves, and jumped from his 13th floor apartment window. "On February 1, 1954, broken and depressed, Howard dressed in his best suit and overcoat, put on his hat and gloves and jumped from his 13th floor window." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JvOEAzmC6l0
**FM Radio Invention and Tragic Outcome (1933)** : FM radio was invented by Edward Howard Armstrong in 1933. Despite this groundbreaking innovation, his patents were challenged by the RCA Corporation in an unfounded legal dispute. Armstrong ultimately lost control of his invention, which left him penniless and deeply distressed, leading him to tragically end his life by jumping from his 13th-floor window. "FM radio was invented by a dude named Edward Howard Armstrong back in 1933." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PNiL63fY1Y8
**FM Surpassed AM in 1978 – AM Kept Alive by Talk Radio; Canada Had Unique Diversity Rules** : AM radio dominated broadcasting from its invention in the 1920s all the way to 1978, when FM listening finally exceeded AM in the United States for the first time. AM survived primarily through right-wing talk radio and sports radio. In Canada, unique regulations protected AM by legally prohibiting FM stations from replicating AM programming formats: no more than 49% of songs could be hits (top 40 songs), no song could be played more than 18 times per week, and stations were required to run programming spanning multiple genres by law. FM stations also faced extensive spoken word quotas. These rules were dropped in the 1990s but left a lasting imprint on how Canadian radio sounds compared to its American counterpart. "In Canada, AM stations playing music continued to be very successful well into the 80s." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iyGUXdDqIlI
**FUMS (Fuck U MS)** : FUMS is a charity initiative created by Billy Talent, their management, and record label to raise money for Multiple Sclerosis research, demonstrating the music community's support for those affected by the disease. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ocMHRLQMQY0

**Fan Abandonment of Popular Artists** : A common phenomenon where a segment of early fans will "blow off" a band or artist once they achieve widespread popularity, often perceiving this success as a "personal betrayal" because the artist is no longer their "little secret treasure." This behavior, termed "the opposite of bandwagonism," occurs despite most musicians' desire for their art to reach a broad audience and regardless of whether the band continues to produce quality music. "Fans who abandoned a group just because they become popular and then blame the band as if this was some kind of personal betrayal." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7Zniri9uSlc

"At the same time, there was growing dissatisfaction by music fans about the price and selection of music, especially amongst college students." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Fan Entitlement vs. Market Reality** : There's a common misconception among fans that they "deserve" to buy front-row seats at a low, fixed price, rather than accepting that concert tickets, like other high-demand goods or services, are subject to market forces and supply-and-demand pricing. "You do not deserve To buy a front row seat for 50 bucks just like you can't get a first class airline ticket to Singapore for a hundred bucks You pay the going rate." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8q2bRZyHnHE

**Fatal Learjet Crash (2008)** : On September 19, 2008, less than a month after Jerry Finn's death, a chartered Learjet 60 carrying Travis Barker and DJ AM (among others) crashed in Columbia, South Carolina. The crash was caused by underinflated tires that burst during takeoff, leading to the collapse of the landing gear. The plane veered off the runway, erupted in sparks, crashed through barriers, and exploded about 60 seconds after Travis and DJ AM managed to escape. Pilots James Bland and Sarah Lemon, along with two other passengers, perished, leaving Travis and DJ AM as the sole survivors. "The tires, which had been underinflated, had burst." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q-QP7ePxkQE

**Feedback Definition** : Feedback occurs when a signal is routed back into its own original input within a circuit. In its uncontrolled form, this manifests as sharp, high-pitched squeals and shrieks from PA systems and amplifiers. However, feedback can also be intentionally harnessed and controlled to produce a distinct type of distortion, creating a musical landscape. "Feedback. This is when you take a signal and run it back into the original input of a circuit." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iGav9uJwA_w

**Fetal Hearing Development and Loud Music Exposure** : A baby's ear structure is fully developed by 24 weeks of a normal pregnancy. While the amniotic sac and mother's body muffle sounds in quiet environments, prolonged exposure to high volume levels from sources like rock concerts, band practices, loud recording sessions near drums or amps, or loud car stereos can potentially damage a baby's hearing development. It is advised to avoid such environments until delivery. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BHN6db7m3DM

**Finite Number of Musical Combinations** : Despite the initial impression of infinite possibilities, the number of ways notes can be used is "very, very big but definitely finite." For playing each note once, it's "around 479 billion, 1,600." When considering different note durations (whole, half, quarter, etc.), the number exceeds "one quintillion possible combinations," which would take "33 billion, 63 million, 236 thousand, 360 years" to play if a new combination was played every second, more than five times the age of the universe. "The numbers are very, very big but definitely finite. Somewhere around 479 billion, 1,600." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rfObVld9rIE
**First All-Christmas Radio Format Flip** : A radio station in Ohio became the first in North America to switch to an all-Christmas music format for the year, making the change on September 25th at precisely 12:25 PM. The time was chosen as a playful reference to Christmas. "The radio station in Ohio was the first station in North America to flip to an all Christmas format this year. They made the flip on September 25th and at exactly 12 25 pm. 12 25." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HoBx6s3JmVQ
