**Magnetic Tape Technology – Developed by Nazis, Adopted by US via Jack Mullin and Ampex** : Magnetic tape recording technology was developed in Nazi Germany and later brought to the United States by Jack Mullin, who worked with Ampex to commercialize it. This technology fundamentally transformed the capacity to record and manipulate audio and made unofficial recordings far easier to produce. "Developed by the Nazis and later adopted in the US by Jack Mullin and Ampex." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OrHtPVBjXw4
**Mainstream Acceptance and Normalization** : Tattoos have become so mainstream that in some social circles, the absence of tattoos can make one an "outsider" or "weirdo." This shift occurred notably in the early 2000s, around 2001-2002, when tattoo shops became widely accessible and common, akin to Starbucks. "In fact, in some circles, if you don't have any ink, you're the outsider in Weirdo." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jZeMmPekKMQ
**Mainstream Music Becoming a Niche (Post-2000)** : The concept of mainstream music, once a pervasive cultural force where "everyone generally listened to the same thing" and "big stars were absolutely ubiquitous," has diminished significantly since 2000 with the rise of the internet. Previously, a limited number of gatekeepers—record labels, record stores, radio, TV video channels, and music magazines—filtered music, creating a "mono culture" and a common music vocabulary. With the internet, consumers gained "free and unfettered access" to vast amounts of music, leading to the collapse of traditional gatekeeper business models (e.g., declining physical sales, music magazine revenue). Music culture fragmented into "disconnected or barely connected, self-organizing music communities," making mainstream appeal just "another of many musical avenues and genres" without special status. "A common mainstream music culture we had before 2000 is gone." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xid8CZf4oYo
**Major Bands Burned by Unauthorized Leaks** : Numerous prominent bands, including Korn, U2, Snow Patrol, Metallica, Linkin Park, and Radiohead, have experienced significant frustration and financial loss due to their albums being leaked online weeks or even months before their official release dates. "Corn, U2, Snow Patrol, Metallica, Lincoln Park, and of course, Radiohead." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vt6DVj7S6nk
**Major Label Historical Role** : Historically, major labels, numbering six or seven at one point, "scooped up all the best stuff" and could afford to take chances on artists. This often left indie labels with "the drags" or music considered unsellable, creating a perceived imbalance in quality. "There was a time when the major labels back when there were six or seven of them scooped up all the best stuff and they could afford to take those kinds of chances back then. The indie labels were for the most part left with the drags or the stuff that could not be sold." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sCtQqVBtCaI
**Major Labels' Failed Digital Initiatives** : In response to the Napster crisis and widespread piracy by 2000, major record labels, initially dismissive of MP3s, found themselves technologically unprepared (most executives lacked computers). Their attempts to create their own online stores failed due to conflicting loyalties with retail partners, consumer demand for one-stop shops stocking all labels, and antitrust laws preventing a unified store (especially given past CD price-fixing scrutiny). This led to two disastrous ventures: "Press Play" (Universal/Sony), which lasted two years until March 2003, and "MusicNet" (BMG/EMI/Warner), which was sold off by 2005. Both services were criticized for being difficult to use, restrictive, and laden with complicated digital rights management (DRM). "Well, a couple of problems with that. First, the record labels had to think about their retail partners, the thousands of stores that for decades had sold their product." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nX8uAFDzDYM
**Major Labels' Financial Crisis and Reputation Decline** : The rise of file sharing and the decline in CD sales led to a financial crisis for major record labels, causing their market share to fall and the industry to shrink. This decline was perceived by many fans as "karma" for years of overpricing CDs, offering one-sided record deals that disadvantaged artists, and exhibiting an overall contempt for both artists and fans. "While the majors were being battered by file sharing and falling market share, the Indies were just bobbin and weave and do whatever they had to do to survive." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=raRCZ0Y5up8
**Major Shift in Music Industry (Present)** : The current era represents an unprecedented, once-in-a-lifetime transformation in how music is created and consumed, constituting a new reality for the industry. "We are seeing a once in a lifetime major shift in music creation and consumption." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Malcolm Gladwell's 10,000-Hour Rule** : Hugh Dillon invoked Malcolm Gladwell's concept of 10,000 hours of dedicated practice to achieve mastery, applying it to his own intensive immersion in music through obsessive record collecting and listening. This dedication fostered a deep, almost innate knowledge of rock and roll that aids his songwriting. "I am of the Malcolm Gladwell 10,000 hours because I grew up just obsessively listening to records." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=y7kmkWJ54ww

**Manipulating Musical Taste** : Researchers at McGill University in Montreal made a discovery that musical taste can be manipulated within minutes using a technique called transcranial magnetic stimulation (a "magnetic zap") to the front of the brain. This method could either increase or decrease the amount of enjoyment individuals derived from music, a process believed to involve the regulation of dopamine within the brain, though the precise mechanism is not yet fully understood. "musical taste can be manipulated in minutes just by a little magnetic zap to the front of the brain." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ

**Marfan Syndrome** : This is an inherited disorder, linked to chromosome 15, that affects the body's connective tissue. Individuals with Marfan Syndrome tend to be tall and thin, with unusually long arms, legs, and fingers. It can lead to serious heart problems, and if left undiagnosed and untreated, the average lifespan is typically 32 years. Joey Ramone was afflicted with this condition. "Young Jeffrey grew up with all sorts of health problems. He was tall and gauky as the result of something called Marfan Syndrome, which is an inherited disorder living on chromosome 15 that messes with connective tissue." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=j8uk7BnbXwU

**Mass Extinction of Big Chain Record Stores** : Starting around 2000, the recorded music industry experienced a "mass extinction event" with the widespread closure of big chain record stores globally. This was driven by the public's shift from physical media to online music access. Major chains like Tower Records (closed all but 1-2 Japan stores by 2006), the Musicland Group (including Suncoast and Sam Goody, bankrupt in 2006), Sam The Record Man (defunct by 2007 except one store), and Virgin Megastores (gone by 2009) disappeared. Record sections also vanished from Best Buy and department stores. The only "bright spots" were HMV's resurrection by Canadian entrepreneur Doug Putnam (who also bought Sunrise Records) and Rough Trade Records maintaining several locations. Most physical record retailing now belongs to independent stores. "This really was a mass extinction event as people moved away from physical media over to online access for music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZzIqIydZTlA

**Mechanical Recording Limitations (Pre-Mid-1920s)** : Before the mid-1920s, sound recording was a purely mechanical process. It involved musicians and singers performing around a large, horn-shaped sound collector that funneled sound to a needle. This needle vibrated and cut a groove into a rotating disc made of soft material, which served as the master. This method produced awful sound quality, offered no editing, overdubs, or special effects, and required restarting from scratch if any mistake occurred. "Up until the mid-1920s, recording sound was a very mechanical process." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PNiL63fY1Y8
**Medical Research on Infant Rhythm Development** : Medical research suggests that bouncing a baby on one's knee or against the chest while music plays can instill a sense of rhythm. "medical research says you should bounce the baby on your knee or against your chest while music plays. **Mid-90s Economic and Political Context** : The mid-1990s were marked by an improved world economy following a "brutal recession" and the presence of a "Democrat in the White House." This period fostered a mood for lighter, more uplifting music, with pop punk serving as a therapeutic "antidote" to the gloom of grunge and the earlier recession. "After a brutal recession earlier in the decade, the world economy began to improve, and people's moods began to improve. While they weren't prepared to leave all their angst behind, they did want to lighten up a little bit." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pE7TaWSUa-o
**Mid-Age Crises and the "Death of Coolness Spiral" (Ages 42-44)** : Around age 42, many individuals experience an "existential mid-age crisis" regarding music, attempting for 12-18 months to reconnect with the music world and recapture the "emotional glory of music discovery" from two decades prior. However, by age 44, most revert to "comfort food music" from their youth, concluding that "this new stuff sucks." This phenomenon is referred to as the "death of coolness spiral," which can be graphically plotted as a line spiraling outwards from the center, showing taste deviating from current music with age. "Around the age of 42, many of us enter existential mid-age crises when it comes to music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Mighty Mighty Bosstones – Bartender Suggested Adding "Mighty" to Solve a Name Conflict** : There was already a local a cappella group called the Mighty Bosstones. **Millennials Fueling Piracy and Indie Discovery** : Millennials, being the most internet-savvy generation, were adept at finding music online. Many were too young to have credit cards or sufficient funds to purchase many CDs, which fueled the piracy boom. Through this, they uncovered and shared a vast amount of music not released by mainstream or major labels, contributing significantly to the indie revolution. "At the same time, many were too young to have credit cards or enough money to buy as many CD's as they wanted. **Misconception of Direct Artist Payment** : There is a common assumption among users that subscription fees directly pay the specific artists whose songs they stream, but this is not how streaming payment systems are structured. "If you stream a song from an artist, you would expect that your subscription money goes to paying that artist. You know, you're listening to their song, so they should get paid with your money. Not necessarily." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Misconceptions About Streaming Music Payouts** : Complaints that streaming music companies (e.g., Spotify, RDO, Slack, DZR) "are ripping off artists by paying out so little money" are often misplaced. These payouts are not arbitrary but are "negotiated with a bunch of people in the middle," including record labels, music publishers, and copyright boards. A music stream is a one-time listen, comparable to radio play (where artists receive a fraction of a cent per play), distinct from purchasing a download. Streaming services pay "billions in fees," representing "70% of what they bring in," but the opaque process by which these fees are distributed to artists by intermediaries is the core issue, as no standalone streaming service is currently profitable. "These payouts are not the doing of the streamers." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7Zniri9uSlc
**Misconceptions of Goth Culture** : Goth culture is often wrongly associated with a "fascination with death" and a desire to "embrace death and wish death upon others," especially when linked to violent incidents in the media. "Hey, these people are fascinated with death. They must embrace death and wish death upon others." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=evlGhfUe6QQ
**Modern Music Piracy and Its Consequences** : Modern music piracy, which began in the early 1990s and became rampant by 2000, was fueled by consumer frustration over high CD prices, the phasing out of CD singles, and albums often containing only a few good songs. The music industry's attempts to sue fans for stealing music exacerbated the problem. This resulted in a catastrophic decline in sales, with 2.5 billion CDs sold globally in 2000 crashing by over 75% in the subsequent decade. The impact included massive revenue losses, job cuts, artists being dropped from rosters, and the destruction of relationships between labels and record stores. The industry, paralyzed by its lack of technological understanding and hindered by antitrust laws (after being scrutinized for CD price-fixing), struggled to adapt until Steve Jobs' iTunes offered a new path. "Modern music piracy began in the early 1990s. And by the time we reached January 1st 2000, it's starting to really get out of control." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nX8uAFDzDYM
**Modern Radio Show Production (Digital Era)** : The production process has dramatically evolved with digital technology. The speaker records voice tracks into Pro Tools at his home studio, uploads them to Dropbox, and a producer edits them on a laptop (even on planes). Music is supplied from extensive hard drives. While the radio version airs on Saturday or Sunday, the podcast version is "telescoped down" to 15-second music clips due to complex copyright and rights management issues that prevent playing full songs. "Now I have a studio at home. I have Pro Tools. I record my voice track into Pro Tools. I uploaded to Dropbox, Rob Downs, and look down loads it. Edit it while watching TV on a laptop." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90
**Modern Streaming Music (Present)** : Current streaming platforms provide access to a digital music library of at least 90 million songs, with new additions daily, allowing users to access virtually any recorded song instantly from any device, often at negligible cost or even for free, thus realizing the "theoretical Celestial Jukebox." "Today, of course, we have streaming. All the platforms draw from a digital music library that contains at least 90 million songs and more are being added every day." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Modern Usage of "Nerd"** : In 1951, Newsweek magazine reported that the term "nerd" was used in Detroit to describe an "awkward sort of dude who really wasn't very cool." The word gained significant popularity in 1974 with the TV series "Happy Days," where Fonzie often called Richie and Potsy "nerds." By the late 1970s, coinciding with the rise of personal computers, consumer technology, and science fiction, its use became widespread, evolving into a compliment in modern technological society, with figures like Bill Gates, Elon Musk, and Mark Zuckerberg celebrated as "nerds." "But the following year, Newsweek magazine reported that nerd was being used in Detroit to describe an awkward sort of dude who really wasn't very cool." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=h6snk0m4200
**Modest Mouse – Passage from Virginia Woolf's Story "The Mark on the Wall"** : The name comes from a line in Virginia Woolf's short story "The Mark on the Wall": "and very frequent in the minds of modest, mouse-colored people." "It's a passage in a story called the mark on the wall by Virginia Woolf." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Monaco's Symphony Orchestra Larger Than Its Army** : In the principality of Monaco, located on the Mediterranean coast, an unusual demographic fact exists: there are more individuals who are members of its symphony orchestra than there are personnel in its army. "If we go to the principality of Monaco on the Mediterranean coast, you'll find that there are more people in its symphony orchestra than in its army." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GO0K_N7Ys7I
**Mondegreen** : This term refers to a "misheard lyric," with Jimi Hendrix's "Purple Haze" ("excuse me while I kiss the sky" often heard as "excuse me while I kiss this guy") provided as a "great example." "That's a misheard lyric and a great example is in Jimmy Hendrix's purple haze." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rfObVld9rIE
**Mondegreens: Definition** : Misheard lyrics or lines of poetry are known as Mondegreens. These errors result in the line acquiring a completely new and unintended meaning, which can persist in a listener's mind. "Misheard lyrics are known as Mondegreens." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Mondegreens: Global Spread** : With the rise of mass media in the 20th century, the phenomenon of Mondegreens spread widely, becoming common across various languages and cultures worldwide. "With the emergence of mass media in the 20th century, Mondegrees be in spread and now they're common worldwide and in every language you want to mention." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Mondegreens: Origin (1954)** : The term "Mondegreen" was coined in 1954 by American writer Sylvia Wright, who published an article in Harper's magazine. Wright had misheard a line from the 1765 Scottish ballad "in the Bonnie Earl Morey." She heard "Lady Montagreen" instead of "laid him on the green," and proposed that all such misheard lines be called Mondegreens. "The word goes back to 1954 when an American writer named Sylvia Wright wrote in Harper's magazine that she messed up with an old Scottish ballot entitled in the Bonnie Earl Morey, which dates back to at least 1765." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Mondegreens: Psychological Basis** : Mondegreens arise from a psychological response called confirmation bias. When phrases are heard indistinctly, the brain instinctively attempts to fill gaps with familiar sounds, often leading to cognitive dissonance. The incorrect words become ingrained, making it difficult to hear the correct lyrics, as people may subconsciously prefer their misheard version. "If we hear a phrase indistinctly, our brains automatically, instinctively, tried filling the gaps with something familiar." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**More Band Name Origins – 60 Additional Examples (Bandminology)** : A second installment of band name origins. "Bandminology" — coined by the podcast in consultation with linguistics academics and branding experts — is proposed as the term for the study of how musical groups choose their names. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Morné Harmse School Attack (2008)** : On August 17, 2008, 18-year-old Morné Harmse carried out a samurai sword attack at Nick Dietrich's Technical School in Kruger's Drop, South Africa, killing one 16-year-old and injuring three others. He initially blamed Satanism but then claimed Slipknot made him "lose control of his body," wearing a mask resembling Slipknot members and referring to it as his "maggot mask." "On August 17th, 2008, there was a horrific incident at Nick Dietrich's Technical School in Kruger's Drop, South Africa." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FtGJHhqXcDI

**Movie Inspiration: Christian F.** : The movie "Christian F." is a film set in the underground punk rock scene of Berlin, with David Bowie contributing to its soundtrack. A scene from this movie, where the lead female character gives herself a stick-and-poke tattoo, directly inspired Dave Grohl to attempt his first tattoo at age 12 or 13. "I watched this movie that was a movie that took place in Berlin in the Underground punk rock scene. It was a movie called Christian F. Yes, I remember that. It was a great movie. "In the 90s, one popular way to break a new act would be to include one of their songs on the soundtrack of a movie that appealed to Jen Exers." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZcF5JMhBj2M
**Multiple Sclerosis (MS) in Canada and UK** : Canada has one of the highest, if not the highest, rates of Multiple Sclerosis in the world, with the UK also experiencing a high incidence. **Multitrack Recording Origins (Nazi Magnetophone)** : The ability to multitrack, overdub, edit, mix, and remix audio today originates from magnetic tape technology, specifically the German Magnetophone machines discovered by Jack Mullen after WWII. This technology, commercialized by Bing Crosby and Ampex, allowed sound to be recorded on tape, then cut, edited, and layered, fundamentally transforming recording capabilities and the modern music industry. "This all led to the modern recording industry and all the music that we listened to today." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NAroxFbYkRw
**Mumford & Sons – Marcus Mumford Wanted to Evoke a Family Business** : Lead singer Marcus Mumford liked the idea of a band name that evoked an old family business. "He'd like the idea of a band evoking an old family business." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Murl Travis and Paul Bigsby's Influence** : Leo Fender met country picker Murl Travis, who owned a solid-body guitar custom-built by motorcycle parts designer Paul Bigsby. This design served as a direct inspiration for Leo Fender's own solid-body guitar prototypes, such as the Esquire. "This is when he met a country picker named Murl Travis, who had a solid-body guitar built for him by a motorcycle parts designer named Paul Bigsby. That design inspired Leo." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=E6cXyaHALBQ
**Muscle Shoals Sound Studio - Legendary Studio** : Muscle Shoals Sound Studio in Alabama is a renowned historical recording location where legendary artists like The Rolling Stones, Lynyrd Skynyrd, Bob Dylan, and Bob Seger recorded. The Black Keys later used it for their *Brothers* album, valuing its acoustics despite technical challenges. "A bunch of it was made at the famous Muscle Shoal Sound Studio in Alabama, a place used by the Rolling Stones, and Leonard Skinner, Bob Dylan, and Bob Seeger." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PmwfC4HR3_I
**Muscle Shoals Sound Studio Electrical Issues (2010)** : During the recording of *Brothers* in 2010, The Black Keys encountered significant technical problems at the legendary Muscle Shoals Sound Studio in Alabama. The studio's in-house equipment was unusable due to 30 years of disuse, and newly brought-in digital gear was subsequently fried by stray voltage entering the building from ongoing electrical line work on the streets. "But then work on the electrical lines on the streets and all kinds of stray voltage into the building, frying most of the modern stuff." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ooNAHswiT5Q
**MusiCares** : The Warped Tour raised hundreds of thousands of dollars for MusiCares, an organization dedicated to helping musicians and roadies obtain new health insurance. **Music Appreciation While High (Cannabis)** : The perception that music sounds better when under the influence of cannabis is not an illusion. Cannabis activates CB1 receptors in the brain, causing them to become hyperactive, which in turn enhances activity in the metalymbic dopamine system when music is present. This leads to increased dopamine secretion for every note heard, intensifying the "feel-good" sensation. Additionally, cannabis interferes with short-term memory, fostering a heightened focus on the present moment and suppressing the brain's natural tendency to anticipate what comes next, allowing listeners to perceive previously unnoticed details in both complex and simple arrangements. "Music plus cannabis enhances activity in the metalymbic dopamine system. That means for every note of music we hear, we get extra dopamine secretion caused by cannabis." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Music Can Assist Brain Surgery – Patients Play Their Instrument While Surgeons Operate** : For certain neurological procedures, patients are awoken from anesthetic and asked to play a musical instrument while surgeons work inside the skull. If the surgeons disturb an area affecting the patient's playing, they know to find a different route. A notable example: Brad Carter, whose Parkinson's disease tremors had left him unable to play guitar, had deep brain stimulation electrodes installed while fully awake and playing guitar, singing, with his skull screwed into a stabilizing frame. The surgery restored his ability to play. "Music can assist with brain surgery." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NMwMwqMQpf4
**Music Creation and Consumption Boom (2000s)** : Despite a challenging business environment in the latter half of the 2000s, more people than ever before were making, distributing, and consuming music. This surge was enabled by new technologies and the bypassing of traditional gatekeepers like record labels and radio stations. "At no point in history, were more people making music, distributing music, and consuming music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Music Cycles and Revivals** : Music often follows cycles where a sound gains popularity, peaks, fades, but rarely disappears completely. Instead, many rock sounds lie in wait for a generation or two before being rediscovered, reactivated, and given a "sonic update," enjoying a new period of popularity before the cycle repeats. "A sound and style will be big for a while, reach a peak with the public, and then slowly fade out." "Instead, what we've seen, rockabilly aside, after enjoying a time at the forefront of music, many of the cycle-prone rock sounds were seeded into the shadows, never really go away, lying in wait until someone comes along, often a generation or two later, to rediscover and reactivate it." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HSvgRyGiOpE

**Music Has Become Sadder Over 50 Years – CDC Monitors the Trend** : Analysis of 150,000 songs from the Top 100 charts between 1965 and 2015 revealed that popular music has grown measurably sadder. Use of the word "love" fell by half, negative words increased, and 50% of contemporary songs are in a minor key compared to just 15% in the 1960s. The Centers for Disease Control monitors this trend. "The use of the word 'love' was reduced by half, negative words increased, and 50% of current songs are in a minor key versus 15% in the 60s." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qtdetc5-MQo
**Music History Defining Eras** : Throughout history, certain periods, like the early 1990s (Grunge/Alternative), mid-1950s (Rock and Roll), 1960s (Beatles-led), and 1970s (Punk), have created a pervasive sense that music history was actively being made, characterized by a constant influx of new sounds and artists. **Music Inadvertently Sent into Space via Radio** : The invention of radio approximately 100 years ago inadvertently began sending music into space. This means that if there is extraterrestrial life on any of the estimated 300 Earth-like planets within 50 light-years, they might be receiving our early broadcasts now. "It started with our invention of radio, which inadvertently sent music into space, starting about 100 years ago." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aSk1XQHNkd8
**Music Industry Shifts and Personal Despair** : During Hugh Dillon's severe addiction, he felt the cultural landscape was overwhelmed by pop acts like the Spice Girls and Backstreet Boys, which he perceived as displacing "great music." **Music Industry in 1995** : When the Warped Tour began in 1995, the music industry was vastly different: the internet was barely used, MP3s were unheard of, streaming was years away, and the compact disc was the dominant music format. These fundamental changes in the industry were a factor in the tour's eventual conclusion in 2018. "when the tour started in 1995, hardly anyone was using the internet. No one had ever heard of MP3s. Streaming was years in the future and the compact disk ruled." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7jfQaUV6Bq4
**Music Industry's "Rule of 30"** : Historically, in periods of industry prosperity, a "rule of 30" often governed record labels' financial model: "If a label released 30 records, 25 would lose money, 3 or 4 would break even, and 1 or 2 would become massive enough to pay for all the others." This illustrates the critical role of highly successful bands in generating the profits necessary to subsidize the development of new acts and cover the losses from less successful releases, maintaining the overall music industry ecosystem. "If a label released 30 records, 25 would lose money, 3 or 4 would break even, and 1 or 2 would become massive enough to pay for all the others." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7Zniri9uSlc
**Music Industry's Environmental Reckoning** : The music industry, recognized as a major polluter and energy consumer (through tours, non-biodegradable plastics, and the carbon footprint of streaming), has slowly begun an "environmental reckoning" and is moving towards more eco-friendly practices. This includes the emergence of "green records" made from sustainable materials, green platforms aiming to reduce energy consumption, and recording studios adopting high-efficiency gear, carbon-neutral methods, and sustainable energy sources. Remote collaboration now reduces travel needs. Concerts and festivals are increasingly powered by renewable energy, encourage waste reduction, and use digital tickets. Artists are selling merchandise made from organic/recycled fabrics with non-harmful dyes, engaging fans on environmental issues, and organizing benefit concerts. The touring industry is adopting biodiesel/sustainable fuels, electric vehicles, carbon offsets, and local sourcing to minimize its environmental impact. "The music industry is a major polluter and a major devourer of energy. The number of pollutants created by a single tour is incredible." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZzIqIydZTlA
**Music Licensing Bypasses Gatekeepers** : Licensing music provides artists with a direct route to their audience, bypassing traditional industry gatekeepers such as record labels, radio stations, and video channels. This approach allows artists to get paid, gain exposure, and potentially open doors to further opportunities without relying on conventional intermediaries. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Music Licensing Deal Value** : The financial compensation an artist can receive from a licensing deal varies significantly, ranging from a quick $10,000 for some placements to potentially half a million dollars or more for a 20 or 30-second snippet if the advertiser is highly motivated. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Music Licensing Process - Agency Outreach** : Alternatively, music personnel or creative directors at an advertising agency might already be familiar with and like a particular band or song. **Music Licensing Process - Pitching** : One method for securing a licensing deal involves artists or their representatives pitching a song to an advertising agency for potential future use in a campaign. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Music Memories Are Stored Separately from All Other Memories** : In 2005, a 71-year-old professional classical musician suffered severe meningitis that destroyed parts of his brain, leaving him with total retrograde amnesia — his entire life was erased — and an inability to form new memories. Yet he could still play complicated pieces learned decades earlier, and could sight-read and memorize new music. In another case, an Ottawa woman named Allison Wojciechowska survived surgery to remove a golf ball-sized brain aneurysm but lost the ability to speak, concentrate, read, or write. However, the moment she was wheeled to a piano, she could play. Music therapists used musical phrases to reconstruct her spoken language — she eventually regained the ability to speak in three languages. "Our music memories are separate and isolated from our day-to-day memories." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NMwMwqMQpf4

**Music Phenatologist in Palliative Care** : A music phenatologist (from the Greek word for death) is a palliative care specialist who plays or sings soft music for patients in their final hours. They monitor vital signs and consciousness, adjusting the music to alleviate physical, emotional, and spiritual pain. Music can trigger happy memories or emotional releases, naturally increasing dopamine and providing comfort. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BHN6db7m3DM

**Music Piracy and Its Impact (Early 2000s)** : The early 2000s witnessed an explosion of music piracy, profoundly impacting the music industry, particularly accelerating the cratering of physical music sales. This phenomenon, alongside the rise of digital access to music, further highlighted the need for artists and the industry to find alternative revenue streams, such as music licensing, as demonstrated by Moby's success with "Play." "music piracy exploded and physical sales cratered." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xid8CZf4oYo
**Music Piracy – Dropped Dramatically After Streaming Arrived** : Before streaming took off in the late 2000s, millions of people were stealing music through file sharing, torrents, and bootlegs. Streaming reduced piracy dramatically by offering high-quality music cheaply with no virus risk, incomplete files, or obligation to seed. A practice called stream ripping — recording songs from streams — persists, but piracy is nowhere near what it was. CD sales continue to decline but more slowly than before. "Why bother going through the hassle of stealing something when you could simply be assured of high quality music from streams." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MQ7PDi-D9Ig

**Music Video Evolution and Decline** : The traditional music video, popular in the 1970s and 80s when seeing a favorite band was a novelty, is considered "dead" in its original form. Once a valuable marketing tool that could generate significant album sales for a half-million dollar investment, videos are now often "sinkholes with no return" due to the constant availability of content on platforms like YouTube via smartphones. The music video is evolving, with some creators utilizing mobile phone video capabilities for production. "At least in the form in which it was born back in the 70s and 80s." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yl2poVWguu0
**Music Video Importance in 80s** : The 1980s, characterized by the rise of MTV and MuchMusic, saw music videos become a crucial medium for storytelling, dancing, and style, captivating audiences with visually driven content from artists like Madonna, Peter Gabriel, Phil Collins, Michael Jackson, and Aerosmith. "I came up in the 80s era where that's what made me fall in love with music videos, right? The MTV, much music era, watching videos by like Madonna, Peter Gabriel, and like Phil Collins and Michael Jackson and Eros Smith." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bYsV3ozbk4M
**Music Video Influences of Director X** : Director X developed his profound appreciation for music videos during the 1980s MTV and Much Music era, being particularly captivated by the storytelling, dancing, and distinctive style found in videos by artists such as Madonna, Peter Gabriel, Phil Collins, Michael Jackson, and Aerosmith. "I came up I came up in the 80s era where that's what made me fall in love with music videos, right? The MTV, much music era watching videos by like Madonna and Peter Gabriel and like Phil Collins and Michael Jackson and Errol Smith." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IIJySSo276k
**Music Video Production (Art Context Podcast)** : The "Art Context" podcast, hosted by Director X and Taj Khrishlo, aims to celebrate music video directors as storytellers and creative artists, exploring their journeys, processes, and influences in creating impactful music videos and films, addressing the lack of recognition for their contributions. "I feel like we live in the world where we don't give these amazing creative artists, the flowers they deserve." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bYsV3ozbk4M
**Music Video Production Process** : The "Art Context" podcast aims to delve into the unseen aspects of music video creation, going beyond the final product. It explores the storyboards, art direction, collaboration with department heads, and the entire process of how filmmakers reach the finish line to create a piece of art. "But you don't see what went into to make that product and that piece of art. I feel is the storyboards and the the art direction and sitting down with your head departments and the collaboration." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LgJ7ww2AgF4
**Music Video Production Trends and Budgets** : In the late 1990s/early 2000s, music videos often involved substantial budgets, reportedly up to $200,000, and frequently featured "hot" young directors who produced abstract or unappealing concepts, such as standing in a "cold, cold puddle in a warehouse." This traditional, expensive approach eventually clashed with the rise of cheaper, more accessible video production methods. "We would do these videos for 200 grand and they'd hire some student out of Mexico City. He was all the hot **** and he'd make a stand in a cold, cold puddle in a warehouse and I'm like, well, what the hell is this about? This is stupid." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=W9gdKha0PLg
**Music and Brain Lobes** : The experience of music actively engages all four major lobes of the brain, with different regions responsible for specific functions such as emotional reactions, memory formation, and movement motivated by music. Scientists have only recently begun to precisely map which brain parts are dedicated to processing music. "Experiencing music requires all four of the brain's major lobes." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Music and Dopamine – Neurologically, Sex, Drugs, and Rock and Roll Are the Same Thing** : Deep inside the brain, the amygdala, hippocampus, and cerebellum produce a hormone called dopamine — the body's feel-good chemical. The body produces dopamine during orgasm, during cocaine use, and when hearing a great song that gives you chills and makes you want to dance. Neurologically speaking, sex, drugs, and rock and roll produce the same chemical reward. "Our brains are built to respond to sex drugs and rock and roll." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NMwMwqMQpf4
**Music as Identity and Comfort Food** : Music consumed between the ages of 14 and 24 becomes deeply intertwined with an individual's identity, used first to understand oneself and then to project that identity to the world (e.g., "I'm a punk kid," "I'm a metal kid," "I'm a goth kid"). This music remains "comfort food forever" for the rest of their lives. "If you grew up in the 90s, if you were between 14 and 24 in the 90s, that will be your music for the rest of your life. It is going to be your comfort food forever." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90
**Music as Sustenance During Slavery** : Over centuries of forced displacement to the West, music, including work songs, protest songs, and satirical songs, served as a crucial means of sustenance for enslaved African people. These songs, with regular or syncopated rhythms, helped them endure brutal times and preserved their identities, history, and traditions. "And these songs and rhythms helped sustain them through those awful brutal times." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hQJ3r-DCoMQ
**Music as a Motivator and Distraction in Exercise** : Numerous studies confirm that listening to music before or during exercise significantly improves results. Music acts as a motivator, enabling individuals to exercise longer and more vigorously. It also serves as a distraction, helping exercisers forget their fatigue and soreness. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BHN6db7m3DM
**Music as a Recycled Art Form** : Music is consistently recycled and renewed, with scenes and sounds reappearing, sometimes discovered independently or stumbled upon through older records. This ongoing process highlights how music continually evolves by referencing its past. "Whatever the case and whatever the source, music is constantly being recycled and renewed." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9CNNsqXiL6U
**Music as a Reflection of Society** : Music consistently serves as a reflection of broader social conditions and attitudes. This principle was exemplified after the 9/11 attacks, when the prevailing mood shifted, rendering previously dominant happy pop music inappropriate. "Music always reflects what's happening in the world at large." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=raRCZ0Y5up8
**Music as an Identity Marker** : During the formative years (roughly high school to early 20s), individuals use music to construct and project their identity. This involves adopting specific fashion trends associated with preferred music (e.g., punk, metal, goth) and forming friendships with like-minded music fans, who become their "tribes" or "social constructs." "This is called using music as an identity marker." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Music for Pain Management** : Research from the University of Utah indicates that listening to music, specifically Mozart, can significantly augment the pain-reducing effects of medication like ibuprofen. While ibuprofen alone reduced inflammation by 70%, its efficacy increased to 90% when combined with listening to Mozart in mouse trials, suggesting a promising avenue for new human pain management strategies. "when they gave pain sufferers ibuprofen and had them listen to Mozart at the same time, that inflammation decreased when from 70% to 90%, which meant even less pain." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Music in Dreams for Musicians vs. Non-Musicians** : Scientists have noted a significant difference in dream content between musicians and non-musicians. For non-musicians, it is rare to experience music in their dreams, with only about eighteen percent of regular people reporting such dreams. In contrast, forty percent of those who play instruments dream with music. "If you're a non-musician, it's very rare to have dreams that contain music. Scientists say about eighteen percent of regular people dream with music compared to forty percent of those who play instruments." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GO0K_N7Ys7I
**Music's Unintended Psychological Impact** : Music, particularly song lyrics or the singer, can become an obsessive focus for individuals "living on a knife's edge" (angry, depressed, disturbed, or mentally ill). Such individuals may decode what they perceive as secret messages directed solely at them, leading to unintended and horrific consequences, over which the artist has no control. "The person begins to obsess over the lyrics or the singer. Perhaps they're able to decode what they think is a secret message directed solely at them. But every once in a while, that person is moved to act." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FtGJHhqXcDI
**Music-Induced Chills (Piloerection)** : A 2020 study by French researchers, using EEG machines on volunteers who regularly experience chills from music, identified specific electrical activity in the Orbital Frontal Cortex (involved in emotion processing), the supplementary motor area (controlling movement), and the audio processing areas of the right temporal lobe (related to music appreciation). These regions collectively prompt the amygdala to release more dopamine, and combined with anticipation, result in a tingly chill emanating from the cerebellum, indicating heightened brain connectivity. "They found that certain music created very specific electrical activity in an area called the Orbital Frontal Cortex, a region that we use for processing emotions." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Musical Generation Cycle Concept** : The term "generation" can also be applied to cycles observed within music, distinct from the child-parent biological cycle of human existence. "We can also use the word generation to describe other cycles, like the cycles we see in music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=v_am7ifh7Pk
**Musical Generation Length** : If a "generation in music" is defined as the 10-year period of coming of age (ages 14-24), the cycles within music will repeat much more rapidly than the standard genealogical definition of a generation. "If we consider that 10-year period to be a generation in music, the cycles will repeat much faster than the standard genealogical definition of generation." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=v_am7ifh7Pk
**Musical Knowledge and Deja Vu** : As listeners become more experienced and knowledgeable, they begin to notice cycles and trends in music, leading to a sense of déjà vu. Current sounds may seem familiar, as "history is on repeat," with old elements being recycled and rehashed. For instance, a band like Beauty School Dropout might evoke Blink-182, which descended from Green Day, which in turn incorporated elements of The Ramones' fast 60s pop songs. "Our musical knowledge can make things very annoying because it makes seem that history is on repeat." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Musical Memories in the Hippocampus** : Musical memories are stored in the hippocampus, the brain region responsible for all memory formation, yet they are distinct and separate from other life memories. Studies on individuals suffering from irreversible amnesia due to disease or accident have shown that while they lose all personal memories, including their name, their ability to remember favorite songs, play instruments, and read music (if previously learned) astonishingly remains intact. "musical memories are personal database of familiar songs, are, while still in the hippocampus, separate from all our other memories." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Musical Offspring Phenomenon** : Children of famous musicians often pursue musical careers, influenced by a blend of genetic predisposition ("nature") and exposure to the music industry lifestyle ("nurture"), including access to parental connections and relationships. "And because your parents have connections and relationships, you might have an inside line on establishing a career." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dY7uB_QQWBc
**Musical Taste and Parent's Height** : Research suggests a curious link between an individual's musical taste and the height of the parent who took primary responsibility for their upbringing. The theory proposes that babies attuned to a shorter parent's quicker walking pace (due to shorter legs) might develop a preference for faster musical rhythms, whereas those with taller parents (longer strides, slower pace) might lean towards slower music. "Your taste in music may be related to the height of your parents, or specifically, the parent which did most of the parenting." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Musician Plane Crash Trend** : Historically, musicians dying in plane crashes was a more common tragedy than it is in modern times, with various high-profile incidents occurring over several decades. Thankfully, the number of such plane crashes and musician fatalities has drastically declined in recent years due to improved technology and regulations. "Musician's dying in plane crashes was tragically more common than it is today." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dgzF_KBSQWM
**Musicians Declining to Perform for Donald Trump** : Donald Trump consistently faced challenges in securing musical support for his political events. While artists like Kid Rock, Ted Nugent, Three Doors Down, and Ace Frehley showed support, prominent musicians such as The Killers, Celine Dion, Meat Loaf, and Aerosmith all declined invitations to perform for him on various occasions. "Donald Trump has always had a problem getting musicians to show their support for him. Outside of Kid Rock, Ted Nugent, three doors down and ace freely. The killers, Celine Dion, Meat Lough and Erasmith all turned him down to play various things." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HoBx6s3JmVQ
**Musicians' Shorter Lifespan** : A University of Sydney professor, after studying musician deaths between 1950 and 2014 and comparing them to the general population, concluded that musicians have an average lifespan 25 years shorter than others. "the average lifespan of a musician is 25 years shorter." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=72Lei7uug8c
**My Chemical Romance – From an Irvine Welsh Book Title Plus My Bloody Valentine** : Irvine Welsh (who wrote Trainspotting) also wrote a book called Five Tales of Chemical Romance. The "My" was added as a homage to My Bloody Valentine. My Bloody Valentine's name itself derives from the title of a 1981 Canadian slasher film. "That's a bonus for this list." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Mystery in Music in the Internet Age** : The pervasive nature of the internet has significantly diminished the sense of mystery that historically surrounded music artists. In earlier times, before music videos and widespread media, knowledge of artists was limited to still pictures and album artwork, requiring fans to infer details. "The internet has destroyed a lot of the mystery surrounding music that we used to have back in the olden days." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8sAxFvktx-A
**Mystify Michael Hutchence (2019) – Documentary** : One of at least two major documentaries about Michael Hutchence, released in 2019. "mystified Michael Hutchinson's in 2019" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=23OgreyK66o
**NME (The Enemy) Magazine** : This mainstream music publication from the UK began to pay more attention to Goth, largely due to its fashion sense. "Mainstream music publications, most notably the enemy and the face, both out of the UK, began to be more attention, drawn largely out of fashion sense of the whole thing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=evlGhfUe6QQ
**Naked Toddler (later Creed) – Creed's Original Name** : Before becoming Creed, the band was called Naked Toddler. "Naked Toddler. That was what Creed was called in the beginning." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Napster (1999) – Enabled Mass Pre-Release Album Piracy** : The launch of Napster in 1999 made mass piracy of albums before their official release dates trivially easy, creating an entirely new category of challenge for the music industry that had not existed in the physical bootleg era. "Facilitated the massive piracy of albums before their official release, creating a new challenge for the industry." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Uly2cT2vc28
**Napster and Digital Music Discovery (Early 2000s)** : The advent of Napster and illegal file-sharing platforms fundamentally altered how music was discovered and accessed in the early 2000s. It made it "super easy" for listeners to explore new bands without the need for traditional record store searches, playing a significant role in the proliferation of new musical movements like the indie rock revival. Napster exemplified how the new digital world could both disrupt traditional models and foster new musical trends. "Suddenly, it was super easy to check out some band that you made her that was supposedly really cool. No board dredging around record stores looking for their stuff." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xid8CZf4oYo
**Napster and Peer-to-Peer File Sharing** : In its early days, Napster and peer-to-peer file sharing provided a novel way for people to access a vast, previously invisible universe of music. It enabled free sampling of new music and the discovery of off-the-radar indie bands, facilitating connections between users with similar tastes. This method was crucial for music discovery before the advent of widespread streaming, YouTube, or a mature iTunes. "Peer-to-peer file sharing, League of Bar-N-O-D, was a way for everyone to get access to a universe of music that had largely been out of sight, totally invisible." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=raRCZ0Y5up8
**Napster and the Rise of A La Carte Music** : The advent of the internet and illegal file-sharing programs like Napster transformed music into an "a la carte buffet," where fans could download individual MP3s instead of buying expensive CDs for a single track, marking the beginning of the end for the album era. "With Napster and all the other original illegal file sharing programs, music became one big allocard buffet." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Napster's Launch and Impact (1999)** : Napster launched online five years after the "Celestial Jukebox" concept, creating a sensation by allowing users to download virtually any song they desired, despite the legal ambiguities surrounding its operation. "Five years later, Napster went online and suddenly it seemed that you could download any song you wanted." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Napster's Launch and Impact (June 1, 1999)** : On June 1st, 1999, amateur programmer Sean Fanning released Napster to 30 friends, marking a pivotal moment in music history. This peer-to-peer file-sharing invention fundamentally changed how music was distributed and consumed, making it easier for millions to access music. "But everything changed on June 1st, 1999, a date that is every bit as important to the history of rock of all music, actually, than anything else you can imagine. This was the date an amateur computer programmer named Sean Fanning gave something he developed to 30 friends on the promise that they not share it with anyone else. He called his invention Napster." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Napster's Legacy in Streaming** : While Napster was initially known for peer-to-peer file sharing, its intellectual property was acquired by Rhapsody in November 2011. In 2016, Rhapsody fully rebranded itself as Napster, continuing its legacy as an on-demand streaming service. "Except that in November 2011, it bought what was left of Napster, all the intellectual property. And in 2016, Rhapsody completely rebranded itself as Napster, which is how it operates today." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Napster's Release and its Date (June 1, 1999)** : The original version of Napster was released on June 1, 1999, precisely 32 years after *Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band*, marking a significant shift away from the album-centric music industry model. "That was the moment when the original version of Napster was released into the wild." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Napster's Sociological Component** : Beyond providing free music, Napster fostered a unique sociological connection. Early file-sharers could discover strangers globally who shared identical musical tastes, creating a powerful sense of not being alone in their preferences—a feeling now taken for granted. "Napster and his descendants not only allowed us to get music for free, but it also had a sociological component. Someone who remembers those early days of file sharing will no doubt recall a time when you found a stranger somewhere on the planet who had musical tastes that were just like yours." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Nash the Slash – EP Playable at Any Speed (33⅓, 45, or 78 RPM)** : Toronto multi-instrumentalist Nash the Slash (real name possibly Jeff, never confirmed; known for always appearing completely wrapped in surgical bandages) released a 1981 instrumental EP called *Decomposing* in which all five tracks were written, arranged, and recorded to sound coherent at any turntable speed — 33⅓, 45, or 78 RPM. He had been part of Toronto prog-rock band FM in the late 1970s before going solo with film soundtrack work and albums. "This EP is written, arranged, and recorded so that each of the five tracks sounded good no matter what speed you played it on." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Dt7mb4yyuWM
**Nashville Bird Sanctuary Creative Inspiration** : Ash Boo Shultz experienced a profound emotional moment at a bird sanctuary in Nashville, describing it as the "most beautiful moment that I'd ever had in my life." This experience, including a conversation with a couple he encountered, directly channeled into the lyrics for a new USS single, demonstrating his receptive creative process. "I was just crying because it was the most beautiful moment that I'd ever had in my life and a couple walked by and I stopped them and I said, can I tell you something?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=N-3eddy4J7g
**Nashville Recording Session (1960)** : In late 1960, a recording session in Nashville for Marty Robbins' song "Don't Worry" led to an accidental discovery of distortion. Guitarist Grady Martin plugged his baritone guitar into a recording console's channel that had a faulty preamplifier due to faulty transistors and transformers from the manufacturer's move from New York to California. This malfunction produced an unintended fuzzy sound that was initially disliked by Robbins but kept by producer Owen Bradley and engineer Glen Snottie, leading to a hit and a quest to replicate the sound. "Meanwhile though, something weird happened during a recording session in Nashville." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iGav9uJwA_w
**Nathaniel Baldwin's Polygamy and Bankruptcy** : Nathaniel Baldwin, the inventor of improved telephone receivers that became US Navy headphones, was a Mormon fundamentalist who strongly believed in and practiced polygamy, as did many employees of his Baldwin Radio Company. Profits from the company were used to promote an offshoot of a fundamentalist version of the Church of Latter-day Saints, contributing to his bankruptcy in 1924 and subsequent fraud conviction. "In fact, profits from the factory went to promoting an offshoot of a very fundamentalist version of the Church of Latter-day Saints." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NAroxFbYkRw
**National Mourning for Gord Downie** : Upon Gord Downie's death on October 18, 2017, the entire country plunged into mourning. Flags were lowered, lights dimmed, moments of silence observed, and numerous tributes and fundraisers for cancer treatment and Indigenous causes were held. The sentiment was captured by a tweet that simply read: "Canada closed, death in the family." "The whole country plunged into mourning. The best tweet I saw was Canada closed, death in the family. The Prime Minister appeared on TV and tears. Flags were lowered, lights were dimmed, moments of silence were held." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Um_KEEcCeT4
**Neanderthal Musical Creativity** : A flute made from a bear's femur, with four holes for Do, Rey, Mi, and Fa, was found in Slovenia and dated to 82,000 years ago. This instrument was crafted by a Neanderthal, demonstrating that early hominids, not just Homo sapiens, possessed the capacity for music creation. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BHN6db7m3DM
**Near-Fatal Karaoke Incident in China** : In China, a 55-year-old woman named Zan nearly died while singing karaoke when attempting to hit a high note. The exertion caused a blood vessel in her brain to burst, leading to a stroke, which was only averted by emergency surgery. "A fifty five year old woman named Zan tried to hit a high note during a song that led to a burst blood vessel in her brain that caused a stroke, and the only thing that saved her was emergency surgery." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HoBx6s3JmVQ
**Necessity of Insurance for Music Venues** : Operating a music venue without adequate insurance is deemed an irresponsible and unviable business practice, given the potential for catastrophic financial liabilities and losses in the event of a disaster. "And if you don't have insurance, man, you should not be in the music venue business at all." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Pgchw2h87aw
**Necessity of Touring for Modern Artists** : With royalty checks from record sales drastically diminished, touring has become the primary means for artists to maintain cash flow and lifestyle, leading to a crowded touring market. "The only way to maintain cashflow in lifestyle is to get back out on the road and tour with everyone else." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Negotiation of Music Snippet Usage** : Once a song is selected for licensing, detailed negotiations occur regarding the specific use of the music snippet. This includes agreeing on how the song will be edited to fit the commercial, the duration of the campaign, and the number of different platforms on which it will appear. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Nerdle** : This is the term for a tiny dab of toothpaste applied to a toothbrush. "What's a nerdle? That's what you call a tiny dab of toothpaste on your brush." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Neurological Basis of Youthful Music Love** : By adolescence, the human brain has developed to fully process auditory information. Combined with the intense emotions of puberty, this leads to the formation of "strong and lasting bonds related to memory, emotion, and identity," all deeply intertwined with music. This foundational love for music in youth profoundly influences an individual's identity for the rest of their life. "The results are strong and lasting bonds related to memory, emotion, and identity, and they're all wrapped up in music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Neuroplasticity and Brain Disruption** : Ash Boo Shultz of USS expressed a deep interest in the concept of neuroplasticity and the idea of "rewind" or disrupting the brain. This interest informed his unique stage performances, where he would play contrasting audio tracks simultaneously to create an uncomfortable, thought-provoking experience for the audience. "I was just so interested in the whole idea of neuroplasticity and the whole idea of of rewind, like just disrupting, you know, just rupting the brain." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=N-3eddy4J7g
**New Wave Fashion** : New Wave developed its own distinctive fashion, immediately recognizable with elements such as skinny ties and big glasses, contributing to the genre's overall visual identity and cultural impact. "When it came to fashion, New Wave had to look all its own. They're probably already thinking about skinny ties and big glasses." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bYsV3ozbk4M
**New Wave Revival of the 2000s** : Beginning in the early 2000s, a new generation of bands emerged, drawing heavily from their parents' or older siblings' record collections. They rediscovered and were inspired by classic New Wave artists like New Order, The Cure, Duran Duran, David Bowie, Depeche Mode, The Smiths, Joy Division, and Blondie, creating a sound that was fresh yet familiar. "At the beginning of the 2000s, we began to hear from a new generation of young bands who obviously spent a lot of time going through their parents or older siblings' record collections." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9CNNsqXiL6U
**New Wave Revivalists in New York (Early 2000s)** : On the American side, many new wave revivalists in the early 2000s were based in New York, including The Yeah Yeah Yeahs, Interpol, The Rapture, and The Bravery. "On this side of the Atlantic, a lot of new wave revivalists seem to be headquartered in New York, the Ye-E-S, Interpol, the Rapture, and maybe the best of them all, or at least the most obvious of them all, the bravery." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9CNNsqXiL6U
**New York City Anti-Dancing Laws (1926-Recent)** : Until recently, it was illegal to dance in New York City venues serving alcohol without an expensive "cabaret license" requiring fingerprinting and denying permits to those with criminal records. Enacted in 1926, this law cracked down on Harlem speakeasies, not just for Prohibition but to prevent racial mixing. It also criminalized playing radio or piano in bars until 1936, leading to common police raids and arrests for swaying. Rudy Giuliani later used it in the 1980s to target hip-hop venues and raves, pushing parties underground. The anti-dancing laws were finally repealed this year. "This law came into effect in 1926 as a way to crack down on the Speakeasies in Harlem, not just because of prohibition, because this was a way to stop whites and blacks from mixing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aSk1XQHNkd8
**New York Dolls – Named After the New York Doll Hospital, a Real Doll Repair Shop** : The New York Dolls took their name from the New York Doll Hospital, a real shop in New York that repaired dolls. "A place that actually repaired dolls." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Nicholas Bourbaki (Pseudonym)** : Nicholas Bourbaki was a collective pseudonym adopted by a group of real-life French mathematicians in the 1930s who engaged in esoteric mathematical research. This name is incorporated into the *Trench* mythology as the true identity of the character Niko, who is also the Blurryface character from the previous album. "The name Niko is derived from Nicholas Borbacchi, which was a pseudonym used by a bunch of real-life French mathematicians back in the 1930s, who did some really esoteric things with numbers that I can't even begin to understand." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8sAxFvktx-A
**Nichols Corporation Dominates Ice Cream Truck Music** : The ubiquitous songs played by ice cream trucks are largely controlled by one family from Minnesota. In 1973, Bob Nichols started providing music boxes specifically preloaded with jingles for ice cream trucks, and currently, the Nichols Corporation accounts for 97% of these music boxes. "And today, 97% of those ice cream truck music boxes are controlled by the Nichols Corporation." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-N6IM5Nm5iw
**Nick Rhodes Refused Hotel Rooms with Brown Walls** : During Duran Duran's glory days, Nick Rhodes absolutely refused to stay in any hotel room with brown walls. No explanation was ever provided. "No one seems to know why." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZbHRIh3RUoo
**Nile Rodgers Producing The Swing** : Producer Nile Rodgers became involved with InXS's album *The Swing* after catching one of their gigs in Toronto, subsequently producing the album in New York. "This journey started in Toronto when producer Nile Rogers caught a gig. That led to him producing the album in New York." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=23OgreyK66o
**Nine Inch Nails – Trent Reznor Simply Liked It After Two Weeks** : Trent Reznor constantly doodled band name ideas; his rule was that if he still liked a name after two weeks, he kept it. Nine Inch Nails was the only name that made the cut. "There isn't a great story behind it." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Nirvana Nevermind Cover (1991) – Swimming Baby Spencer Elden; Underwater Birth Idea; Photoshopped Fish Hook; Dad's Handprint Visible** : Kurt Cobain came up with the Nevermind cover concept inspired by a documentary on underwater births he and Dave Grohl watched during recording sessions, combined with his memories of supervising preschooler swims as a YMCA lifeguard in Aberdeen, Washington. A stock photo was found but the photographer demanded $7,500 per year while the album remained in print — so a photographer named Kurt Wettle (ex-Navy, previously had experience blowing things up with dynamite, also a mail-order minister who had married the baby's parents) was hired instead. Multiple babies were brought to the Pasadena Aquatic Center and thrown into the pool while Wettle shot pictures. Four-month-old Spencer Elden (son of Rick and Renata Elden of Eagle Rock, California) was selected. The fish hook with a dollar bill was added later via Photoshop — Kurt's idea. If you look at the right side of Spencer's rib cage, you can see his dad's handprint from where he was being held before the toss. Spencer was paid $150 for his troubles. At last word he still lives in the LA area, has a platinum award for Nevermind over his bed, and is not much of a Nirvana fan — the White Stripes are his thing. "Spencer, he was paid $150 for all his troubles." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JdSUHkXM1mQ
**Nirvana's Nevermind Producer (Butch Vig)** : Butch Vig, who produced L7's breakthrough album "Bricks Are Heavy," is also known for producing Nirvana's iconic album "Nevermind." "And it was produced by Butch Vig, the same guy who did never mind with Nirvana." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=oLC49nCf0ZM

**Non-Copyrightable Musical Elements - Chord Progressions** : "Chord progressions" are not copyrightable, as demonstrated by groups like Axis of Awesome, who show how "dozens of songs are built on the exact same four chords." "Another thing that can't be copyrighted is chord per reshians." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rfObVld9rIE
**Non-Copyrightable Musical Elements - Guitar Riffs** : Guitar riffs "can't copyright" them. This explains why similar riffs can appear across different songs, such as those by Green Day, Chicago, Led Zeppelin, and The Beatles. "You can't copyright a guitar riff, which also takes us back to that Foo Fighters Ronnie James D.O. Case." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rfObVld9rIE
**Non-Copyrightable Musical Elements - Rhythms and Beats** : "Rhythms and beats are not protected" by copyright. This allows for the widespread use of patterns like the "Bo Diddley beat" or the "shave and a haircut, two bits rhythm" by multiple artists without legal issues. "Rhythms and beats are not protected." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rfObVld9rIE
**Non-Copyrightable Musical Elements - Song Titles** : Song titles are "not protected by copyright," meaning one "could write a piano ballad and call it smells like teen spirit, and there is nothing anybody could do" legally. "Song titles for one. If you wanted to, you could write a piano ballad and call it smells like teen spirit, and there is nothing anybody could do." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rfObVld9rIE
**Non-Pythagorean Musical Systems** : Not all cultures adopted Pythagoras's mathematically precise system of organizing music. Many cultures, including those in Africa, the Indian subcontinent, China, and more recently the US South, utilized notes that fell between Pythagoras's "perfect" natural ratios, indicating a broader approach to musical intonation. "Other cultures were fond of using the notes between Pythagoras' perfect natural ratios." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**Nostalgia for 1950s Music (Early 1970s)** : Following the disillusionment of the late 1960s, a period of "nostalgia for music of the 1950s" emerged, characterized by media like "American graffiti and happy days in Shanana and Elton John singing Crocodile Rock in 1972." **Nostalgia: Definition and History** : Nostalgia is broadly defined as "being sentimental about the past," functioning as a "psychic happy place." The term originated in the 16th century with a medical student observing Swiss mercenaries exhibiting anxiety away from home, initially viewing it as a form of melancholy or mental illness. Today, it generally refers to a "pining for the good old days." "Broadly defined, nostalgia is being sentimental about the past. It's a psychic happy place." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Nostalgic "Sweet Spot" in Youth** : The "good old days for music" typically refer to the period when an individual was around 14 years old and extending into their early 20s. Studies place the specific "nostalgic sweet spot" at ages 17 or 19. This trend remains stable over many years, marking the "all-important coming of age musically years." "Other studies have shown that the nostalgic sweet spot is at age 17." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE

**Novel Vinyl Pressing Materials** : Beyond standard and colored vinyl, records have been experimentally pressed using a variety of unusual and sometimes shocking materials. These include blood, hair, urine, marijuana leaves, razor blades, gunpowder, and even human cremated remains. One notable example is an album for Emperor Yes, released in 100 copies, each sprinkled with dust from a 16th-century asteroid. **Nucleus Accumbens and Dopamine Release** : The nucleus accumbens, identified as the pleasure-seeking center of the brain, releases a blast of dopamine—the body's natural "feel-good" hormone—when an individual encounters something they like, including a favorite song. This biological mechanism implies a design within our brains that seeks out pleasurable experiences akin to "sex, drugs, and rock and roll." "When we find something we like, the nucleus accumbens give us a blast of a hormone called dopamine, which is the body's natural feel-good drug." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ

**Oil Crisis of 1973-1974 and Vinyl Quality** : The oil crisis, triggered by Arab oil-producing states cutting production after the October 6, 1973, war between Egypt/Syria and Israel, caused a spike in petrochemical prices. Since vinyl is a petrochemical product, its cost increased significantly, forcing the recording industry to use recycled, impure vinyl and make records thinner. This led to a drastic deterioration in sound quality (more noise, shallow grooves, warping) by the late 1970s and early 1980s. "This was the oil crisis of 1973 and 1974, which resulted in all kinds of shortages and a recession." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NAroxFbYkRw
**Oingo Boingo – The Mystic Knights of the Oingo Boingo, a Secret Society in Amos and Andy** : Danny Elfman's band was originally called The Mystic Knights of the Oingo Boingo, borrowing the name of a fictional secret society from the old Amos and Andy radio show (circa 1930s). Elfman later moved into film and TV scoring, writing themes including The Simpsons. "Which was a secret society used in the old Amos and Andy Radio Show." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Oklahoma City Bombing (April 19, 1995)** : On April 19, 1995, Timothy McVeigh detonated a bomb at the federal building in Oklahoma City, an event that, until September 11, 2001, was the worst terrorist attack on American soil. This incident forced Kevin Lyman to change the name of his planned tour from "The Bomb" to "Warped" on the very day of its intended announcement. "Timothy McVey blew up the federal building in Oklahoma City. Until September 11, 2001, that was the worst terrorist attack on American soil. **Old Hamilton Library as Recording Studio** : Daniel Landwom utilized a vacant, historical Hamilton library building, dating back to the 1920s or 30s, as an experimental recording space. The city provided him with the key to this architecturally rich building, which featured "endless corridors and labyrinths and beautiful foyers and mezzanines," offering unique reverberant and dense acoustics for recording, particularly for drums, contrasting with his own conventional, padded studio. "I had already experimented in the old Hamilton library because the library had relocated and the building they vacated was a beautiful building. I think built in the 20s or 30s and it had endless corridors and labyrinths and beautiful foyes and mezzanines" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=L03Yk1SHRNM
**Oldest Existing US and Canadian Record Stores** : The title of the oldest existing record store in the US is disputed, with claims for Ryan Hart's Music and Video, a piano store that began selling records in 1901, and Georgia Sound Shop, which opened in 1932. In Canada, Wilson and Lee in Oshawa, founded in 1922, was a significant contender but unfortunately closed permanently in the fall of 2019. "The oldest existing record store in the US is either Ryan Hart's Music and Video, a piano store that started selling records in 1901, or it could be Georgia Sound Shop, which opened for business in 1932." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jD1dWxNLvfE
