**One-Hit Wonder Definition** : The standard definition of a one-hit wonder in the recorded music industry is an artist who places only one song in the top 40 of the Billboard Hot 100 singles chart. However, for alt-rock, this definition is too narrow as alternative songs rarely reached the top 40. "The standard definition of a one-hit wonder within the recorded music industry is an artist who manages to place just one song inside the top 40 of the Billboard Hot 100 singles chart." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZcF5JMhBj2M
**Ongoing History Theme Song Creation (1993)** : The theme song for the ongoing history show was created in 1993 by imaging producer Amin Batia, following a quick directive related to the concept of "time." It combines synthesizers, production library elements, and sound effects, including a dat tape scrubbed backward for the opening and a Roland S760 sampler for the guitar ending. The source of the female vocal slide is unknown. "The theme song is a combo of me doing stuff with my synthesizers, some production library stuff, some sound effects, the opening is just a dat tape scrubbing backwards through a whole bunch of stuff because ongoing history, just a rewind through time kind of thing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90
**Online Ticketing Shift (Circa 2000)** : Around 2000, concert ticket sales began transitioning from physical box offices and phone lines to online platforms. This shift, driven by technological improvements and increased efficiency, allowed for faster sales of greater ticket volumes but also required significant capital investment in hardware and software, making it difficult for new players to enter the market. "That all began to change around 2000 when concert tickets began to be sold online." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8q2bRZyHnHE
**Onset of Musical Paralysis (Ages 27 and 33)** : Research from 2023 involving American Spotify and Amazon Echo users indicates that around age 33, individuals typically begin to "drift away from new music," perceiving it as "a racket, a cacophony, noise," signifying a type of "musical paralysis." This threshold drops to age 27 for those with children, likely due to constant exposure to contemporary pop music played by their kids. "It found that by the time we turned 33, we start to not only drift away from new music, the new music of the day, but we find it to be a rocket, a cacophony, noise." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Openness to Music (Adolescence vs. Adulthood)** : Young people, particularly adolescents, exhibit greater "open iridness" or openness to music, including unfamiliar styles. A 2013 study of 250,000 people found that adolescents devoted 20% of their waking time to music, compared to 13% in adulthood. This decline in adulthood is partly due to increased busyness but also to "psychosocial maturation," where adults rely less on external factors like music to define their identity. "In fact, our desire for musical discovery and preference for new music is at its all-time peak when we are 23 for women and 24 for men." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Optimal Daily Music Listening for Health** : A study conducted in France has determined that listening to music for exactly 78 minutes daily can contribute positively to overall health. For maximum health benefits, this daily listening should be structured into specific emotional categories: 14 minutes of uplifting music for happiness, 16 minutes of calming music, 16 minutes of music to counteract sadness, 15 minutes of motivational music for concentration, and 17 minutes of music specifically for dealing with anger. "A study from France determined the exact amount of music that we should listen to every day so we stay in good health, and that number is exactly 78 minutes." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Optimal Ticket Purchase Time for Fair Value** : Studies suggest that the "fair market value" for a concert ticket, balancing demand and willingness to pay, is often achieved 24 to 48 hours before the showtime, regardless of the seller. This indicates that waiting closer to the event may result in better prices as demand moderates or secondary sellers try to unload inventory. "Study show that the fair market value of a concert ticket, that balance between demand and what we're willing to pay, is usually achieved 24 to 48 hours before showtime." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8q2bRZyHnHE
**Orgy – Named for an Encounter with a Drag Queen That Embodied Their Mix of Influences** : Inspired by an encounter with a drag queen that the band felt encapsulated their sound — an orgy of multiple influences coming together. "It was inspired by some kind of encounter with a drag queen." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Origin of "Record Album" Term** : The terms "phonograph album" or "record album" originated from the early 20th-century practice of packaging multiple 10-inch, 78 RPM discs. These individual records were bound together in book-like formats with paperboard covers and sleeves, resembling a photo album. The German company Odeon first introduced such bundles in 1909. "It was an album for records, and this is where the term phonograph album or record album came from." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_tbKuJR0cPs
**Origin of "Smells Like Teen Spirit" Title** : The title for Nirvana's iconic song "Smells Like Teen Spirit" originated from a comment made by Kathleen Hannah to Kurt Cobain in 1991. She remarked that he smelled "sweet, almost like a particular type of deodorant marketed to teens," unaware that "Teen Spirit" was an actual brand of deodorant that Cobain did not use. "She remarked that Kurt smelled sweet, almost like a particular type of deodorant marketed to teens. Kurt was confused because he never wore deodorant. He thought she was referring to his undying punk rock ethos and was so inspired by what she said that he used her remark as the title of a new song. Smells like teen spirit. In the case you don't know, teen spirit is actually the name of deodorant." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Eo32mAZd8DI
**Origin of "Stick a Sock in It"** : In the early days of phonographs and gramophones, the volume of a record was fixed, determined by the size of its acoustic horn. To reduce volume, listeners would insert a ball of fabric, known as a "sock," into the horn to muffle the sound. This practice is the origin of the common phrase "stick a sock in it." "That ball of fabric was known as a sock. And now you know where the phrase stick a sock in it comes from." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NAroxFbYkRw
**Origin of On-Hold Music (1962)** : The concept of on-hold music originated in 1962 with Alfred Levy, who owned a factory in New York. A loose wire in his phone system touched a metal girder, turning his building into a giant radio antenna that picked up a signal from a nearby radio station. Callers placed on hold would hear this music, leading Levy to realize it kept them occupied and confirmed they were still connected. "This meant that every time someone was put on hold, this interference with the phone system resulted in music leaking through to the callers who were waiting." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D8GU8ZpSgY8
**Origin of Paid Public Concerts (1672)** : The modern concept of a paid public concert, where tickets are sold in advance for a specific performance in a private venue, is traced back to 1672. In London, John Bannister organized and performed a concert for which the general public paid one shilling for admission in his home, marking the earliest known evidence of such an event. "The general public was allowed into the gig after they bought a ticket, which sold for the price of one shilling. And this happened in 1672." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D8GU8ZpSgY8
**Origin of the Term "Grunge"** : Mark Arm, a member of Green River, worked at the warehouse at MuZac Corporation and, in the early 1980s, wrote a letter to a local entertainment weekly describing his pre-Green River band as "Pure Grunge." This letter is believed to be the first recorded instance of anyone referring to the Seattle sound using the "G word." "In the early 80s, he wrote a letter to one of the local entertainment weeklies describing his pre-Green River band as Pure Grunge. And this letter seems to be the first time anyone referred to this Seattle sound using the G word." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sCtQqVBtCaI
**Origin of the Word "Bootleg" – Prohibition-Era Hidden Alcohol** : The term "bootleg" dates to the Prohibition era in the United States, when illegal alcohol was transported and sold clandestinely, often hidden inside the shaft of tall boots. "The word 'bootleg' dates to Prohibition, when illegal alcohol was hidden in the shaft of boots." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OrHtPVBjXw4
**Original "Ghostbusters" Film Theme** : The original "Ghostbusters" film, starring Bill Murray, Harold Ramis, Ernie Hudson, and Dan Aykroyd, did not initially feature Ray Parker Jr.'s iconic theme song. **Pain and Addictive Nature of Tattoos** : While getting a tattoo is painful, particularly in areas like the elbow and knee where bone is close to the surface, this pain can induce an "adrenaline rush" and "endorphin rush." This physiological response contributes to a "dicking element" (addictive quality), making the process pleasurable for many and leading them to seek more tattoos. "There's this adrenaline rush. There's this endorphin rush that you get. That's why I think it's a dicking element because a lot of people get that rush. And the pain has gone and now it's pleasurable. Not feels good." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jZeMmPekKMQ
**Pan Am Flight 103 Missed Flights (1988)** : Several notable figures narrowly avoided the Pan Am Flight 103 bombing over Lockerbie, Scotland, on December 21, 1988. Actress Kim Cattrall changed her flight for last-minute shopping, then-world No. 1 tennis player Matt Zvilandr did not board for an unknown reason, The Four Tops overslept after performing on BBC's Top of the Pops, and Johnny Lydon and his wife Nora missed the flight by minutes due to packing delays, a fight, and traffic. "What's not widely known are the people who didn't die because they weren't on the plane when they should have been." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hmnMG6f80Sg
**Panda Mating Songs** : When a male panda is interested in mating, it communicates this interest by singing. The sound produced by a male panda is described as more akin to a bleat, but for a female panda, this sound is perceived as "sweet, sweet music." "The sound of a male panda is more like a bleat. But as far as the female panda is concerned, it's sweet, sweet music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GO0K_N7Ys7I
**Panic at the Disco – From a Line in One of Their Own Early Songs** : The band had an early song called "Panic" containing the line "panic at the disco, sat back and took it slow." The exclamation point (!), which migrated in and out of the name, was never officially part of it from the band's perspective. Guitarist Ryan Ross said fans added it, and it was eventually officially dropped. "It was never part of the name to us." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Parallel Groove Records – Two Independent Spirals on One Side; Monty Python's Matching Tie and Handkerchief (1973)** : A parallel groove record places two completely independent audio spirals on the same side, creating three sides on a two-sided record — whichever groove the stylus catches first determines what you hear. Monty Python's 1973 album Matching Tie and Handkerchief confused people who kept getting different audio each time they dropped the needle on side one. This technique dates to 1901 when Victor issued a fortune-telling record with three different fortunes on the same side. Artists who have used it include Laurie Anderson, the Sugar Cubes, Stereolab, Fine Young Cannibals, Marillion, Mr. Bungle, Kate Bush, Garbage, and Jack White. Tool's 1992 Opiate EP has a double groove that plays either the listed track or a hidden bonus track ("The Gaping Lotus Experience"). "People couldn't figure out why they kept getting different audio each time they dropped the needle on side one." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=I291j5WBc4k
**Pasturella Pestus Bacteria** : Pasturella Pestus is identified as the bacteria responsible for the Black Plague. Ash Boo Shultz of USS used this scientific name as the title for a song part he had developed, demonstrating a unique source of lyrical inspiration and linking it to the concept of depression. "Pasturella Pestus. That's the bacteria that was responsible for the black plague." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=N-3eddy4J7g
**Patent Disputes in Early Electric Guitar Industry** : The burgeoning electric guitar industry was marked by numerous patent fights and disputes over who held the rights to various technologies. One individual even attempted to sue all competitors, claiming sole ownership of all electric guitar patents. "There were patent fights and arguments about who had the right to do what with the technology. And one guy tried to sue everyone, saying that he and he alone owned all the patents to the electric guitar." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=E6cXyaHALBQ
**Patience in Music Industry** : Success stories of bands like Red Hot Chili Peppers, Muse, R.E.M., and The Black Keys emphasize the critical importance of patience and foresight from record labels, managers, and all parties involved in an artist's welfare. If genuine potential is recognized, a long-term strategy, potentially spanning years, is required. "These success stories underscore the need for patience and foresight on behalf of record labels, managers and everyone else associated with the welfare of a particular artist." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8sAxFvktx-A
**Paul Allen's Investment in Ticketmaster (1990s)** : Paul Allen, co-founder of Microsoft, recognized the growing business of concert ticket sales and invested $325 million USD to acquire an 80% stake in Ticketmaster. His involvement, providing access to the latest Microsoft technology, significantly contributed to Ticketmaster's early lead in online ticketing. "Paul Allen, the co-founder of Microsoft, recognized this and he spent $325 million US dollars to acquire an 80% stake in the company." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8q2bRZyHnHE
**Paul McCartney's Health Regimen – Eye Yoga and Daily Unsupported Headstands** : Paul McCartney does "eye yoga" (exercises to maintain sharp sight) and every morning performs an unsupported headstand for five minutes. "Dude, whatever works." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZbHRIh3RUoo
**Paul Mooney's World's Largest Private Record Collection (2008)** : Paul Mooney of Pittsburgh amassed the world's largest private record collection, which started about 50 years prior with a Frankie Lane 45. By early 2008, it contained over 3 million records (LPs, EPs, 78s, 45s, cassettes, eight tracks, CD singles, full albums) and 300,000 compact discs, covering every genre. The collection grew so vast that it required a 16,000 square foot climate-controlled warehouse, and was put up for sale on eBay for a minimum bid of $3 million, with an estimated worth closer to $50 million, though the auction fell through. "Paul Mooney, reluctant owner, still, of the world's largest private record collection." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zWNzlSxrj6s
**Paul Pontius – Immortal Records Executive** : Paul Pontius worked at Immortal Records, Korn's label in 1994. He is notable as the uncle of Justine Ferrarra, the eight-year-old model who posed for Korn's self-titled debut album cover. His family was significantly displeased with the creepy and sinister aesthetic of the final artwork. "She's the niece of Paul Pontius, who worked at Immortal Records, Korn's label at the time." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_tbKuJR0cPs
**Payola** : Payola refers to the illegal practice of paying radio stations or DJs to play a song without disclosing the payment. While illegal, it has historically occurred, particularly in the US, which is described as the biggest payola market worldwide. "no one pays a radio station to play a song, at least not legally. That's called Peola and such pay for play is illegal." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Pearl Jam – Named After Neil Young; Earlier Named After Basketball Player Mookie Blalock** : The fabricated story about Eddie Vedder's grandmother Pearl and her hallucinogenic jam spread was invented by Eddie himself, who has admitted it. The band was originally called Mookie Blalock after the New Jersey Nets point guard, but lawyers made noise about trademark use. They liked the word "Pearl" and after seeing Neil Young jam at a New Jersey concert, combined the two. "He made that all up." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Peer Licensing by Independent Bands** : Around the same time The Apples in Stereo, a fiercely independent band, made their licensing deal with Sony, similar indie bands they admired, such as Spiritualized and Stereolab, were also making deals, specifically with Volkswagen. **Percentage-Based Service Charges** : Since the 1990s, service charges have shifted from flat fees to being calculated as a percentage of the ticket's face value. This change means that as ticket prices increase, the service charge also rises significantly, impacting the final cost for consumers. "And remember, service charges are often set as a percentage of the face value of the ticket." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8q2bRZyHnHE

**Periods of Cultural Revival** : History shows a cyclical pattern where old productions, movies, TV shows, and musical sounds are constantly brought back and renewed, sometimes by generations removed from the original. Examples include Broadway revivals (West Side Story, Porgy and Bess), movie reboots (Ghostbusters, King Kong, Spider-Man, A Star Is Born), and TV remakes (90210, Twin Peaks, Star Trek). **Permanence of Tattoos** : Unlike other trends such as clothing or hairstyles, tattoos are permanent. Once they are acquired, they are "there for life," and cannot simply be shed as one "moves on to other forms of addictions or life forms," emphasizing the lasting commitment involved. "But what tattoos is, once you got them, you got them. And you can move on to other forms of addictions or life forms, you know, being, I'm going to add a lessons to adults and having a real job, again, a quote unquote, a real job. But what you have those tattoos, they're there for life." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jZeMmPekKMQ

**Peter Capaldi (12th Doctor) Was in a Punk Band Called The Dream Boats with Craig Ferguson** : Actor Peter Capaldi, who played the 12th Doctor on Doctor Who, was in a punk band called The Dream Boats when he was younger. **Peter Saville – Joy Division Unknown Pleasures (Pulsar CP1919 Signal); New Order Blue Monday (Lost £9,000 on Every Copy)** : Peter Saville from Manchester became the official go-to designer for Factory Records. His inspirations were classical arts, religious imagery, and the industrial world. Joy Division's Unknown Pleasures album cover shows 100 consecutive pulses from pulsar CP1919 — a dying star in the center of the Dumbbell Nebula in the constellation Vulpecula, essentially screaming radio waves. The Blue Monday 12-inch (1983) was designed to look like a computer floppy disk, with no band name or song title visible, and a series of colored blocks encoding a message that could only be cracked with a key included in New Order's next album Power Corruption and Lies. The code was supposed to say "Blue Monday" but due to an error it actually reads "X96." The sleeve was so expensive to produce that Factory Records lost 5p (about £0.05 / 30p accounting for 1983 values) on every single copy sold — and Blue Monday went on to sell 3 million copies, the biggest-selling 12-inch single ever, generating a net loss of approximately £9,000 on the artwork alone. "New Order and Factory actually lost 30 pints on every single copy they sold." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JdSUHkXM1mQ
**Phil Smith – Oasis Roadie** : Phil Smith was a roadie for Oasis who, together with sound guy Mark Coyle, brought a blow-up globe to the "Definitely Maybe" album cover photoshoot. This prop was included as a visual representation of the band's collective ambition for "world domination." "Mark Coil, the sound guy for Oasis, and a roadie named Phil Smith found it and brought it along to signal that the bang was bound for world domination." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_tbKuJR0cPs
**Phoenix – Either Named After a Daft Punk Song or After a Band Member's Cleft Palate Scar** : Two theories: the name comes from a song on Daft Punk's Homework album; or one of the band members was born with a cleft palate that required surgery, leaving a scar similar to actor Joaquin Phoenix's scar. **Pink Duck Studios - Josh Homme's Recording Space** : Pink Duck Studios in Burbank, owned by Josh Homme, is described as having an unassuming exterior, resembling "an old corner store with the door blocked up" from the front. **Plagiarism Definition** : Plagiarism is defined as "the act of appropriating someone else's work and passing it off as your own." "That's plagiarism. The act of appropriating someone else's work and passing it off as your own." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rfObVld9rIE
**Plato's Philosophy on Music and Societal Change** : Plato held that alterations in "news and rhythms in music" invariably lead to changes in the "entire fabric of society." He cautioned that new musical forms, though seemingly harmless diversions, creep in imperceptibly, gradually spreading into manners and pursuits, eventually attacking laws and the Constitution with impudence, ultimately overthrowing public and private life. Plato personally disliked slow music, believing it fostered "laziness and sloth," and fast music, as he thought it hindered "sober contemplation." "News and rhythms in music are never altered without producing changes in the entire fabric of society." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE

**Pogues – Short for the Irish Gaelic Phrase "Pog Mahon," Meaning Kiss My Ass** : The name is an abbreviation of the Gaelic phrase "póg mo thóin," which translates as "kiss my ass." "Which translates as Kiss My Ass." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Polyvinyl Chloride (PVC) Properties and Environmental Impact** : Polyvinyl chloride (PVC) is the third most popular plastic globally, with applications ranging from bottles and plastic cards to plumbing products, having been used in sewer pipes since the 1920s. Most PVC is produced in China and Southeast Asia. PVC production is a byproduct of fossil fuels. In its raw, brittle state, it requires stabilizing chemicals known as plasticizers, which historically included toxic substances like lead and cadmium. Carbon is added to make the plastic black. As plastic, vinyl is non-biodegradable and records in landfills can leach hazardous chemicals for centuries. Melting old records is costly and releases highly toxic hydrogen chloride gas, a significant environmental problem given the billions of records produced since 1948 (e.g., 160 million kilos of PVC for records in a typical 1970s year). "Polyvinyl chloride is plastic. It's the third most popular type of plastic ever." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B2g4QSREzpw
**Polyvinyl Chloride (PVC) Shortage (2020 onwards)** : A global shortage of polyvinyl chloride (PVC) began in 2020, primarily due to supply chain disruptions caused by the pandemic. While increased online record sales and backed-up pressing plants contributed, a major factor in the shortage was the surging demand for plastic containers used by take-out restaurants. "Starting in 2020, the world suffered a shortage of polyvinyl chloride because of supply chain issues during the pandemic." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B2g4QSREzpw
**Pop Music Disruptions History** : Every ten years or so, significant events disrupt the pop music landscape. This pattern traces back to the 1950s with the birth of rock (initially dismissed as a fad), continued with The Beatles and the rise of the album in the 1960s, the emergence of Punk in the 1970s, the ascent of Hip Hop and Rap alongside music video channels in the 1980s, and the Alt Rock explosion of the 1990s. "every ten years or so, something happens to disrupt everything." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=raRCZ0Y5up8
**Pop Music Dominance in 2000** : By the end of 2000, "vacuous pop music had taken over the universe," selling hundreds of millions of CDs, with rap and hip hop in second place, and rock struggling, leading to a grim prognosis for the genre. "When the dust cleared at the end of 2000, it was very clear that vacuous pop music had taken over the universe." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MK7L0eCpDHc

**Pop Punk as a Juxtaposition** : The term "Pop Punk" itself is highlighted as a contradictory combination of words. This is because punk music was originally conceived as an "attack on pop," making their eventual fusion somewhat incongruous. "Pop, punk. But those words should not go together. Punk was originally created as an attack on pop." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pE7TaWSUa-o

**Portugal. The Man – A Period Separating the Collective (Portugal) from the Individual (The Man)** : The period separating "Portugal" and "The Man" symbolically separates the many (a country full of people, like a band of multiple members) from the individual (a specific person, like each band member). The name was intended to feel larger than life. "The period that we see between Portugal and the man is to separate the many from the one." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Possible Combinations of 12 Notes (Once Each)** : According to Frank Barons, who wrote in the Arts Times in 2004, there are 479,160,000 possible combinations if you play the 12 notes of the chromatic scale just once each. This figure highlights the vast but finite number of basic musical sequences available. "A quick bit of factoring... reveals that there are 479 million 1,600 possible combinations of those 12 notes. If you just play them once each, 479 million combinations." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=L09R2evjyMc
**Possible Combinations of Notes (with Durations)** : When accounting for the various ways a single note can be played (e.g., whole, half, quarter, eighth, sixteenth, thirty-second notes), the number of possible note combinations expands exponentially to just over one quintillion (a one followed by 18 zeros). This illustrates the immense complexity and theoretical diversity in musical composition. "Something just north of one quintillion possible combinations. That's a one followed by 18 zeros, one quintillion." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=L09R2evjyMc
**Post-2010 Influences on Pop Punk Tone** : The "darker" tone observed in the "new generation of pop punk bands" emerging after 2010 is speculated to be a possible consequence of significant societal events such as the "2008 financial crisis or the election of Donald Trump." "Today, the biggest deals in the music business involve well capitalized companies who are buying up the catalogs and publishing rights of major artists." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM

**Post-Punk Era Musical Diversity** : The post-punk era, immediately following the punk rock explosion of the 1970s, witnessed a significant "blossoming of all kinds of new and interesting music." **Post-Punk Explosion of the Late 70s and Early 80s** : This era followed the original punk rock explosion, serving as a "great musical decluttering" and attitude shift towards DIY. It resulted in a "big bang" for alternative music, unleashing chain reactions of new ideas, sounds, attitudes, fashion, and belief systems. This period laid "so many of the basic foundations of the music that we hear today," giving rise to genres like New Wave, Techno Pop, Industrial, Goth, and Ska. "We now look back on this as the great post punk explosion of the late 70s and early 80s, an era that created so many of the basic foundations of the music that we hear today." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LgJ7ww2AgF4
**Post-Punk Segmentation** : In the early and mid-1980s, while major labels still controlled most of the music market, the market share for independent music steadily increased. "But started in the punk years just kept gaining in momentum. Let's stay in the UK for a bit. The left of center slash underground stuff that was being released by the indie labels kept on coming. **Power Soaks** : Power soaks were devices developed to allow guitarists to emulate the sound of big, loud amplifiers while still using a small amplifier at a low volume. This addressed the issue of achieving desirable distortion from overdriven vacuum tubes without ear-splitting volume, making practice and performance in small spaces more feasible. "These became known as power soaks." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iGav9uJwA_w
**Pre-Artwork Record Packaging (1909-1938)** : For three decades following Odeon's 1909 innovation of bundling records, all records were sold in plain paper sleeves, typically with minimal text. These early "phonograph albums" were largely anonymous, consisting of simple paperboard bindings without any decorative or photographic artwork. "For the next 30 years, all records were sold in plain paper sleeves." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_tbKuJR0cPs
**Pre-CanCon Canadian Radio Bias – The Guess Who Had to Pretend to Be British (1965)** : In January 1965, Canadian band Chad Allan and the Expressions recorded "Shakin' All Over" on Quality Records. Quality Records knew Canadian radio would not add it because stations only played Canadian songs after they had become US hits. The label shipped 17 singles to stations across Canada with no band name listed — just a question mark reading "Guess Who?" — implying it was a mystery British band. The ruse worked. When stations realized in mid-March 1965 they had been tricked into playing a Canadian group, the name had already stuck. The band later officially became The Guess Who. "Quality purposely left the name of the group off the record." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-JWO_jYXwEM
**Pre-Internet Music Era Characteristics (Pre-2000)** : The pre-internet music era (before 2000) was characterized by peak industry revenues, bustling record stores, the crucial role of MTV and MuchMusic in artist development, the possibility of acts filling stadiums, and record labels' long-term investment in artists, often over several albums, with radio hits guaranteeing success. "The industry revenues were peaking at all time highs. Record stores were busy places, MTV and much music were very important to breaking an act." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Pre-Internet Music Leaks** : In earlier times, before widespread internet access, the creation, manufacturing, and distribution of records were tightly controlled, making it relatively easy to prevent leaks. Marketing, press, and tour schedules could be carefully synchronized for maximum impact, and any rare leaks, usually from inside jobs at studios or pressing plants, were manageable. "Now, in olden times, when the creation, manufacturing, and distribution processes were so tightly controlled, it was easy to keep a record under wraps until the label let it out." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vt6DVj7S6nk
**Pre-Internet Music News** : Before the internet, news traveled slowly and was heavily filtered, often stripping out or drastically altering information. This was particularly evident around sensitive events like the deaths of figures such as Kurt Cobain and Michael Hutchence, leading to much confusion, speculation, and conspiracy theories. "News traveled slowly and often passed through many filters." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=23OgreyK66o
**Pre-Internet Music Research** : Before the internet became widespread in 1996, researching music was a manual and costly endeavor. The speaker personally spent around $3,000 annually on magazines, as an independent contractor unable to expense them. Additionally, radio stations maintained libraries of press clippings and press releases from record labels, alphabetized by artist, serving as the primary source of information. "Well, what we would do is, you know, I would go and at one point I was buying, and because I was an independent contractor, as you'll recall, I didn't get to expense anything. So I was buying $3,000 worth of magazines every year." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90
**Pre-SoundScan Chart Compilation (Pre-March 1, 1991)** : Before March 1, 1991, weekly album charts were compiled based on "merely estimates." Billboard magazine would gather verbal sales reports from "a select group of record stores," then extrapolate this data across the country for its top 200 chart, a method acknowledged as highly susceptible to "mistakes, lies, bribery, in all manner of manipulation." "Up until February 28, 1991, album sales were merely estimates. Billboard magazine, the keeper of the charts, would phone around to a select group of record stores and get verbal reports of what albums were selling." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pE7TaWSUa-o
**Precursors to "Jackass" Stunts** : Hugh Dillon recalled engaging in dangerous and reckless activities like "bumper hitching" with Frankie Venom during their youth, stunts that predated and resembled the actions later popularized by the television show "Jackass." "before Jackass was invented. We were playing Jackass." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zBd13KtYlAA
**Predominance of Older Guitar Buyers** : Currently, the majority of guitars being bought and sold are acquired by older players, with their numbers decreasing annually. "Most guitars today are being bought and sold by older players, and there are fewer and fewer of them each year." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=oLC49nCf0ZM

**Pressure for Vinyl Production** : It requires between 100 and 150 tons of pressure to transform a lump of raw vinyl into a playable record. "It takes between 100 and 150 tons of pressure to squeeze a lump of raw vinyl into a playable record." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=72Lei7uug8c
**Prevalence of Stand-up Sitcoms in 1995** : In 1995, all six broadcast networks, including the newer WB and UPN, had at least one show featuring a comic in a central role. ABC notably had seven of its 15 sitcom slots filled by stand-up shows, including *Roseanne*, *Home Improvement*, *Grace Under Fire*, *All-American Girl*, *Allen*, *Hanging with Mr. Cooper*, and *On Our Own*. Meanwhile, Fox aired a George Carlin sitcom and *Martin*, while NBC had *Mad About You*, *The Nannies* (mummies), and *Seinfeld*. "In 1995, all six broadcast networks, including the WB and UPN, had at least one show with a comic front and center." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6O5TCTO-go4
**Private Jet Crash (September 21, 2008)** : Travis Barker (Blink 182) and DJ AM were the sole survivors of a private Learjet crash on this date, which occurred during takeoff, slamming into a fence and exploding, resulting in severe burns for Travis. "Travis and his buddy DJ Am were the only two survivors of a jet plane crash." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=yR3xc3ra5tE
**Pro Rata Payment Model – Drake Gets Paid from Jazz Fans' Subscriptions** : Spotify does not pay artists based on who specifically listened to them. Instead, artists are paid based on their percentage of overall streams in a given month. If Drake accounts for X percent of all streams, he receives X percent of all subscription revenue — regardless of who subscribed or why. This means a jazz fan's subscription money does not go to Miles Davis; it goes into a collective pool that flows primarily to whoever dominates the stream count. Small-audience artists with loyal but numerically limited fan bases are effectively squeezed out. "Musicians that used to have a small but loyal fan base are now making next to nothing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MQ7PDi-D9Ig
**Pro Tools Software Overview** : Pro Tools, a digital audio workstation, emerged as the standard recording software in most studios, originally conceived by students at the University of California at Berkeley in 1989 and launched in 1991. Initially costing $6,000 for a four-track system, it now offers extensive capabilities, including waveform visualization, cutting, pasting, and infinite sound tweaking, enabling precise correction of vocal errors, rhythmic lags, or incorrect notes. It has made recording significantly easier, though it can also serve as "compensation for a lack of talent," allowing for less precise initial performances. GarageBand, Audacity, and Adobe Edition are its technological descendants. "Most studios use pro tools, which is pretty much the standard for recording software." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7Zniri9uSlc
**Professor Dieter Selzer's Patent Rejection** : Professor Dieter Selzer's 1980s patent application for his "digital jukebox" concept, which involved storing and transmitting all music via telephone lines, was rejected. The examiner deemed the proposal "impossible," stating, "It'll never work." "Selzer applied for a patent, but it was rejected on the grounds that the examiner decided that what he proposed was impossible." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Progressive Networks** : Founded by ex-Microsoft employee Rob Glazer in 1994, Progressive Networks developed the Real Audio system, a proprietary technology for streaming audio in real-time over the internet. This company was a pioneer in early internet broadcasting. "Rob Glazer, an ex-Microsoft employee who created a company called Progressive Networks in 1994." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Proliferation of Peer-to-Peer File Sharing Sites** : Following Napster's success, numerous other peer-to-peer file-sharing sites emerged, including Scour, Qtmx, Freenet, Imesh, Bear Share, Edonkey, Audio Galaxy, Rapstar, Rockstar, Limewire, and Kazaa. This proliferation significantly amplified the scale of unauthorized music distribution. "There were dozens of other peer-to-peer file sharing sites. It was Scour and Qtmx and Freenet and Imesh, Bear Share, Edonkey, Audio Galaxy, Rapstar, Rockstar, Limewara, Kazah, endless list of these things." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Promoter Test Riders** : Many bands incorporate unusual or seemingly trivial requests into their riders, such as Van Halen's brown M&M's clause or Queens of the Stone Age's map of Ireland, as a test. These clauses help determine whether a promoter has thoroughly read the entire document, indicating their attention to detail and likelihood of fulfilling more critical requirements. "This was a test to see if the promoter actually read through the entire document, which is something that had happened far too few times in the past, resulting in, well, let's just call them fractious relations." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=z2hvUDtBxho
**Propaganda Magazine** : This magazine was considered a "Goth Bible for a while" and played a role in formalizing aspects of Goth culture. "the biggest of which was probably propaganda." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=evlGhfUe6QQ
**Proposed Shocking Mobile Phones (London)** : A design firm in London once proposed the concept of mobile phones that would deliver a shock to their owners. This mechanism would be activated if the phone detected that the user was speaking too loudly during a call. "A design firm in London once proposed phones, mobile phones, that would shock their owners if the phone perceived the owner was talking too loud." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aSk1XQHNkd8
**Psychic Link in Rhythm Sections** : The most effective drum and bass combinations are characterized by a "psychic link" between the players, allowing their styles and timing to be seamlessly complimentary. This connection ensures that once the beat and groove begin, everything flows and falls into place, whether they are tight and accurate or have a relaxed feel. "The drummer and the bass player have some kind of psychic link so that once the beat and the groove starts, everything just flows and everything just falls into place." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CVPPymc_qrk
**Psychological Link: Introverts as Front Persons** : Psychologists theorize that introverted musicians often excel as band front persons. This is because shy musicians tend to be more attuned to a crowd's energy, which enables them to establish a closer and more authentic connection with the audience. "psychologists say that introverts often make the best front persons for bands. Why? Well because shine musicians tend to pick up on the crowd's energy and can create a closer, more authentic connection with the audience." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aSk1XQHNkd8
**Psychopathy and Music Taste Study (NYU)** : A study conducted by psychology professor Pasco Walsh at New York University involved 190 students who completed psychopathy tests and then rated over 100 unfamiliar songs across various genres. The study found that students with psychopathic tendencies strongly preferred songs like Eminem's "Lose Yourself," Blackstreet's "No Diggity," and Justin Bieber's "Boyfriend" (likely "Do What You Mean"). Conversely, they disliked songs such as Dire Straits' "Money for Nothing," The Knack's "My Sharona," and classical music. "Psychopathic trending students really dug M&M's lose yourself, black streets no diggity, and Justin Bieber's do what you mean." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aSk1XQHNkd8
**Punched Card Data Tabulation for US Census (1860, 18xx Census)** : Herman Hollerith, born in Buffalo in 1860, developed an ingenious system to tabulate US Census data using cards with holes punched in them. This innovation drastically reduced the time required for census completion, enabling the 18xx Census (likely 1890 based on historical context) to be finished in just three months, a massive improvement from the previous 10-year timeframe. "Hollerith figured out a way to tabulate all the data using cards with holes punched in them." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PNiL63fY1Y8
**Purpose of Art Context Podcast** : The podcast "Art Context" aims to give "amazing creative artists" from the music video world the recognition they deserve. The hosts believe these directors create some of the "most impactful content on the planet" and seek to uncover their stories, influences, highs, lows, and breakthrough moments, providing a "close set behind experience" of the music video production process. "I feel like we live in the world where we don't give these amazing creative artists the flowers they deserve." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LgJ7ww2AgF4
**Putamen and Movement to Music** : The putamen, an area of the brain responsible for processing rhythm, body movement, and coordination, becomes active when music-generated dopamine flows into it. This often results in a spontaneous need to move with the music, such as tapping a foot, banging a beat, or dancing, as the body instinctively synchronizes. "Once music-generated dopamine gets into this area of the brain, we may feel a spontaneous need to move with the music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Pythagoras and the Institutionalization of Music (c. 570 BC)** : Pythagoras, known for his mathematical contributions, is considered arguably the most important figure in the history of music for institutionalizing musical sounds. Around 570 BC, he sought to bring order to the unconstrained and undefined state of music, using math and science to coordinate and confine musical notes and tuning. His work forms the basis for distinguishing melody from noise and underpins virtually all music today. "But Pythagoras was also arguably the most important person in the history of music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**Pythagorean Tuning System** : Pythagoras developed a fundamental tuning system based on mathematical ratios by experimenting with string lengths. He observed that a string half the length of another produced a tone exactly twice as high, leading to the organization of tones using a 3:2 ratio. This mathematically pure system became the foundational method for tuning instruments and composing Western music, influencing intonations and scales. "And Pythagorean tuning became the basis for tuning instruments and thus composing music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**Pythagorean Tuning in Western Music History** : Pythagorean tuning was the dominant and almost exclusive method for tuning Western music from around 570 BC until the early 1500s. Although Western music began to experiment with and move beyond this tuning by the 1800s, Pythagoras's foundational argument that music should be based on mathematics profoundly influenced all subsequent musical development, laying the groundwork for the music listened to today. "In fact it was pretty much the only accepted way of tuning for Western music until the beginning of the 1500s." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**Python Programming for Songwriting** : Rivers Cuomo hired programmers who used Python to organize his lyrical data in a highly granular way for the "Pacific Daydream" album, tagging everything with specific attributes. He later learned Python himself to create his "Drive Times" app. "In case you're wondering, the programmers did everything in Python." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=LYRPxtP61JM
**Queen Mary University Chills Playlist** : Queen Mary University in London compiled an extensive Spotify playlist featuring 700 songs that were found to be most likely to create a chills and/or goosebumps response in listeners. Their research highlighted that sadder, slower, less intense, and more instrumental songs were generally the most effective in inducing these physiological reactions. "Queen Mary University in London went so far as to create a Spotify playlist of the 700 songs, most likely to create a chills and or goosebumps response in people." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Queens of the Stone Age – Chris Goss Suggested Changing "Kings" to "Queens"** : Producer Chris Goss of Masters of Reality suggested the name during recording sessions. The band had been considering "Kings of the Stone Age." Goss's argument: "queens" implied they were heavy enough for boys and sweet enough for girls. "Which seems to have worked." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Quentin Tarantino's Songwriting Credit** : Quentin Tarantino received 37% of all royalties and a songwriting credit for Fun Lovin' Criminals' "Scooby Snacks" because the song featured multiple samples from his movies "Reservoir Dogs" and "Pulp Fiction." "And when Tarantino heard the song, he called his lawyers and demanded 37% of all royalties and a songwriting credit, which he got." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZcF5JMhBj2M
**R.E.M. – Michael Stipe Randomly Pulled It From a Dictionary** : The band needed a name before their first gig at a church in Athens, Georgia. Michael Stipe opened a dictionary at random and pulled out REM, which stands for Rapid Eye Movement and relates to dreaming. For the band, the letters don't stand for anything. "Singer Michael Stipe just randomly pulled it out of a dictionary." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Rabena – Photography Prop** : Rabena is a British soft drink that was intentionally diluted and used as a prop in place of real red wine for the "Definitely Maybe" album cover photoshoot. This creative decision was made because actual red wine tends to appear black in photographs, whereas the diluted Rabena successfully mimicked the visual appearance of red wine. "It's a British soft drink called Rabina that was diluted just enough to look like red wine because if you photograph real wine, it tends to look black in the photographs." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_tbKuJR0cPs
**Radio "Power Gold" Song Categories** : Rock radio stations, in addition to current "power" songs, often have a "power gold" category. These are songs typically over two years old that have been established as all-time favorites through rigorous audience research. Such songs might be played five to eight times a week, depending on the station's audience and philosophy. "A rock station will have a power gold category or something like it. These are songs usually more than two years old that have established themselves as all time favorites with the station's audience, something that's determined through rigorous audience research and testing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Radio Broadcasting Shift in Late 1940s/Early 1950s** : The emergence of television caused major networks (NBC, CBS, Mutual) to pivot away from radio programming, leaving hundreds of local radio stations without content. This led to a major shift where stations, seeking cheap and fast solutions, began hiring DJs to play popular records, moving radio's focus from dramas and variety shows to music and aiding the mixing of R&B, Blues, Country, and Western into rock and roll. "The networks began to pivot away from cross-country radio program to cross-country TV program." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hQJ3r-DCoMQ
**Radio Call Letter Conventions – Why Canadian Stations Begin With C, US East Is W, West Is K** : Radio call letters function as a station's license plate. In Canada, all station call signs must begin with the letter C, with the second letter being F, H, I, J, or K (e.g., CFTO, CHUM, CKCO). Most Canadian stations have four letters; the few three-letter stations (e.g., CKX Brandon) date from the 1920s and 1930s. In the US, stations east of the Mississippi must begin with W; stations west of it must begin with K — with historical exceptions grandfathered in from before the rule change. "Why do all Canadian radio stations have call letters that begin with the letter C?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JvOEAzmC6l0
**Radio Ratings vs. Artistic Fulfillment** : While extended mixes and diverse playlists were artistically fulfilling for 80s alt-rock radio staff, they were detrimental to ratings. Commercial radio relies on appealing to the largest possible audience for extended periods, and for many, this means easily singable songs, not necessarily "good music" in the hardcore fan sense. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Radio Station Hijack in Malmö, Sweden** : A radio station in Malmö, Sweden, experienced a signal hijack for half an hour. During this time, someone managed to repeatedly play an English-language ISIS recruiting song over the airwaves. "A radio station in Malmo Sweden had their signal hijacked for half an hour this year by someone who managed to play an English language ISIS recruiting song on repeat." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=aSk1XQHNkd8
**Radio as a Source of Real-time Information (Pre-Internet)** : Before the widespread adoption of the internet (prior to 1996), radio was the primary and often sole source for real-time information. Record labels and international contacts, such as Lee Carter in the UK, would feed stations the latest music information weeks before music magazines arrived in Canadian stores. "radio at that time was where everyone went to get real-time information." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bI6TTA-fn7c
**Radio's Impact on Wired Music Services** : The invention of radio ultimately led to the demise of the Tiatrophone/Electrophone service in 1931. Radio's ability to transmit audio wirelessly, without the need for extensive physical telephone lines running to individual homes, made it a superior and more convenient technology for accessing music. "This lasted a long time, too, all the way to 1931, in fact, and the thing that killed it, radio, which required no wires running all over the place." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Rage Against the Machine – A 1979 Chevy Van That Kept Breaking Down, or Political Metaphor** : The phrase "Rage Against the Machine" was used in a punk fanzine called No Answers in 1989 by a writer covering the pre-RATM band Inside Out, which featured Zack de la Rocha. Conventional wisdom holds that "the machine" represents oppressive capitalism. However, de la Rocha once noted literally: the band's constant-breakdown 1979 Chevy van was the thing they raged against, taking sledgehammers to it when they finally had money to buy a new one. "So the machine that they were raging against was 1979 Chevy van." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Rainbow Butt Monkeys (later Finger Eleven) – Joke Name for a High School Band That Got a Record Deal** : Named as a joke because no one expected the high school band to amount to anything. After signing to a label and releasing four EPs and an album under that name, they changed to Finger Eleven — but Rainbow Butt Monkeys artifacts remain in existence. "They picked it as a joke because there was no way their high school band would amount to anything." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Ramones – Paul McCartney Once Checked Into Hotels as "Paul Ramone"** : When the Beatles were touring, Paul McCartney sometimes checked into hotels under the pseudonym Paul Ramone. That name was good enough for the Ramones. "When the Beatles were touring, Paul McCartney would often sign into hotels as Paul Ramone." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Ramones' First Gig Sound** : At their debut performance at CBGB on August 16, 1974, the Ramones' sound was described by scene-ster Ligs McNeil as "just this wall of noise." Their appearance, featuring leather jackets, t-shirts, torn jeans, and Converse high-tops, struck him as "completely new" and distinctly non-hippie. "And it was just this wall of noise. They look so striking. These guys were not hippies. This was something completely new." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=j8uk7BnbXwU
**Ranking Methodology** : Ranking for alt-rock one-hit wonders involved consulting alt-rock radio charts over decades to create a list of around 100 candidates. Then, Spotify plays and YouTube views were summed, and a power ranking scale from 1 to 10 (created by "Walter the Mathematician") was assigned for "one-hit wonder-ness." "I looked up the number of Spotify plays and YouTube views. Those two numbers were added together." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZcF5JMhBj2M
**Rationale for Radio Song Repetition** : Radio stations repeatedly play popular songs to cater to listeners who tune in for short durations (e.g., 10-20 minutes). Since listeners cannot customize their playlists, frequent repetition increases the chance that any individual tuning in will hear a song they like, thereby maximizing audience satisfaction and retention. "So the only way to make sure as many people as possible here, the biggest and most popular songs is to play those songs more often, thereby increasing the chances that any individual when they tune in will hear in what they're hoping for." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Real Audio Development** : Rob Glazer, an ex-Microsoft employee, founded Progressive Networks in 1994, viewing the internet as a new broadcasting system. His team created Real Audio, a proprietary system designed to stream audio in real-time and from dedicated servers, pioneering internet audio delivery. "He and his team created a proprietary system called Real Audio, which was designed to stream audio in both real-time and from a dedicated server." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Real Grooves vs. Machine-Made** : The discussion emphasizes the value of "real grooves" created by human rhythm sections, distinguishing them from those "made with a machine or cooked up on Pro Tools." A skilled rhythm section can elevate even an average band into something truly special. "And we're talking real grooves too, nothing made with a machine or cooked up on Pro Tools." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CVPPymc_qrk
**Real Networks** : Real Networks is the later name for Rob Glazer's pioneering company, Progressive Networks. It eventually acquired Rhapsody, which later rebranded itself as Napster. "And then it was bought by Real Networks, which was, of course, the new name for Rob Glazer's progressive networks." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Real-Time Data Analytics in Music Industry** : Streaming platforms generate vast amounts of data, enabling unprecedented real-time identification of music trends and career opportunities; record labels now have internal analytics departments, and specialized companies assist musicians in tracking global song performance and consumption. "The insane amount of data that can be harvested from the streaming platforms makes it possible to identify trends and opportunities in ways never before possible." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Reasons for Catalog Sales (Older Artists)** : Older artists, particularly those in their 60s or 70s, sell their catalogs for various reasons: to cash out and enjoy retirement, to address financial needs, concerns about future touring revenue (exacerbated by COVID-19), or a struggle to accept declining record sales in the streaming era. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Reasons for Music Licensing** : Artists increasingly pursue music licensing opportunities (for commercials, TV shows, movies, video games) as a crucial replacement for lost revenue. Factors like crashing physical music sales, inadequate income from touring or streaming, and global events such as pandemics have driven musicians to find alternative income streams. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Reasons for Slam Dancing's Emergence** : Several factors contributed to the rise of slam dancing: it was a rejection of "hippie" culture, it served as a defiant response to the prevalent disco and "Saturday Night Fever" culture, and it offered an outlet for aggressive expression, particularly among young men. Bands sometimes actively provoked audiences to increase the intensity. "But slam dancing is something hippies would not do." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KMx4bmq8o2Y
**Rebecca Schaefer Murder by John Bardo (Year not given)** : Actress Rebecca Schaefer, 21, was stalked for three years by John Bardo, who eventually murdered her by shooting her at point-blank range in Los Angeles. His obsession escalated after seeing her in a movie scene in bed with another actor, believing she needed to be "punished for becoming another Hollywood whore." "Rebecca Schaefer was having a good life. She was 21 years old and already had a run on a CBS sitcom called My Sister Sam." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FtGJHhqXcDI
**Recent Musician Plane Crash Fatalities (Post-2000)** : The incidence of musician deaths in plane crashes has drastically decreased since the turn of the millennium. Notable, though infrequent, incidents include singer and actress Aaliyah, who died in a twin-engine Cessna crash in the Bahamas in 2001. That same year, Melanie Thornton of the group LaBouche perished in a Crossair plane crash in Switzerland. In 2009, two members of Chuck Mangione's band were killed in a commuter plane crash outside of Buffalo. "The last big name to die in a small plane crash was Alia, the singer in actress. That was a twin-engine Cessna in the Bahamas in 2001." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dgzF_KBSQWM
**Record Collecting and Valuation** : The value of a collectible record or CD depends on its condition, rarity, and market demand. A unique item, like a one-of-a-kind purple vinyl, might be worthless if there's no demand. Historically, prices were set by dealers and collectors at record fairs, and guides like Record Collector and Goldmine (Record Collector still active) provided pricing. The internet, particularly sites like eBay, gemm.com, and 991.com, has made valuation easier but has also caused prices for some items to spike dramatically. Collectors are advised to be aware of "buyer beware" situations where online prices might be inflated compared to established guides. "See how much a record is worth is dependent on its condition, its rarity, and how much demand there is for it in the marketplace." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zUQ2vZzmRiI
**Record Collector Obsession** : Engaging in record collecting can become an "expensive obsession," metaphorically described as being "sucked into a very, very deep rat hole." "if you get into record collecting, you could end up being sucked into a very, very deep rat hole where a hobby becomes an obsession, a very expensive obsession." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IIJySSo276k
**Record Condition Factors** : The price of any used record is directly affected by its physical condition, encompassing both the packaging (e.g., absence of marks, water damage, written names, and the presence of all original inserts) and the vinyl itself (e.g., free from scratches, scuffs, warping, or a misshapen spindle hole). "The price of any used record also depends on its physical condition, both in terms of the packaging and the vinyl itself." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IIJySSo276k
**Record Industry Sales Crisis and Home Taping (Late 1970s - Early 1980s)** : The record industry faced a major sales crisis in the late 1970s and early 1980s, triggered by the burst of the disco bubble, which caused record sales to enter "free fall." The industry identified "home taping" – people copying albums onto cassettes for friends – as the primary problem. "Last time the record industry found themselves facing a major sales crisis was in the late 1970s and the early 1980s." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2RKchFW42Jc
**Record Industry's Emphasis on Songs vs. Albums** : The recorded music industry, struggling with the breakdown of old physical sales models, shifted focus to individual songs and their placement on playlists rather than nurturing artists over multiple albums. This "WAM-BAM Thank You MAM" speed makes it harder for new acts to develop, affecting all genres. "There's been a bigger emphasis on individual songs and where they fit on a Spotify playlist than there is for an album that might be promoted over two or three or even four years." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5Y6nHw5xx88
**Record Label Streaming Revenue (Mid-2017)** : In mid-2017, record labels were collectively earning $150,000 USD every minute from streaming. "In mid-2017, we learned that the labels were making a hundred and fifty thousand dollars US per minute from streaming." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Record Labels Phasing Out Singles** : Record labels, enjoying fantastic album profits, gradually phased out singles, coercing fans to buy full albums even if they only desired one song, a move described as "arrogant and cynical." "In fact, they were enjoying such fantastic profits that they gradually phased out singles." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Record Size Extremes – Largest: 50 cm (Europe 1900–1930); Smallest: 2-Inch Compilation; 16-Inch for Film/Radio** : The biggest records ever made were 50 centimeters (about 20 inches), seen in Europe between 1900 and 1930. Sixteen-inch records were used for movie soundtracks (the Vitaphone system) and radio transcription discs for pre-recorded programming before magnetic tape arrived in the 1940s. The smallest known records are 2 inches in diameter: one was a P-brain compilation of six bands each playing a 10-second song; the other was a 20-second hardcore song called "Soda Tax" by Two Minute Minor, protesting Cook County, Illinois accidentally imposing a tax on soft drinks. "The smallest record I know of has a diameter of just two inches." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=I291j5WBc4k
**Record Store Day Founding and Impact (2007)** : Record Store Day originated in 2007 from a meeting of independent record store owners in Baltimore who sought to revitalize their struggling businesses. Inspired by "Free Comic Book Day," they developed an event featuring special products and appearances to draw customers back to stores. The first Record Store Day in 2007 successfully spread worldwide, with hundreds of thousands of independent stores participating annually. Record labels recognized the marketing opportunity and joined with special, limited-edition vinyl releases, leading to the saving of numerous small shops and a significant increase in vinyl sales. "This led to the first record store day in 2007." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jD1dWxNLvfE
**Record Store Day Genesis (2008)** : The idea for Record Store Day originated from independent record store owners in Baltimore who were struggling due to digital music and piracy. Inspired by "comic book day," they conceived an annual event featuring free and exclusive products to attract customers, increase revenues, and boost vinyl sales. The first Record Store Day took place in 2008. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Record Store Day Gougers** : "Record Store Day gougers" are individuals who exploit the annual event by lining up early, or paying others to do so, to purchase limited edition stock specifically created for the day. Their intent is not personal enjoyment but rather to resell these items "for inflated prices on eBay," demonstrating a form of opportunistic entrepreneurship that disrupts the spirit of the event for genuine collectors. "These are the people who line up early on record store day or pay people to line up for them and then buy up all the limited edition stock created just for that day and then sell it all for inflated prices on eBay." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7Zniri9uSlc
**Record Store Day Scheduling and 2020 Changes** : Record Store Day is typically held on the third Saturday of April, with a secondary event scheduled for Black Friday in November. In 2020, due to the COVID-19 pandemic, the schedule was adjusted to include three Record Store Days in addition to the Black Friday sale. "Normally, record store day is held on the third Saturday of April with a secondary event scheduled for Black Friday in November." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jD1dWxNLvfE
**Record Store Growth and Great Depression Impact** : New record stores emerged throughout the 1920s, indicating a period of growth. However, this expansion was severely interrupted by the Great Depression, which caused an astonishing 95% drop in record sales between 1930 and 1932. The market eventually recovered, albeit slowly. "There was a big setback with a great depression, which saw sales dropped by an astounding 95% between 1930 and 1932." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jD1dWxNLvfE
**Record Store-Scented Candle from DW Campbell's** : A company called DW Campbell's now offers a candle designed to evoke the scent of a record store. The candle's fragrance is described as a blend of "press vinyl, warm woods, accented by notes of sweet blossoms, hints of amber and soft fruit." "You could now buy a record store-scented candle. It's from a company called DW Campbell's." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-N6IM5Nm5iw
**Recordings by Black Musicians on White-Owned Labels** : Throughout the 1910s and 1920s, many Black musicians were recorded by white-owned record labels. These recordings, released on 10-inch, 78 RPM records, gained widespread popularity across all audiences, highlighting the broad appeal of early Black music. "Through the 1910s and into the 1920s, many black musicians found themselves being recorded by white-owned record labels." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hQJ3r-DCoMQ
**Red Hot Chili Peppers vs. Red Hot Chili Pipers Mix-up** : A man from the UK purchased a ticket for approximately fifty dollars to see the Red Hot Chili Peppers perform in Dublin. Upon arrival, he was confused by the presence of numerous people wearing kilts, only to realize he had mistakenly bought a ticket to see the Red Hot Chili Pipers, a renowned bagpipes band. "He bought a ticket for around fifty bucks to see the Red Hot Chili Peppers play in Dublin. And when he got there, he was confused by all the people wearing kiltz." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GO0K_N7Ys7I

**Rediscovering "Missed" Music from Youth** : When current music loses its appeal, many adults revert to their "coming of age years" (14-24) to explore songs, albums, and artists they might have missed. This includes music that was "too radical and too different" or simply "fell through the cracks" due to the rapid absorption of new sounds. This material, though decades old, feels "new to you" and offers the familiar power and energy of that era. "So what do many of us do? We go back to those coming of age years between 14 and 24 and start exploring songs, albums, and artists that we missed the first time around." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Refusal of Christmas Visit** : He refused Michael Hutchence's request to allow his children with Paula Yates to visit Australia for Christmas, leading to a loud argument witnessed by a hotel guest in Hutchence's final hours. "But Geldoff refused." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=23OgreyK66o
**Reginald Fessenden – Canadian-Born Engineer, First to Broadcast a Human Voice (1906)** : While Guglielmo Marconi is commonly credited with inventing radio, he actually invented the wireless telegraph, capable of sending Morse code but not voice or music. The first person to actually broadcast a human voice through the air was Reginald Fessenden, a Canadian-born engineer working in a lab near Washington, D.C., who achieved intelligible transmission as early as 1900. On December 24, 1906, from Brant Rock, Massachusetts, he presided over the first proper radio broadcast: he played a Handel piece on a phonograph, read from the Bible, and played "O Holy Night" on his violin. Atlantic sailors accustomed to Morse code were bewildered. Fessenden became simultaneously the first DJ, first radio performer, and first radio announcer. "In the space of those few minutes, Fessenden became the first DJ, the first radio performer, and the first radio announcer." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JvOEAzmC6l0
**Regional Goth Terminology** : Goth followers have different names in various regions: "Gogan" in Australia, "Ku Khoracha" in Spain, and "dark" in Italy. "If you're an Australian, you're a Gogan. In Spain, you might be called a Ku Khoracha. In Italy, the term is dark." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=evlGhfUe6QQ

**Repetitive Listening by Young Streamers** : Young users, who are the heaviest consumers of streaming services, frequently listen to their favorite songs on repeat, a behavior historically observed in youth (dating back to portable turntables and 45s) but now quantifiable through data analytics to inform the creation of new music designed to encourage similar repetition. "The heaviest users of streaming music services tend to skew young. They also tend to listen to their favorite songs over and over and over and over and over and over and over and over and over again." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Repetitive Listening's Impact on Charts and Payouts** : Repetitive listening by users propels songs up streaming charts and through algorithms, increasing their exposure and leading to more repeat listens, ultimately resulting in higher payouts for creators and greater profits for record labels. "Repetition then pushes the song up the streaming charts and up through the algorithms, so it's exposed to more people who also put it on repeat." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Republican Presidency and Rock Music Resurgence Theory** : Historically, the election of a Republican president, especially a polarizing one, has often correlated with young people responding through loud, angry rock music, as seen during the Nixon (1968), Reagan (1981), George H.W. Bush (1991), and George W. Bush (2001) administrations. However, this trend did not significantly materialize following Donald Trump's election in 2016, with only isolated examples. "usually whenever there's a Republican in the White House and the more polarizing and controversial, the better. Young people have traditionally responded to that, to that political and social circumstance with a lot more loud angry rock." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5Y6nHw5xx88
**Revenue Splitting in Licensing Deals** : When an artist licenses a song for third-party use, such as a movie trailer, the revenue generated usually needs to be split. This split occurs between the artist and any other entities, such as music publishers and record companies, who hold ownership stakes in pieces of the song. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Revolution Summer in D.C.** : The "Revolution Summer" was a period in the mid-1980s when hardcore bands in Washington D.C. actively sought to break free from the restrictive dogma that had traditionally limited the hardcore genre. "They became part of what is now remembered as the Revolution Summer when DC hardcore bands tried to break out of the dogma that had limited what hardcore could be." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=v_am7ifh7Pk
**Rhapsody Acquisition and Rebranding** : After its launch, Rhapsody was acquired by Real Networks (formerly Progressive Networks, founded by Rob Glazer). In November 2011, Rhapsody acquired the intellectual property of Napster. By 2016, Rhapsody fully rebranded itself as Napster, operating under that name today. "And then it was bought by Real Networks, which was, of course, the new name for Rob Glazer's progressive networks. Nobody still exists. Except that in November 2011, it bought what was left of Napster, all the intellectual property. And in 2016, Rhapsody completely rebranded itself as Napster, which is how it operates today." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw
**Rhapsody Development** : In 1999, a team created a program for Tune2.com, a customizable internet radio station, and developed a prototype of a "celestial jukebox" called Aladdin. In 2001, Listen.com purchased this technology, transforming Aladdin into Rhapsody, which launched on December 31, 2001, as the first modern on-demand streaming service offering an "all-you-can-eat buffet" of music for a flat monthly fee. "In 2001, all that tech was purchased by a company called Listen.com. And from there, Aladdin was transformed into the first modern on-demand streaming service, which was called Rhapsody." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw

"Things started to get better when he got a job as a janitor at a Cleveland recording studio called Right Track. Trent convinced the owner to let him record demos when the studio wasn't being used. **Rise of Indie Labels** : Beyond the three major record labels (Universal, Sony, and Warner), there are hundreds, even thousands, of independent labels that operate autonomously. These "indie labels" and their "indie artists" are considered unaffiliated with the big three, representing the underground, non-mainstream, experimental, daring, outlier, unusual, and non-conformist segments of the music industry. "But beyond those three companies are hundreds, thousands of labels that do their own thing. And because they are unaffiliated with the big three, we consider them to be independent." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VOv5mT1dJd8

However, the period of 2006-2007 also saw a slight opening up of musical variety within rock. "2005, the last year rock music peaked as far as our theory of rock versus pop cycles are concerned. **Rock vs. Pop Cycle Theory** : A theory posits that rock and pop music are in a cyclical "death struggle" that repeats every 13 years. Rock music rises in popularity and creativity, peaks, then declines, while pop music follows an inverse pattern, dropping as rock ascends and rising as rock falls. "That theory contends that rock and pop music are locked in a death struggle that plays itself out like clockwork every 13 years." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Rock vs. Pop Cycle Timeline (1951-2010)** : The rock versus pop cycle theory suggests four complete cycles have occurred since 1951. In 2010, the music world was in its fifth cycle, which began in the spring of 2003, with rock peaking in 2005 and hitting bottom in the preceding couple of years. "the rock versus pop cycle has played itself out through four complete cycles since 1951. If you want to know why, you don't have to go back and review chapter 14." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk

**Roger Daltrey's Flat Stomach – Caused by Talcum Powder Scarring from 1948 Surgery** : When Roger Daltrey was four years old, he swallowed a two-inch nail. Surgeons removed it by cutting him open; at the time (around 1948), surgical gloves were dusted with talcum powder, which was later discovered to cause significant scar tissue. Those scars are why Daltrey's stomach has remained so flat. "If you look up pictures of a shirtless Roger Daltrey, you'll see the scars." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fnZx8EGnszw

**Sampling Rate Theory (1928, 1949)** : The theory that a musical signal sampled at 44,100 times per second is indistinguishable to the human ear and brain from a smooth analog source was first proposed in a paper in 1928 and experimentally proven in 1949. This underpins the fidelity of compact disc audio. "This sampling rate theory was first discussed in a paper printed in 1928 and then proven experimentally in 1949." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D8GU8ZpSgY8

**Santana High School Shooting (2001)** : On March 5, 2001, 15-year-old Charles Andrew Williams, described as unpopular and bullied, carried out a shooting at Santana High School in Santee, California. He killed two students and wounded 13 others, influenced by Linkin Park songs "Papercut," "One Step Closer," and "In The End," even quoting "In the End" in a note to his father. "In 915 in the morning of March 5, 2001, a 15-year-old unpopular and uncool kid named Charles Andrew Williams went into the boys' bathroom at Santana High School in Santé, California." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FtGJHhqXcDI
**Sarajevo Cafe and World War I Trigger (April 1914)** : In April 1914, a newspaper clipping in a letter arrived at the Salat Number Runa cafe in Sarajevo, detailing Archduke Franz Ferdinand's upcoming visit on June 28th. This information prompted a terrorist group to plan his assassination, which Gavrilo Princip carried out, triggering World War I and fundamentally shaping the 20th century. "That assassination was the trigger for World War I and everything in the 20th century that followed." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qC0Ee4-dpnI
**Scalping Methods: "Diggers" and "ICE"** : Early ticket scalpers, often called "sidewalk men," used specific methods to obtain tickets. They would hire individuals, known as "diggers," to stand in line for them. Another tactic was "ICE," which involved bribing box office personnel for a share of the ticket proceeds. "Some would hire people to stand on the sidewalk in line for them, and these folks were called diggers." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=D8GU8ZpSgY8

**Scarcity of 21st Century Arena-Filling Rock Bands** : A challenge posed is to list rock bands that emerged since 2000 capable of drawing tens of thousands of fans to a single gig. The observation is that most acts still filling arenas or stadiums first appeared in the 1990s, 1980s, 1970s, or even 1960s, indicating a difficulty in creating new superstars in the current century. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
