**Scientific Evidence for Brain Benefits of Drumming** : A scientific publication from June 2020, titled "Drum Training Induces Long-Term Plasticity in the Sarah Bellum and Connected Cortical Tissues," and authored by thirteen researchers, concluded that playing the drums is beneficial for brain health. "The scientific publication, which was written by thirteen researchers, is entitled Drum Training Induces Long-Term Plasticity in the Sarah Bellum and Connected Cortical Tissues." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HoBx6s3JmVQ
**Scotland's Music Ban in Bars Due to COVID-19** : Scotland implemented a ban on playing music in bars and pubs, specifically to mitigate the spread of COVID-19. The reasoning was that music would cause patrons to lean in closer to hear each other, and this increased proximity would create a dangerous possibility of viral transmission. "Scotland banned music and bars and pubs for an odd reason. I think he was that if music was being played, people would have to lean into each other to be heard. And that close proximity created a dangerous possibility of transmission of COVID-19." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HoBx6s3JmVQ
**Scottish Bars Implement Low Volume Rule (2020)** : In 2020, Scottish bars implemented a rule to keep the volume low on all music and televisions. This measure was intended to prevent people from having to shout over noise, which authorities believed would help control the spread of COVID-19. "The volume had to be kept low on all music and all televisions so people wouldn't have to shout over the noise." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-N6IM5Nm5iw
**Sean Fanning and Napster's Transformative Launch (1999)** : Sean Fanning, while a college student at Northeastern University in Boston, developed Napster out of frustration with the cumbersome methods of sharing music files online. Using his uncle's laptop, Fanning coded the program, named after his "nappy hairstyle." On June 1, 1999, he shared it with friends, and within hours, Napster was "in the wild," ushering in the era of peer-to-peer file sharing and profoundly altering the music industry landscape. "On June 1st, 1999, he offered the program to some friends, saying, hey, this is pretty cool, but okay, keep it to yourself, all right?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PNiL63fY1Y8
**Seattle Karaoke Parlor Attack (Undated)** : An unnamed man at a Seattle karaoke parlor called "Change" was attacked by a woman from the audience who jumped on stage and punched him multiple times, asserting that his singing "sucked," requiring four people to pull her off him. "Just ask the guy in Seattle who was attacked by a woman at a Karyoki parlor called Change when he refused to stop singing this song." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dVJuITJyNTU
**Seattle Sound Characteristics** : The unique local hybrid rock sound in Seattle was sludgy, slow, and low, often as negative and pessimistic as nihilistic hardcore acts, yet with more introspective lyrics. The distinctive "look" of the Seattle bands—flannel and functional logging industry clothing from thrift shops—was unintentional, stemming from poverty rather than fashion. "Rock that was sludgy and slow and low. And often everybody's negative and pessimistic is some of the more nihilistic hardcore acts. And there was more. Some of the lyrics seem to be more introspective than usual." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sCtQqVBtCaI

**Second British Invasion (MTV-Fueled)** : MTV's demand for content led it to draw heavily from the UK's tradition of music films, pioneering a "second British invasion" of artists. These videos emphasized visual appeal and fashion, launching groups like ABC, Culture Club, and Duran Duran to North American prominence, though the transcript erroneously stated this growth occurred "through most of the 1960s" when MTV launched in 1981. "The result was what could be called a second British invasion." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bYsV3ozbk4M

**Selling Out Definition 1 - Major Label Signing** : This definition describes an artist as "selling out" when they sign with a major multinational music corporation after previously being cool and independent. The perception is that they become "part of the machine" and will be transformed into something bland for the mainstream. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Selling Out Definition 2 - Pursuit of Riches** : This definition states that a band becomes a sell-out when their music is primarily influenced by their pursuit of wealth, implying they will do "whatever it takes" to maximize their earnings, regardless of the artistic consequences. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Selling Out Definition 3 - Becoming Too Popular** : This definition considers a band a "sell-out" if they become excessively popular for some fans' comfort, selling too many records and concert tickets or appearing on too many magazine covers. Fans may feel their band has been "stolen" by new, trendy followers. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Selling Out Definition 4 - Music for Product Advertising** : This definition, considered "dodgiest" by some, labels a band as having "sold out" when their music is used to sell a product unrelated to music itself, such as cars, candy, or TVs. Even usage in a scene in a mainstream TV network show can be viewed with "derision" by some, dismissed as "filthy lucre." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk

**Service Charge Evolution (1990s)** : In the 1990s, service charges on concert tickets began to increase aggressively, encouraged by Ticketmaster, and became more uniform across different types of events, whereas previously, tickets for events like circuses had lower charges than concerts. Portions of these service charges were often rebated to the promoter and the venue. "However, in the 1990s, these charges started to creep up and the industry, encouraged by Ticketmaster, was pretty aggressive in boosting these charges for its services." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8q2bRZyHnHE
**Sesame Street Sued Over "Letter B" (1979) – Settled for $50** : In 1979, Sesame Street featured a song called "Letter B" sung to the tune of the Beatles' "Let It Be." It ran for several years before someone who had purchased the song's rights (not the Beatles themselves) filed a lawsuit. The suit was settled for a fine of $50. "It wasn't the Beatles who filed this suit, but someone who had purchased the rights to the song." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZbHRIh3RUoo
**Sex Pistols + Devo Merger (1978) – Richard Branson's Unrealized Idea** : When the Sex Pistols exploded in 1978, Richard Branson of Virgin Records had an idea: what if Johnny Rotten joined Devo as the band's new frontman, using the combination to break Devo in Europe? The plan never materialized. "What if that had?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fnZx8EGnszw
**Sex Pistols – Named After Manager Malcolm McLaren's Bondage Clothing Store "Sex"** : The Sex Pistols were essentially a manufactured punk boy band put together by Malcolm McLaren, who ran a bondage clothing store in London called Sex. He also liked the word "pistols" for its dangerous connotation. The name was "basically a living, breathing advertisement for his store." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Sexist Attitudes in 1967 Rock Scene** : In 1967, the idea of an all-female rock band, particularly one that wrote its own songs and featured women shredding guitars and playing drums, was considered radical. Despite early support from figures like Jimi Hendrix, traditional sexist attitudes prevailed, leading to the dissolution of bands like Ace of Cups by 1972, with the concept of a female-fronted rock band being dismissed as "silly" until the advent of punk rock. "Even in 1967, this was radical. Hendrix was so impressed by their chops that he invited them to open a couple of his shows. Those really did seem like some kind of defining moments. But then the old sexist attitudes took over." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Eo32mAZd8DI
**Seymour Stein (Record Executive) - Beijing Punk Club Visit** : During a music industry conference in Beijing, Seymour Stein, despite his age and using a cane, visited a punk club called D22 at 1 AM. He sat near the front, closing his eyes and listening for hours to various Chinese punk and alternative bands, demonstrating his enduring passion for discovering new talent. "Seymour found a stool near the front, closed his eyes, and listened to band after band performed Chinese punk and alternative. And he stayed that way for hours." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hjProJd_JrM
**Seymour Stein (Record Executive) - Legendary Career** : Seymour Stein is a legendary record executive, widely known as the founder of Sire Records. His career is marked by discovering and signing iconic artists such as The Ramones and Talking Heads, giving Madonna her "first proper record deal," and introducing significant English bands like The Smiths, The Pretenders, and The English Beat to the North American market. "Seymour is a legend." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hjProJd_JrM

Something's happening here. It's going to be big everywhere." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hjProJd_JrM

**Shelley Lynn and Tadah Catering** : Shelley Lynn owns Tadah Catering, the company that managed all the catering for the Warped Tour from its inception. **Shift from "Mash" to "Mosh" (Early 1980s)** : In the early 1980s, punk fanzines used the term "mash" (as in "mashed potatoes") to describe the frenzied activity in the pit. However, the pronunciation shifted to "Mosh," largely influenced by HR, the singer of Bad Brains, whose Jamaican accent made "mash" sound like "mosh" when he urged audiences to "mash it up." "But somehow the pronunciation shifted to Mosh." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KMx4bmq8o2Y
**Shift from Album Cycles to Continuous Singles Release** : The streaming world encourages artists to keep fans continuously engaged through a "steady, drip, drip, drip" of new songs, which is gradually replacing the traditional album cycle. This older model involved spending a year recording an album and then touring behind it for three years. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Shift from Physical to Streaming Media (2000s-2016)** : The early 2000s began with robust sales of physical music media, but the rise of the internet and piracy led to a drastic decline. After roughly 15 years of adaptation, the industry embraced streaming, leading to revenue growth starting in 2016. Today, streaming accounts for at least 75% of record label revenue, with platforms like Spotify boasting massive user bases and market capitalization. This shift has resulted in lower artist payouts compared to physical sales, forcing artists to diversify income through merch, touring, and licensing. It also created a top-heavy economic structure with many struggling artists. Streaming has influenced song composition (e.g., shorter intros to grab attention for the first 30 seconds to qualify for payouts) and fostered a "lean back listening" culture where music often serves as background "organized noise" rather than being actively engaged with, unlike the detailed experience of listening to a CD with artwork and liner notes. "revenues started to go up because the industry embraced streaming." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nX8uAFDzDYM
**Shift from Singles to Albums in the 1960s** : Following the 1967 release of The Beatles' *Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band*, the music industry's primary focus shifted from low-margin singles to high-margin albums, making the album the central product and generating significant revenue. "And from then on, the music industry's main focus was no longer on low margin singles, but on high margin albums." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Shift in Advertising Strategy** : The immense success of the Volkswagen "Milky Way" ad, particularly its use of an obscure artist, caused a significant shift in the advertising world. Agencies began to favor "cool songs by lesser known artists" in TV commercials, which in turn were "legitimately regarded as taste makers" and boosted sales for both products and, if the artists were alive, their concert tickets and merchandise. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Shifting Perceptions of "Selling Out" (Post-2000)** : Before 2000, an artist licensing their music for commercial products or services was widely considered a "giant sin," often leading to career-ending scorn and ridicule. However, the early 21st century saw a dramatic shift where licensing became an "essential part of any act's income stream." This change was driven by the decline in physical music sales (down 90% in 25 years) and the minimal income generated from streaming for most artists, making sync deals a crucial way to pay rent and survive. The financial environment for artists transformed dramatically, making licensing an aspiration rather than an insult. "Selling out isn't a bad thing anymore. In fact, it's something to aspire to." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xid8CZf4oYo
**Shifting Pop Punk Audience (Late 2000s)** : By the late 2000s, the original audience that had embraced pop punk since the mid-90s had "grown up and moved on." This demographic shift contributed to changes in the genre's landscape and mainstream presence. "Meanwhile, the pop punk audience that had been with this music scene since the middle 90s had grown up and moved on." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pE7TaWSUa-o
**Shifting Radio Programming Post-Grunge** : After grunge popularized alt-rock, industry magazines began compiling charts and monitoring airplay for the genre. This led program directors in smaller markets, like Des Moines, Iowa, to emulate playlists of major stations such as K-Rock in Los Angeles, leading to increased homogeneity rather than localized curation. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Shifting Stigma of Tattoos** : For many years, tattoos carried a significant stigma, often associated with "deviance and weirdos," or with specific groups like sailors, gangs, and the mafia. This perception began to change dramatically over the last 60 years, particularly since the early 21st century, with tattoos moving into the mainstream. "But even with all this, many people still consider tattoos to carry some kind of stigma, only deviance and weirdos get tattoos. But that's changed a lot in the last 60 years, especially since the beginning of the 21st century. Tattoos have long gone mainstream." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jZeMmPekKMQ

**Significance of "Hinge Points"** : Academics define "hinge points" as singular historical events that profoundly alter everything that follows, often with clear understanding in hindsight. The fall of the Berlin Wall is cited as a modern example of such an event with long-lasting effects. "History is full of what academics call hinge points. These are singular events that changed everything that came after." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qC0Ee4-dpnI

**Simple Minds – Taken from a David Bowie Lyric; Deliberately Avoided Starting with "The"** : Formed from the ashes of Johnny and the Self-Abusers. Singer Jim Kerr and guitarist Charlie Burchill consulted Bowie lyrics specifically to avoid having a name that started with "The." They found the line "so simple-minded he can drive his module" in a Bowie song and adopted Simple Minds. "They didn't want to be another group whose name began with the." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Singing-Specific Neurons** : Within the auditory cortex, there exists a unique group of neurons that activate and align themselves exclusively when the brain perceives singing. These specialized neurons do not respond to spoken words or purely instrumental music, and their specific function and reason for this selectivity remain unknown to scientists. "the auditory cortex contains a group of neurons that line up only when we hear singing. That's all they do." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Single-Driven Album Releases (Mid-Late 1950s)** : During the mid to late 1950s, even with the existence of notable rock and roll albums, the single reigned supreme; albums were typically released only after an artist had achieved success with a series of singles, which were then compiled with additional tracks, reflecting how consumers purchased individual radio hits. "The single ruled. Kids went out and bought the individual songs that they heard on the radio." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Siouxsie and the Banshees – Siouxsie Sioux's Indigenous Fascination; 1970 Vincent Price Film** : Siouxsie Sioux was fascinated by indigenous North American cultures, which explains "Siouxsie." "Banshees" came from the 1970 Vincent Price film Cry of the Banshee. Banshees in Irish lore are female spirits whose wailing foretells a death. "Banshees, by the way, are a female spirit from Irish lore whose will foretells that someone is going to die." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Skateboarding's Mainstream Takeover (New Millennium)** : By the new millennium, skateboarding culture achieved unprecedented mainstream interest, leading to millions of sales for Tony Hawk's video games (featuring skate punk music) and a statistic showing more Americans were into skateboarding than baseball in 2001. **Skepticism About Vinyl Revival's Longevity** : Industry insiders express skepticism about the long-term sustainability of the vinyl resurrection due to several factors: record labels increasing prices to "ridiculous prices," supply chain issues (like a 2020 fire at a lacquer master plant that produced 80% of the world's supply), and the impact of COVID-19 on record store closures. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Skinny Bobby Harper, Inspiration for WKRP's Johnny Fever** : The character of Johnny Fever, the eccentric DJ from the classic TV show "WKRP in Cincinnati," was based on a real-life Canadian-born DJ named Skinny Bobby Harper. Harper, who moved from Saskatchewan to the US, worked at Atlanta radio station WXQI in the mid-1960s, where his unconventional behavior often led to trouble. Bill Dyle, a future writer for "WKRP," worked alongside Harper at WXQI and subsequently used him as the template for the Johnny Fever character. "Bill Dyle, a writer who would later end up writing for WKRP, worked at the same station, and he used Canadian Skinny Bobby Harper as the template for Johnny Fever." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-N6IM5Nm5iw
**Slam Dancing** : Slam dancing originated during the hardcore punk movement as an aggressive form of dancing, where participants deliberately crashed into or "slammed" into each other. It emerged as a response to the disco era and a desire for aggressive expression, particularly for those looking to distance themselves from "hippie" culture. The most frequent location for slam dancing was directly in front of the stage. "deliberately crashing or slamming into other dancers, hence the term slam dancing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KMx4bmq8o2Y

**Sloan – Named After a French-Speaking Boss's Mispronunciation of "Slow One"** : The band's friend Jason had a French-speaking boss who thought Jason wasn't very bright and called him "a slow one." With the French accent, it came out as "Sloan," which became Jason's nickname. The band asked to use the name, and Jason agreed on condition that he be on the cover of their first release. He is indeed on the cover of the Peppermint EP. "So if you have a copy of Sloan's peppermint EP, that's a picture of Jason on the front." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Slow Dial-up Downloads (1990s)** : In the mid-1990s, the online world was characterized by slow dial-up modems, with a 7-megabyte song like Bowie's "Telling Lies" taking approximately 50 minutes to download even with a fast connection, making it a "mind blowing thing" to interact with artists online. "If you had a fast dial-up, you could expect to have this song in your computer in about 50 minutes." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM
**Small New York City Club and Punk Rock** : By 1973, a sense of dissatisfaction with mainstream music and the failure of 1960s ideals was growing. This led to a belief that "somebody had to do something," and "it was time to get real." Things began to escalate at a "small club in one of the scusiest parts of New York city," which is identified as the place where the concept of punk rock truly began to take shape. "And things began to get very real at a small club in one of the scusiest parts of New York city." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0xd0Hf5REg4
**Smallest Vinyl Record (Nano Made)** : Researchers from the Nano Made section at the Technical University of Denmark created the world's smallest "vinyl" record, measuring an astonishing 15 micrometers across. Although not made of traditional polyvinyl chloride, it functions like a full-size record, playing 25 seconds of Brenda Lee's "Rockin' Around the Christmas Tree" in stereo. "The hook here is that this record is just 15 micrometers across. You can't even see it." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B2g4QSREzpw
**Smart Speaker Poop Songs – Dedicated Genre for Kids Asking Alexa for Poop Songs** : A cottage industry exists of artists writing songs about excrement specifically for smart speakers, knowing that young children ask Alexa or Google to play poop songs. These songs include titles like "Puppy Diaper Song," "Puppy Stupid Butt," and "Never Going to Flush Again," and the writers make decent income from the streams. "Yes, they're making good coin doing this." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZbHRIh3RUoo
**Snowboarding Videos as Music Platform** : Songs from skate punk bands, such as The Offspring, started to appear in snowboarding videos, which served as an early platform for broader exposure before their mainstream breakthrough. "Plus some of these songs started showing up in snowboarding videos." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=44dXy0StjIQ
**Social Media's Increasing Role in Music** : Social media platforms like Facebook, YouTube, and Twitter are destined to play an even larger role in music, influencing its creation, spread, and consumption. This evolving landscape suggests significant opportunities for new, successful ideas and wealth creation. "social media, Facebook, YouTube, Twitter and whatever comes next will play a bigger and bigger part in music. It's creation, it's spread and it's consumption." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Social Media's Role in Music Discovery and Sharing** : Social media platforms significantly altered how people discover, consume, and share music. Fans could easily search bands on Google, read blog reviews, check MySpace pages, watch YouTube videos, and share findings with friends via Facebook or Twitter, often accessing free downloads directly from artists. "social media is changing the way we find out about music, consume it and share it with others." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Social Media's Transformative Impact on Music** : Social media, beginning with MySpace and later significantly impacted by YouTube, has fundamentally reshaped the music industry through platforms like X, Threads, Blue Sky, TikTok, Instagram Reels, and YouTube Shorts. These platforms facilitate songs going viral rapidly, with algorithms pushing trending sounds globally, enabling artists to build fan bases directly without traditional labels or marketing. This includes diverse content like dance trends, memes, collaborations, and live streaming via Instagram Live, TikTok Live, and Twitch, fostering unprecedented fan engagement and community. However, it has also led to a "snippet culture" emphasizing short songs and hooks, pressure on artists for constant viral content leading to burnout, intense competition, and a "flattening of music" where trends are chased, resulting in similar-sounding material. Social media has also augmented or replaced traditional A&R talent scouting. "Social media and music really began to come together with the debut of MySpace." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nX8uAFDzDYM
**Socrates' View on Youth and Society (c. 400 BCE)** : Around 400 BCE, Socrates, anticipating later generations' criticisms of youth, expressed concerns about the behavior of children. He noted their love of luxury, bad manners, contempt for authority, disrespect for elders, and preference for chatter over exercise, labeling them as "tyrants" who contradict parents and tyrannize teachers. This quote reflects a timeless complaint of older generations about younger ones, albeit not directly about music. "The children now love luxury. They have bad manners, contempt for authority. They show disrespect for elders and love chatter and place of exercise. Children are now tyrants, not the servants of their households. They no longer rise when elders enter the room. They contradict their parents chatter before company, gobble up dainty at the table, cross their legs and tyrannize their teachers." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Song Catalog Acquisition Companies** : Approximately a dozen companies, including Hypnosis, Primary Wave, Round Hill, and Iconic Artists, are actively involved in the business of buying song catalogs. Their strategy involves acquiring publishing rights with the belief that these songs will generate consistent royalties for decades. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Song Catalog Acquisition Strategy** : Companies acquire song catalogs by purchasing the publishing rights, operating under the belief that by carefully managing these assets over time—potentially decades—the songs will consistently generate royalties and provide a steady rate of return. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Song Catalog Valuation Method** : The price for a song catalog is determined by first calculating the annual royalties an artist's catalog generates. This annual figure is then multiplied by a negotiated factor (e.g., 10X or 15X) to arrive at the final lump-sum payout, potentially reaching $100 million to $150 million for a catalog earning $10 million annually. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk
**Song-Centric Consumption in Streaming Era** : In the streaming era, many music fans prioritize individual songs over artists, often being unable to name the artist behind a viral track on platforms like Spotify, Instagram, or TikTok, leading to fleeting relationships where interest ends with the song. "People love the song, not you, as the artist. And once they're done with the song, they're done with you." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Songs Are Deconstructed and Stored in Multiple Brain Locations** : When music enters the brain, the auditory cortex processes the entire signal as one piece. It is then passed to the mid-superior temporal sulcus, which splits the song into music and lyrics. Music is routed to the anterior superior sulcus; lyrics are routed to the brain's speech centers, where word recognition, meaning, and context must all be processed. This creates two separate databases — music and lyrics — in two different brain regions. This explains why most people pay more attention to a song's music than its words, and why singing through a song is often the only way to remember its lyrics. "Processing the lyrics takes more time, and depending on the song, we just might not be up to it." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NMwMwqMQpf4
**Songwriter's Hall of Fame** : David Bowie is honored as an inductee into the Songwriter's Hall of Fame, recognizing his prolific and influential songwriting career. "He's in the songwriter's Hall of Fame." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM
**Songwriting Adaptation to Streaming Algorithms** : Due to listeners skipping songs within the first 30 seconds and the payment threshold, producers and songwriters now "throw everything they can" into the first 30 seconds of a song. This includes shorter intros, putting choruses upfront, and adding many "sugar high hooks" to grab attention and prevent skips, ensuring payment. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Sonic Soak Ultrasonic Cleaning Device** : The Sonic Soak is a portable device designed to clean clothes using sound waves. It eliminates the need for water and detergent by hitting dirty clothes with sound waves, making it an environmentally friendly cleaning solution. "The sonic soak is a portable device that hits dirty clothes with sound waves and cleans them right up. No water and detergent needed, so very environmentally friendly." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GO0K_N7Ys7I
**Sony Soundabout Introduction (1979)** : In 1979, Sony, led by founders Masura Ibuka and Akio Morita, introduced a "very personal stereo" called the Sony Soundabout. Despite facing initial marketing skepticism and being considered too large, complicated, and expensive at first, its introduction is regarded as "the big bang of the portable personal stereo revolution." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z9T9wi0vEvc
**Sony Walkman Renaming and Improvements (1981)** : The Sony Soundabout was renamed The Walkman in 1981 after engineers refined its design. The improved Walkman featured 50% fewer parts, was more affordable, and quickly became a massive commercial success. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z9T9wi0vEvc
**Sony Walkman's Impact** : The Sony Walkman significantly influenced music consumption by transforming listeners into "headphone-wearing zombies" within their individual musical bubbles. This marked an early shift towards personalized and isolated listening experiences. "Who would have guessed that the Sony Walkman would turn us all into headphone-waring zombies inside our individual bubbles of music?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-CT7yYXonIk
**Sound Symbolism and Lyrics** : Humans possess the capacity to appreciate and enjoy sounds, including singing, without necessarily needing to understand the literal meaning of the lyrics. The brain is primarily evolved to respond to sound first, treating lyrics as enjoyable sounds rather than words. This explains why people can appreciate songs in foreign languages or derive pleasure from music without concentrating on lyrics in their native tongue. "Basically, you could appreciate and enjoy sounds, like singing, without really needing to understand what's being sung. We're just enjoying the lyrics as sounds, not as words." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**SoundScan's Impact on Genre Perception** : The inaugural SoundScan report revealed that certain genres and artists had been historically over-counted, while others, notably country music and "left of center rock music," were "greatly underestimated." This demonstrated that these previously overlooked genres were "selling way better than anyone knew." "When the first report arrived, it was obvious that certain genres and certain artists were being over-counted while others were being greatly underestimated. And everyone's surprise, country music was selling way better than anyone knew." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pE7TaWSUa-o
**Soundcloud Music Upload Rate** : Soundcloud, a popular audio distribution platform, experiences a rapid influx of content. Approximately twelve hours of music are uploaded to the site every single minute, demonstrating its high usage. "Soundcloud is super popular. Twelve hours of music are uploaded to the site every minute." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GO0K_N7Ys7I
**Soundgarden – Named After a Sculpture at NOAA in Seattle** : There is a sculpture by artist Doug Hollis on the grounds of the National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration in Seattle; when the wind blows, it makes "cool sinister noises." The sculpture is called Soundgarden. "In the wind blows, the sculpture makes some cool sinister noises." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**South American Human Rights Atrocities** : The transcript highlights severe human rights abuses in South America, specifically referencing the forced disappearances of children by military governments in Argentina and Chile between 1976 and 1983. This was exemplified by groups like the Madre's Deplaced de Mayo. U2's songs, particularly "Mothers of the Disappeared," "Bullet the Blue Sky," and "One Tree Hill," were written to address these atrocities, including the Pinochet dictatorship in Chile, political instability in Nicaragua and El Salvador, and American involvement in these regimes. "This was a group of women whose children had been forcibly disappeared by the military governments in both that country and Chile between 1976 and 1983. This was nothing short of a human rights atrocity." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VR5Fncdc2kQ
**South Korea Gyms Ban Fast Music (COVID-19)** : In South Korea, gyms banned music faster than 120 beats per minute due to alarms over a COVID-19 outbreak. The rationale was that fast music encouraged heavy workouts, leading to heavy breathing and sweat splashing, both of which could contribute to the spread of the virus. "The thinking was fast music encouraged heavy workouts, which meant a lot of heavy breathing which could spread COVID." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-N6IM5Nm5iw
**Soviet Guards Used Tango Music to Torture German Soldiers in World War II** : During the Second World War, Soviet guards used tango music as a method of psychological torture against German prisoners of war, who for some reason found the music deeply sinister. "Soviet guards used tango music to torture German soldiers during World War II, who found it 'sinister.'" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qtdetc5-MQo
**Soviet Union – Bootlegs on X-Ray Film (Roentgenizdat) and Tape (Magnitizdat)** : In the Soviet Union, unauthorized recordings of Western music — including The Beatles and The Rolling Stones — were essential to citizens who had no legal access to it. Records were pressed onto used X-ray film (a practice known as *Roentgenizdat*) and tape recordings circulated under the name *Magnitizdat*. "Bootlegs on X-ray films and tapes were fundamental for citizens to access censored Western music, such as The Beatles or The Rolling Stones." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Uly2cT2vc28
**Soviet X-Ray Records ("Ribs")** : During the period when Western records were prohibited in the Soviet Union, resourceful music enthusiasts created black market recordings known as "ribs" (reo bra in Russian). These were made by repurposing old medical X-rays retrieved from hospital dumpsters, onto which music was cut at 78 RPM using adapted gramophones. A cigarette was used to burn the center hole. Despite very poor sound quality, these cost around one ruble and provided illicit access to artists like The Beatles, The Rolling Stones, Elvis, and The Beach Boys. Possession of these records could lead to imprisonment in a gulag, and they are now sought-after collectibles. "These black market recordings were known as ribs, reo bra in Russian, because you could still see the bones of someone in the film." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=B2g4QSREzpw
**Speaker's Musical Evolution** : The speaker's musical journey began in a small town outside Winnipeg, where he was an "album rockhead" and metal drummer until 1983. Working at KX96 in Brandon, Manitoba, exposed him to an eclectic mix including Aztec Camera, The Jam, and The Clash. Moving to CFNY introduced him to alternative music (The Smiths, Depeche Mode, New Order), leading him to realize, "Where has this music been all my life? Why has this been hidden from me?" He converted from a "Mollethead rockhead to an alternative kid" and never looked back, feeling he was on "a mission from God" to teach the world about great music. "But after about a week of being able to go through the entire library, the thought was, where has this music been all my life? Why has this been hidden from me?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90
**Species of Spider Named After Bowie** : A species of spider has been named after David Bowie, a curious honor reflecting his unique and often otherworldly public image. "There's a species of spider after him. Of course there is." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM
**Speed of Song Recognition** : The human brain is extraordinarily fast at recognizing songs, capable of retrieving virtually all associated information from its musical database in the hippocampus. The typical time required to retrieve a musical memory is approximately 100 milliseconds, which is quicker than the blink of an eye and faster than a beam of light could travel around the Earth's equator. "Science says that the typical amount of time it takes us to retrieve a musical memory is about a hundred milliseconds. That's faster than the blink of an eye." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ
**Spin Magazine's "California Dreaming" (Summer 1992)** : In the summer of 1992, *Spin Magazine* published an influential article titled "California Dreaming." This piece focused on a number of melodic punk bands, including those signed to the Bay Area indie label Lookout Records such as Green Day, and contributed significantly to the wider recognition of the emerging pop punk scene. "That summer, Spid Magazine published an article called California Dreaming, that mentioned a bunch of these melodic punk bands." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tZV1lz-obQE
**SpongeBob Squarepants Musical Contribution** : In his final creative burst before his death, David Bowie wrote songs for a Broadway musical based on SpongeBob Squarepants, a choice that seemed "a very Bowie thing to do" given his eclectic nature. "There were songs for a Broadway musical based on SpongeBob Squarepants, which somehow seems like a very Bowie thing to do." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM
**Spotify Data on Taste Formation (New York Times Analysis)** : An analysis of Spotify data by The New York Times revealed specific age ranges for musical taste formation. For men, the most critical period is between 13 and 16, with their all-time favorite song typically released when they were 14. For women, the most impressionable years are 11 to 14, with their favorite song likely released when they were 13. This data suggests that childhood or preteen musical influences might be stronger for women. "The most important period for forming musical taste is between the ages of 13 and 16. On average, men were 14 when their all-time favorite song was released. It's a little different for women. Their most impressionable years for music are between 11 and 14. Their favorite song probably came out when they were 13." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Spotify's 30-Second Payout Threshold** : Spotify only pays artists for a stream if 30 seconds have passed. This critical threshold influences artists, composers, and producers to prioritize capturing and retaining listener attention within the first 30 seconds of a song at all costs. "Because Spotify does not pay out for a stream until 30 seconds have passed." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Spotify's Business Model – Podcasts as a Way to Reduce Royalty Obligations** : Spotify's strategy for achieving profitability involves growing its podcast business. If 15 to 25% of users spend their listening time on podcasts, that portion of usage generates no music royalty costs. This is why the company paid enormous sums for exclusive rights to programs like the Joe Rogan Experience. As of Q1 2021, Spotify reported an operating profit of 15 million euros. They also earn from sponsored recommendation campaigns, where artists and labels pay to have music promoted — which some compare to payola and others compare to record store promotional placement. "This explains why the company is willing to pay huge dollars for exclusive rights to programs like the Joe Rogan experience." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MQ7PDi-D9Ig
**Spotify's Hardcore Gardening Playlist – Plants Supposedly Grow Better to Hardcore Punk** : Spotify launched a playlist in 2024 called Hardcore Gardening, whose curators claim plants grow best when exposed to hardcore punk — better results than with classical or pop music. "Hardcore punk is better than playing your plants classical or pop music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fnZx8EGnszw
**Squeeze 5-Inch Record (1980) – Songs Mixed in Mono Due to Space Constraints** : In 1980, the band Squeeze issued a five-inch record spinning at 33⅓ RPM. Space was so tight that the songs had to be mixed in mono. This was one of many non-standard record sizes attempted over the decades. "Space was so tight, the songs had to be mixed in mono." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=I291j5WBc4k
**Stage Diving History** : Stage diving, where audience members jump from the stage into the crowd, has a long and disputed history. Iggy Pop with The Stooges and Jim Morrison of The Doors were doing it in 1969. There's also documented evidence from a Rolling Stones show in Germany in 1964. Dee Snider of Twisted Sister claims he invented it in the 70s out of aggression. "Iggy Pop was doing this with the Stooges as far back as 1969." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KMx4bmq8o2Y
**Stagnation in Rock and Hip Hop** : The question of whether current music is as "good" as older music is highly subjective and technical. It's argued that rock, being a relatively young genre, was once constantly evolving, allowing bands like The Beatles, Jimi Hendrix, Eddie Van Halen, Black Sabbath, and Led Zeppelin to be "first" in their innovations. However, rock is perceived to have experienced a "stagnation" as its sound hasn't revolutionized in a long time. Similarly, hip hop, despite being "game changing," has "hit something of a wall," creating its own generation gap. "And let's face it, there hasn't been a revolution in the sound of rock in forever." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=m7MbV-eCLyE
**Stand-up Comedy as a "Safe Bet" for Networks** : The format of building a sitcom around a stand-up comedian was highly appealing to networks. According to TV critic Greg David, comedians were considered a "safe bet" because they possessed proven performance "chops" and often came with a "built-in audience." Matt Williams, creator of *Roseanne* and *Home Improvement*, added that a fully realized stand-up routine offered a complete world and characters, solving the challenges of finding a concept, jokes, and a star simultaneously. "I mean, I think at the time sitcoms were perennially in the top 10 most popular shows, you know, you can make however many 25 to 30 of them a year if they're a success or a big business." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6O5TCTO-go4

**State of Canadian Music Industry Pre-1971** : Before January 18, 1971, the Canadian music industry was underdeveloped, largely consisting of remote offices of foreign record companies and tiny, uninfluential domestic labels. Canadian radio was dominated by UK and US artists, making it rare to hear Canadian music and leading to a lack of national musical identity. "Before January 18, 1971, there really wasn't much of a Canadian music industry." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA

**Steve Lillywhite (Producer) - Working Philosophy** : Steve Lillywhite, a renowned British producer who has worked with dozens of major artists, maintains a philosophy of never listening to his past projects. He intentionally avoids revisiting old work, stating that he doesn't "want to be distracted by the past." "Of all the albums he's worked on, has he ever gone back and wished he did something different? No, he never listens to past projects because he doesn't want to be distracted by the past." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hjProJd_JrM
**Steve Lillywhite (Producer) - Working Style** : Steve Lillywhite is characterized by his multifaceted and consistently cheerful approach in the studio. He acts as a "coach, a teacher, a lion tamer, a psychologist, a cheerleader, a sounding board," always enthusiastic, and never pushy, demonstrating a supportive yet directive presence. "He was a coach, a teacher, a lion tamer, a psychologist, a cheerleader, a sounding board, and he was always, always cheerful, never pushy and always super enthusiastic." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hjProJd_JrM
**Stomach Problems Theory** : Similar to Michael Hutchence's alleged brain tumor theory, Kurt Cobain reportedly suffered from stomach problems, which some suggested may have contributed to his state. "just like Kurt Cobain and his stomach problems, at least one friend maintained that Michael said he, quote, would do a curt before the cancer got to him." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=23OgreyK66o
**Stone Temple Pilots – Reverse-Engineered from an STP Oil Treatment Sticker** : Originally called Mighty Joe Young, the band had to change names due to a blues musician using the same name. In their backyard was an STP oil treatment sticker on a shrine-like structure. They tried to make the initials stand for something: after considering "Stinky Toilet Paper" and obscene options, they landed on Stone Temple Pilots. STP is also slang for the hallucinogen 2,5-dimethoxy-4-methylamphetamine. "They went through a bunch of possibilities, including stinky toilet paper." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE
**Storm Thorgerson – Legendary Album Art Designer** : Storm Thorgerson is widely celebrated as one of the most famous and influential album art creators of all time. Alongside his partner Aubrey Powell, he was responsible for designing iconic covers for Pink Floyd (including "The Dark Side of the Moon," "Wish You Were Here," "Animals"), Led Zeppelin (logo, "Presence," "In Through the Out Door"), Black Sabbath, AC/DC, The Police, Genesis, Peter Gabriel, ELO, Paul McCartney, and Wings. "The cover was designed by Storm Thorgerson, probably the most famous album art creator of all time." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_tbKuJR0cPs
**Strategic Use of Data Analytics by Artists** : Artists are advised to utilize available streaming data analytics to inform career decisions such as tour planning (where and when), merchandise sales management, and optimal new music release timing, mirroring strategies employed by major stars to enhance their success. "You need to get into data analytics. That's what all the big stars are doing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Stream Ripping and Fake Artists – New Forms of Music Piracy in the Streaming Era** : The streaming era has generated new forms of piracy: "stream ripping" (saving streamed songs to a local file), "fake artists" (uploading another artist's music under a false identity, as in the case of "LaTesha Escalero" uploading Van Morrison recordings), and fake streams (purchasing plays to inflate numbers, divert royalties, and manipulate algorithms). "New forms of piracy include 'stream ripping,' 'fake artists' (uploading others' music under a false identity), and fake streams." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Uly2cT2vc28
**Streaming History – Rhapsody Launched December 3, 2001; Now Trades as Napster** : The modern all-you-can-hear streaming subscription model traces back to Rhapsody, which first went online on December 3, 2001. Over the following year, Universal, EMI, BMG, Warner, and Sony all joined. Rhapsody still exists but rebranded as Napster after purchasing that trademark in 2011, making it the legitimate successor to the original file-sharing service. "This is the legitimate form of Napster." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MQ7PDi-D9Ig
**Streaming Library Size – 90 Million Songs, 60,000 New Tracks Uploaded Daily** : As of early 2021, the available streaming universe contained approximately 90 million songs, all of which are accessible on any major platform. Spotify reported that 60,000 new tracks were being uploaded every single day — 2.2 million per year. Between 20 and 25% of all Spotify songs have never been streamed even once, meaning 30 to 35 million songs have been heard by no one. A site called Forgotify lets users stream only songs with zero plays using a Spotify login. "There's even an app for that." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MQ7PDi-D9Ig
**Streaming Payouts – Platform by Platform Comparison** : Streaming payout rates vary significantly between services. For 100 listens, Spotify pays approximately 40 US cents; Apple Music and Amazon Music each pay about 50 cents; Deezer (France) pays 47 cents; YouTube pays only 18 cents; SoundCloud pays 13 cents; and Tidal may pay as much as $1.20. These figures are estimates because the system is opaque even for artists. A single Spotify stream pays roughly 6 tenths of a cent on the subscription tier, but the freemium (ad-supported) tier pays less — hence the blended average of approximately 40 cents per 100 streams. "The whole system is very, very opaque, even for the artist." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MQ7PDi-D9Ig
**Streaming Platforms – Approximately Three Dozen Active Services Worldwide** : Most streaming conversations focus on Spotify, Apple Music, Amazon Music, Tidal, YouTube Music, and Deezer, but there are approximately three dozen active services globally at any given time. These include Anghami (Abu Dhabi, the Arab world's first streaming platform), Gaana and JioSaavn (India's two largest), Patari (Lahore, Pakistan), KKBox (Taiwan), and several large Chinese services including QQ Music. Defunct services include Songs, Mog, Xbox Music, and Slacker Radio. "There are about, and it changes from day to day, three dozen active companies operating around the world." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MQ7PDi-D9Ig
**Streaming Pricing – Same Service, Wildly Different Prices by Country** : Spotify is available in approximately 170 countries and charges different rates adjusted for local currencies and economic conditions. In Canada, the price is $9.99 CAD; in the US, $9.99 USD (about $12 CAD); in Egypt, roughly $4 CAD; in Vietnam, $3 CAD; and in India, $1.97 CAD. These represent different tiers of Spotify Premium, which grants full functionality and no commercials. "If you're in Japan, you're paying $980 per month." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MQ7PDi-D9Ig
**Streaming Revenue Flow – Labels Take Their Share Before Artists See a Cent** : Before any payout reaches an artist, it passes through the record label, which deducts its share first. At the high end, Spotify might pay out $4 for 100 streams, but the label absorbs approximately $3.60 before the artist sees anything. Whatever the artist does receive is almost always less than the 10% they received from physical CD sales. The 10% figure on CDs assumed a $10 wholesale price, so $1 per album; streaming makes even that look generous. "Think about that the next time you don't pay for a streaming music service and go with a freemium tier." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MQ7PDi-D9Ig
**Streaming Services and CanCon – Unregulated Platforms Drain Canadian Revenue** : Streaming platforms — all foreign-owned — operate in Canada without CanCon obligations. Unlike Canadian radio stations, they are not required to invest in Canadian culture or contribute to funds like FACTOR. Critics argue this drains revenue from the country while providing nothing back to the domestic music ecosystem. Canada, France, Australia, New Zealand, Mexico, South Africa, Nigeria, Jamaica, Venezuela, Israel, and the Philippines all have domestic music quotas for radio for this reason. "Streaming services put nothing back into the system." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-JWO_jYXwEM
**Streaming Skip Statistics** : Data indicates that 24% of streaming listeners skip unfamiliar songs within the first five seconds, 29% within ten seconds, and by the crucial 30-second mark, 35% of listeners have already moved on. "Twenty-four percent of streaming listeners will skip an unfamiliar song in the first five seconds." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Streaming Surpassing Physical Sales (2016)** : In 2016, streaming officially became the leading revenue generator for the American recorded music business, surpassing all other forms of music distribution combined for the first time. This marked a watershed moment following years of disruption from illegal file sharing and the rise of iTunes, as streaming offered a convenient, low-cost, and legal way to consume music. By 2023, streaming accounted for 67% of the industry's total revenue, signaling an irreversible shift away from physical products, though vinyl has seen a comeback with "nice fat margins." "In 2016, there was a tipping point. For the first time, streaming generated more money for the American recorded music business than all other forms of music distribution put together." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZzIqIydZTlA
**Streaming and the 30-Second Payout Rule** : As streaming gained popularity in the 2000s, rampant skipping necessitated a universal rule: artists are only paid for a song play if it runs for a minimum of 30 seconds. "No one gets paid for a play on a streaming music platform unless the song runs for at least 30 seconds." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Streaming and the Environment – Streaming 27 Times Uses More Energy Than Manufacturing a CD** : A 2017 Norwegian study found that, despite involving only digital zeros and ones, streaming music is actually worse for the environment than manufacturing physical media. Downloading one gigabyte of music data uses roughly the energy required to run a light bulb for an hour. Data centers consume approximately 2% of the world's energy to run and to keep cool. Streaming an album 27 times uses more energy than manufacturing a single CD or vinyl record. The amount of greenhouse gases generated by music streaming reaches up to 350 million kilograms per year. "Streaming an album over the internet just 27 times will use more energy than it takes to produce and manufacture a single CD or vinyl record." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MQ7PDi-D9Ig
**Streaming as Cheaper and More Convenient Consumption** : Streaming music services revolutionized music consumption by offering a cheaper alternative to buying downloads and a far more convenient method than purchasing physical media. By the mid-2010s, it became evident that streaming represented the future of music consumption. "Streaming was cheaper than buying downloads and far more convenient than traveling through time and space to buy your music on a piece of plastic." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5Y6nHw5xx88
**Streaming as Primary Revenue for Labels** : Streaming music services have become the largest source of revenue for record labels, accounting for over half of their earnings. Physical products like CDs contribute progressively less each quarter. "Streaming is now the greatest source of revenue for record labels. Over half the money they make comes from streaming, with physical product like CDs offering up less and less and less every quarter." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Streaming's Erosion of Album Concept (Present)** : Streaming services have further diminished the album's relevance, as the internet generation prioritizes individual songs and playlists over cohesive album experiences, leading to deep album cuts being lost among millions of tracks and effectively returning music consumption to a 1964-era single-focused model. "Streaming has continued the assault on the concept of the album. The internet generation as a whole doesn't care about albums." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Streaming's Focus on Singles Over Albums** : In the streaming world, the emphasis is heavily on individual songs, specifically singles, with album tracks receiving much less attention. This shift raises questions about the future relevance and purpose of recording full albums when consumption patterns are so fragmented. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Streaming's Impact on Albums and Playlists** : Streaming services further diminished the album concept, with people primarily streaming playlists rather than full albums, and album tracks receiving almost no traction in the streaming world. "Then came streaming. Instead of albums, people are streaming playlists. Album tracks get almost zero traction in the streaming world." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Streaming's Impact on Attention Spans and Song Structure** : Streaming, with its vast supply of music, contributes to shrinking attention spans. Listeners are quick to skip songs they dislike (25% in 5 seconds, 35% before 30 seconds), fundamentally changing the nature of music as artists focus on retaining attention within the crucial 30-second Spotify payout window. "It is changing the very nature of music. And it has to do with our ever shrinking attention spans." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**Streaming's Impact on Music Consumption and Value** : Streaming has liberated recorded music from physical limitations, making the entire history of music accessible as pure data. However, this has changed user behavior; without the financial investment of buying physical music, listeners are less inclined to fully engage with an album, often skipping songs quickly and valuing music differently. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eqTFinLk3oU
**Streaming's Impact on the Album Concept** : Streaming music is observed to be gradually eroding the traditional concept of the album as a cohesive artistic work. "Another thing that's happening with streaming is that we're slowly killing the concept of the album." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Sc9HApnyBLM
**Street in Paris Named After Bowie** : A street in Paris has been named after David Bowie, an international recognition of his global cultural impact and legacy. "there's a street in Paris named after him." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM
**Stylus Force during Playback** : As a record plays, the stylus vibrates a thousand times per second, subjecting it to a force of 90 Gs. This force is comparable to an airplane accelerating to Mach 2.6 in one second. "This subjects the stylus to a force of 90 Gs." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=72Lei7uug8c
**Sub-Culture Lifespans** : Some rock-related subcultures, like New Wave and Grunge, have a lifespan corresponding to a particular musical trend, withering and dying once the trend concludes. "Some of these sub-cultures come and go." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=evlGhfUe6QQ
**Sublime's Slightly Stoopid Connection – Bradley Nowell Signed Them While They Were in High School** : Slightly Stoopid is a very rock/reggae/ska/punk band from San Diego. Bradley Nowell of Sublime liked them so much he signed them to his label while they were still in high school. In a stunt, they pressed a record not on vinyl but on hash resin — it took $6,000 worth of bubble hash, $1,000 to press, and the record sounded terrible. The failed hash record was simply crushed up and smoked. "Because once it didn't work, you just crush it up and smoke it." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**Success and Impact of Cancon** : After about a decade, the Canadian content rules proved highly successful. They stimulated a strong domestic music scene and robust music exports, enabling Canada to produce and export more music globally than a country of its size would typically achieve. "But now, the Canadian system cranks out more music to the rest of the world than a country of our size should otherwise. We have a very strong domestic scene and strong music exports. The Cancon rules have been a great success." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_YjwRApoJhA
**Sum 41 – Three Competing Stories; Random Number Most Likely** : Three theories: (1) band formed 41 days into summer 1996 (which would be September 28th, past summer's end — problematic); (2) a penny, nickel, dime, and quarter sum to 41 cents; (3) on a computer keyboard, Shift+4 gives a dollar sign and 1 gives an exclamation mark, together expressing a wish to get rich. No definitive answer. "Take your pick." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NCQ1ERgSfeE

**Summary of Music's Evolutionary Roles** : Music evolved to hold a special place in the human brain due to its multiple crucial roles in survival and cultural development: facilitating mating, serving as a survival mechanism for protecting infants via lullabies, uniting tribes, and preserving cultural stories and history before the advent of written language. "Music therefore evolved in a special place in our brains because we needed to mate. We needed to keep our babies from turning us all into food. We needed to bring the tribe together and we needed to preserve our stories and thus our culture." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI

"The summer of 2005 was an embarrassment of riches. Rock, and remember this is music based on alt-rock heritage, ruled." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MK7L0eCpDHc

**Super Secret iPod for US Department of Defense** : The US Department of Defense once requested Apple to develop a unique iPod unit equipped with special, undetectable hardware. **Supermassive Black Hole's B Flat Emission** : A supermassive black hole located in the Perseus cluster, approximately 250 million light-years away, emits a profound acoustic wave. This wave is identified as a B flat, positioned an astonishing 57 octaves below middle C, representing an incredibly deep bass sound. "There is a singing black hole, a supermassive black hole in the Perseus cluster, which is a group of galaxies about 250 million light years away. It emits a super deep acoustic wave. And just so you know, it's a B flat, 57 octaves below middle sea." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GO0K_N7Ys7I
**Supernova Explosion ~41,000 Years Ago – Possible Cosmic Origin of Music** : A theory proposes that a supernova explosion approximately 41,000 years ago may have caused genetic mutations in *Homo sapiens*, resulting in enlarged brains capable of complex thought, language, visual art (as in cave paintings), and ultimately music. The oldest known musical instruments date to approximately 30,000 years ago, consistent with this timeline. "A supernova explosion about 41,000 years ago may have caused mutations in Homo sapiens leading to larger brains and, ultimately, music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=f2KA97T4u08
**Surprise Album Release Trend (2010s)** : David Bowie's 2013 album, *The Next Day*, which was released without prior announcement, was the first in a series of "surprise albums" by superstar acts in the 2010s, predating Beyoncé's well-known use of the strategy. "It was the first of a series of surprise albums recorded and released by superstar acts in the 2010s." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM
**Synergy Between College Bands and Radio** : A perfect synergy existed between college bands and college radio: many indie bands were formed by college students, played their first gigs on or around campus, and toured by playing other colleges, making college radio their natural supporter. This created a well-organized musical subculture. "The synergy was perfect, indie bands were often formed by college students. The first gigs were usually in and around the campus and when they went on the road, they most likely played in and around other colleges. So it was only natural for these college bands to be supported by college radio." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sCtQqVBtCaI
**Synesthesia – Music Experienced as Colors; Affects Kanye West, Stevie Wonder, Tori Amos, Eddie Van Halen, and Others** : Synesthesia is a neurological condition where the senses overlap. Musical synesthesia — where notes, chords, and combinations of sounds are perceived as specific colors — has been reported by Kanye West, Stevie Wonder (who is also totally blind), Tori Amos, Billy Joel, Patrick Stump of Fall Out Boy, Eddie Van Halen, and Pharrell Williams. Growing up with synesthesia, these artists generally assumed everyone experienced music this way. Singer Sam Endicott of The Bravery, who also writes songs for Shakira and Christina Aguilera, has credited synesthesia with giving him an unusual range. "They all say that they have music or sound to color synesthesia." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NMwMwqMQpf4
**Synesthesia – Overlapping Senses with Music** : Synesthesia is a neurological quirk where senses overlap, leading to interesting perceptions. One type involves seeing music, where notes or timbers appear to have colors (e.g., a middle C might be red, a piano might sound green, or a song might have a golden halo). This experience is consistent for individuals, usually present from birth, and they find it difficult to describe to non-synesthetes due to its inherent nature. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BHN6db7m3DM
**Synthesizers in Early 1980s** : Around 1980, synthesizers became widespread because the gear became sufficiently cheap, portable, and powerful for everyday musicians. This accessibility fostered a "punk" approach to the technology, as many users lacked formal musical training but enjoyed experimenting to create cool, unprecedented sounds. "it took until the beginning of the 80s for the gear to become cheap enough, portable enough, and powerful enough to be taken up by everyday musicians." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9CNNsqXiL6U
**System of a Down – Changed from "Victims of a Down" to "System" for Shelf Proximity to Slayer** : Originally called Soil, then "Victims of a Down" — referencing the Armenian genocide, drawn from a poem by guitarist Daron Malakian. Against this backdrop, the idea of centering a show around a "salt of the Earth" family of factory workers from the Midwest, like *Roseanne*, was considered a "pretty radical idea." **Tag Team Mixing Technique** : A collaborative mixing method was described where two individuals take 15-minute turns at the mixing board, with the key rule that "nothing sacred" from the previous person's work is off-limits for alteration. This rapid-fire process results in four different mixes within an hour and is likened to "speed chess." "You get 15 minutes to mix. You finish a mix. You leave the room. The other guy comes in, and the only rule is nothing sacred." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VR5Fncdc2kQ
**Tangential Excision Medical Procedure** : Travis Barker underwent tangential excision as part of his recovery from severe burns. This surgical procedure involves a surgeon scraping away dead, burned skin until viable, bleeding tissue is reached. While necessary for healing, it carries risks of significant blood loss and infection. "He ended up in something called tangential excision. This is where a surgeon scrapes away dead, burned skin until it starts to bleed." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q-QP7ePxkQE

**Tax Benefits of Catalog Sales (US)** : In the United States, selling a song catalog offers significant tax advantages. Regular royalty income is taxed at high personal income rates (40-50%), but taking a large lump sum from a catalog sale is treated as capital gains, which may be taxed at a much lower rate (around 20%). ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sfie4YYncxk

**Temporal Lobe and Music Recognition** : The temporal lobe, situated centrally in the brain, has two hemispheres: the left hemisphere is responsible for interpreting speech, while the right hemisphere is crucial for recognizing the structures and patterns inherent in music. This right-side region is interconnected with the auditory cortex. "The temporal lobe, a hunk of brain right in the middle, has two hemispheres. One, the one on the left, interprets speech. The one on the right helps us recognize the structures and patterns of music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mTbagQE7akQ

**The 13-Year Rock-Pop Cycle Theory** : Since 1951, rock and pop music have been "locked in a battle" where their popularity and creativity are 180 degrees out of phase, with each cycle lasting approximately 13 years. **The 13th Amendment's Indirect Role in Rock and Roll** : The ratification of the 13th Amendment, which outlawed slavery on December 16, 1865, set in motion a chain of events that profoundly influenced American music. It enabled the Great Migration of African Americans from the South to the North in the early 20th century, which in turn fostered the cultural conditions for the birth of genres like blues and jazz, ultimately leading to the rise of rock and roll in the 1950s. "All that, the rise of rock and roll, began with the great migration of the early 20th century, which was made possible by the ratification of the 13th Amendment, outlawing slavery on December 16th, 1865." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**The 1992 Grunge Era** : The year 1992 is identified as "the era of grunge," characterized by dominant bands such as Nirvana, Pearl Jam, Soundgarden, Alice in Chains, The Smashing Pumpkins, and Stone Temple Pilots. **The Amen Break (1969) – 6-Second Drum Sample from The Winstons That Became the Foundation of an Era** : The Amen Break is a six-second drum solo performed by GC Coleman on "Amen Brother," the B-side to a 1969 Grammy-winning single called "Color Him Father" by a funk soul group called The Winstons. When sampling became widespread in the 1980s and 1990s, this passage was discovered and became one of the most recycled drum breaks in history, appearing in thousands of songs across hip-hop, rave, techno, jungle, and drum and bass. Documented uses include Linkin Park's "Faint," N.W.A.'s "Straight Outta Compton," Public Enemy's "Fight the Power," Oasis's "D'You Know What I Mean," and The Prodigy's "Firestarter." Despite this ubiquity, neither GC Coleman the drummer nor Richard L. Spencer the composer has received a single cent in royalties from any of these uses. "Since then, the Amen Break has been sliced and diced and rearranged into a million different ways in a million different songs." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mmI2oN9zolQ
**The Bathhouse Recording Studio** : The Bathhouse is a local recording studio where Cassadour's first full album, *Brude and Bloom*, was recorded. "recording was done at a local recording studio called The Bathhouse." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MmXDbXI6Sqk

**The Can Rock Renaissance of the 1990s – Tragically Hip, Alanis Morissette, Nickelback, and Dozens More** : By the 1990s, after two decades of CanCon nurturing, Canadian music had come of age. **The Chromatic Scale and Musical Building Blocks** : The chromatic scale is the standard scale of pitches or notes used for centuries in Western music, consisting of 12 notes within an octave that then repeat. These notes are mathematically related through a set series of ratios, or semitone intervals, and form the basic DNA for all music, from Mozart's operas to punk songs. "For centuries, we've used a standard scale of pitches or notes, called the chromatic scale. 12 notes in an octave, then repeat." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=L09R2evjyMc

When they submitted a demo to a record label, it was returned addressed to "The Cranberries" (a typo). They decided it was a better name and kept it. "It was returned, addressed to the cranberries. So it was a typo." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ

This date refers to the tragic small plane crash in a cornfield outside Mason City, Iowa, that killed rock and roll pioneers Buddy Holly, Ritchie Valens, and Big Wopper. "February 3rd, 1957 has gone down in history as the day the music died." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=3eGBnwPWRGo
**The Day the Music Died (1959)** : The infamous event known as "The Day the Music Died" occurred in 1959, claiming the lives of Buddy Holly, The Big Bopper, and Ritchie Valens. Their chartered single-engine aircraft crashed in an Iowa cornfield, a tragedy that left a profound mark on music history. "There was the infamous The Day the Music died in 1959 that saw Buddy Holly, the big bopper and Richie Valens die when their chartered single engine aircraft went down in an Iowa cornfield." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dgzF_KBSQWM
**The Dead Milkmen – From a Tony Morrison Novel ("Song of Solomon")** : There is a character in Toni Morrison's novel Song of Solomon called "Milkman Dead." "There's a character in a Tony Morrison novel called Song of Solomon called Milkman Dead." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=QkYHaJKohVQ
**The Death of the Album Concept** : The traditional rock album, conceived as a coherent collection of carefully recorded and sequenced songs to be consumed as a whole (a concept that solidified in the mid-1960s with *Sgt. Pepper*), is undergoing a "long, slow death." "The concept of the rock album, this collection of songs carefully recorded and sequenced and meant to be consumed as a whole, really began to take form in the middles 60s." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z7glrAoXtkA
**The Decline of Western Civilization (Film)** : This film, made by Penelope Spheeris, documented the peculiar punk scenes in D.C. and Southern California. It captured footage of predominantly male audiences moshing to bands like the Circle Jerks and Black Flag, and its global distribution played a significant role in spreading moshing behavior to other parts of the world. "A filmmaker named Penelope Sphereis decided she needed to document this peculiar form of punk scene in DC and Southern California." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KMx4bmq8o2Y

**The Genesis of Songs** : Beyond the meaning of lyrics, the stories of how songs are created are often rich with context, serendipity, accidents, and crazy coincidences that contribute to a great song's birth. These behind-the-scenes narratives reveal the circumstances that brought a piece of music to life. "Something happened for that song to be born. What was it? And what were the circumstances, the serendipity, the accidents, the crazy coincidences that needed to manifest for a great song to come to life?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DAjcCk9xYWk
**The Good, the Bad and the Ugly (1966) – Movie** : The classic 1966 Spaghetti Western film "The Good, the Bad and the Ugly," starring Clint Eastwood, is shown playing on the television set in the background of Oasis's "Definitely Maybe" album cover. **The Great Metric Shift to 4/4 Time (c. 1910)** : Prior to 1900, the most popular time signature in Western music was 3/4 time, or waltz time, exemplified by songs like "The Star-Spangled Banner" or "Take Me Out to the Ball Game." However, around 1910, a significant change known as the "Great Metric Shift" occurred, moving Western music's preference from 3/4 to 4/4 time. Musicologists largely credit ragtime, with its highly rhythmic, syncopated, and choppy nature, as the primary catalyst for this fundamental shift in musical rhythm. "But then, about 120 years ago, western music underwent something that might be called the Great Metric Shift." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**The Great Migration and the Birth of Jazz and Blues (1910-1940)** : The Great Migration, occurring between 1910 and 1940, saw approximately 2 million African Americans move from the impoverished, racially discriminatory US South to the Midwest and Northeast, enabled by the expanding railroad system. This mass movement followed the abolition of slavery in 1865 by the 13th Amendment and years of living under Jim Crow laws. As they settled in cities like Memphis, St. Louis, Chicago, and Detroit, they brought their rich cultural traditions, including work songs, spirituals, gospel, and African musical influences, which collectively led to the birth of jazz and the blues. "And this led to the birth of two extremely important musical genres, jazz and the blues." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_Pi7JLwAeOI
**The Grey Ghost - Chrysler Tour Van** : In their early touring days, The Black Keys used a 1994 Chrysler van affectionately named "the Grey Ghost" to travel from gig to gig. "chugging from gig to gig in a 1994 Chrysler van that they called the Grey Ghost". ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PmwfC4HR3_I
**The Grunge Gold Rush** : Prompted by the accurate sales data from SoundScan, which highlighted the unexpected popularity of alternative rock, record labels "pivot[ed]" their strategies. This led to an aggressive pursuit of new alt-rock acts, initiating what became known as the "Grunge Gold Rush." "So this caused the record labels to pivot. If that's what was selling, well then let's go find more of it. And so began the Grunge Gold Rush." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pE7TaWSUa-o
